| width2 = 113
| alt2 = 
| caption2 = As Pope
| footer = The gold star represents the [[Virgin Mary]], the grape-like plantthe [[spikenard]]is associated with [[Saint Joseph]] and the [[Holy Name of Jesus|IHS]] is the symbol of the Jesuits&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news |title=Vatican releases Pope Francis' coat of arms, motto and ring |url= https://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/religion/the-pope/9937813/Vatican-releases-Pope-Francis-coat-of-arms-motto-and-ring.html|publisher= The Daily Telegraph |date=18 March 2013 |accessdate=18 March 2013 |location=London}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web |url=http://www.vatican.va/holy_father/francesco/elezione/stemma-papa-francesco_it.html |title=Lo Stemma di Papa Francesco |date= |work= |publisher=L'Osservatore Romano (Vatican website) |accessdate=18 March 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref name="NCR"/&gt;
}}
Elected at the age of 76, Francis was reported to be healthy and his doctors have said his missing lung tissue, removed in his youth, does not have a significant impact on his health.&lt;ref name="Pope Francis's missing lung should not be a problem, say doctors"/&gt; The only concern would be decreased respiratory reserve if he had a respiratory infection.&lt;ref name="Why Pope Francis Only Has One Lung"/&gt; In the past, one attack of [[sciatica]] in 2007 prevented him from attending a consistory and delayed his return to Argentina for several days.&lt;ref name="falasca" /&gt;

Francis is the first [[Jesuit]] pope. This was an unexpected appointment, because of the tense relations between the [[Society of Jesus]] and the Holy See.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.religionnews.com/2013/03/14/why-the-first-jesuit-pope-is-a-big-deal/|title=Why the first Jesuit pope is a big deal|date=14 March 2013|publisher=Religion News Service|author=Caleb K. Bell|accessdate=8 June 2015}}&lt;/ref&gt; He is also the first from the Americas,&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|url=http://world.time.com/2013/03/13/pope-of-the-americas/|title=Pope of the Americas|date=13 March 2013|publisher=TIME|author=Howard Chua-Eoan|accessdate=8 June 2015}}&lt;/ref&gt; and the first from the [[Southern Hemisphere]]. Many media reported him as being the first non-European pope, but he is actually the 11th; the previous was [[Pope Gregory III|Gregory III]] from Syria, who died in 741. However, although Francis does not have a European nationality, he has a European ethnicity.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/blogs/worldviews/wp/2013/03/13/sorry-jorge-mario-bergoglio-is-not-the-first-non-european-pope/|title=Sorry, Jorge Mario Bergoglio is not the first non-European pope|last=Fisher|first=Max|date=13 March 2013|publisher=The Washington Post|accessdate=8 June 2015}}&lt;/ref&gt;

As pope, his manner is less formal than that of his immediate predecessors: a style that news coverage has referred to as "no frills", noting that it is "his common touch and accessibility that is proving the greatest inspiration."&lt;ref name="nofrills"&gt;[http://www.cbsnews.com/8301-505263_162-57576725/pope-francis-brings-no-frills-style-to-papacy/ "Pope Francis brings no-frills style to papacy"], CBS News, 28 March 2013, Retrieved 28 March 2013&lt;/ref&gt; On the night of his election, he took a bus back to his hotel with the cardinals, rather than be driven in the papal car.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|url=https://www.reuters.com/article/2013/03/16/us-pope-poor-idUSBRE92F05P20130316|title=Pope Francis wants a 'poor Church for the poor'|date=16 March 2013|publisher=Reuters|accessdate=16 March 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt; The next day, he visited Cardinal [[Jorge Mara Meja]] in the hospital and chatted with patients and staff.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://abcnews.go.com/International/retired-argentine-cardinal-heart-attack/comments?type=story&amp;id=18736841|title=Pope visits ailing Argentine cardinal in hospital|date=|publisher=ABC News|archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20130316062247/http://abcnews.go.com/International/retired-argentine-cardinal-heart-attack/comments?type=story&amp;id=18736841|archivedate=16 March 2013|work=|accessdate=9 May 2014}}&lt;/ref&gt; At his first media audience, the Saturday after his election, the Pope said of Saint Francis of Assisi: "The man who gives us this spirit of peace, the poor man", and he added "[h]ow I would like a poor Church, and for the poor".&lt;ref name=PapalName/&gt;

In addition to his [[Native language|native]] Spanish, Francis is also conversant in Latin (the [[official language]] of the Holy See), he speaks fluent Italian (the official language of Vatican City and the "everyday language" of the Holy See), German,&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2013/mar/13/new-pope-thirteen-key-facts|title=Pope Francis: 13 key facts about the new pontiff|date=13 March 2013|work=The Guardian|location=London|accessdate=13 March 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt; French,&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|url=http://www.news.va/it/news/briefing-di-padre-lombardi|title=Briefing di padre Lombardi|date=14 March 2013|publisher=The Vatican Today|accessdate=14 March 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt; [[Portuguese language|Portuguese]],&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|url=http://www.corriere.it/cronache/13_marzo_14/papa-francesco-primo-giorno_9d687672-8c78-11e2-ab2c-711cc67f5f67.shtml|title=Francis and those humble gestures by the Pope, he does not sit on a throne, paying the bill at the hotel|date=14 March 2013|publisher=Corriere Della Sera|language=it|accessdate=1 April 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt; English,&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2013/mar/14/pope-francis-first-day|title=Pope Francis, first day after election|date=14 March 2013|publisher=The Guardian|location=London|author1=Peter Walker, Paul Owen|author2=David Batty|lastauthoramp=yes|accessdate=19 March 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref name="languages"&gt;Willey, David, [http://www.bbc.co.uk/news/world-europe-21986185 News analysis sidebar to "Pope Francis delivers Easter plea for peace"], BBC News, 31 March 2013, Retrieved 31 March 2013&lt;/ref&gt; and he understands the [[Piedmontese language]] and some [[Genoese dialect|Genoese]].&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|url=http://www.catholicnews.com/data/stories/cns/1301486.htm|archive-url=http://webarchive.loc.gov/all/20130402184851/http%3A//www.catholicnews.com/data/stories/cns/1301486.htm|dead-url=yes|archive-date=2 April 2013|title=Can't chant, can't speak English? Pope says it's because he's tone-deaf|last=Glatz|first=Carol|date=2 April 2013|publisher=Catholic News Service|accessdate=15 September 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt;

Francis chose not to live in the official [[papal apartments|papal residence]] in the [[Apostolic Palace]], but to remain in the [[Domus Sanctae Marthae|Vatican guest house]], in a suite in which he can receive visitors and hold meetings. He is the first pope since [[Pope Pius X]] to live outside the papal apartments.&lt;ref name="Vatican guesthouse"&gt;{{cite web|url=http://ncronline.org/news/vatican/pope-francis-live-vatican-guesthouse-not-papal-apartments|title=Pope Francis to live in Vatican guesthouse, not papal apartments|last=Wooden|first=Cindy|date=26 March 2013|accessdate=26 March 2013|work=[[National Catholic Reporter]]}}&lt;/ref&gt; Francis still appears at the window of the Apostolic Palace for the Sunday [[Angelus]].&lt;ref name="guesthouse"&gt;Speciale, Alessandro, [http://www.religionnews.com/2013/03/26/pope-francis-opts-for-vatican-guesthouse-instead-of-papal-apartment/ "Pope Francis opts for Vatican guesthouse instead of spacious papal apartment"], Religion News Service, 26 March 2013, Retrieved 27 March 2013&lt;/ref&gt;

===Election===
{{Main article|Papal conclave, 2013|Papal inauguration of Pope Francis}}
[[File:Papa Francisco recin elegido 2.jpg|thumb|left|upright=1.25|Francis appears in public for the first time as pope, at St. Peter's Basilica balcony, 13 March 2013.]]
Bergoglio was elected pope on 13 March 2013,&lt;ref name="directory"/&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.vatican.va/holy_father/francesco/elezione/index_sp.htm |title=FRANCISCUS |date=13 March 2013 |publisher=Holy See |quote=Annuntio vobis gaudium magnum; habemus Papam: Eminentissimum ac Reverendissimum Dominum, Dominum Georgium MariumSanctae Romanae Ecclesiae Cardinalem Bergoglio qui sibi nomen imposuit Franciscum |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6F60wLVTO?url=http://www.vatican.va/holy_father/francesco/elezione/index_sp.htm |archivedate=13 March 2013 |deadurl=yes |df= }}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.news.va/en/news/habemus-papam-cardinal-bergolio-elected-pope|title=Habemus Papam! Cardinal Bergoglio Elected Pope Francis|date=|publisher=Official Vatican Network|accessdate=14 March 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt; the second day of the [[Papal conclave, 2013|2013 papal conclave]], taking the [[papal name]] Francis.&lt;ref name="directory"/&gt;&lt;ref name="cnbc"&gt;{{cite news|url=https://www.cnbc.com/id/100538976|title=Cardinal Jorge Mario Bergoglio of Argentina Named as New Pope of the Roman Catholic Church|date=13 March 2013|publisher=CNBC|accessdate=13 March 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt; Francis was elected on the fifth ballot of the conclave.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|url=http://www.catholicsun.org/2013/03/13/white-smoke-cardinals-elect-new-pope-on-fifth-ballot/|title=White smoke: Cardinals elect new pope on fifth ballot|date=13 March 2013|publisher=The Catholic Sun|accessdate=15 March 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt; The [[Habemus Papam]] was delivered by [[Cardinal protodeacon]] [[Jean-Louis Tauran]].&lt;ref name="SuarezPBS"&gt;{{cite news|url=https://www.pbs.org/newshour/rundown/2013/03/a-new-pope-and-maybe-a-new-era.html|title=A New Pope, and Maybe a New Era|last=Suarez|first=Ray|publisher=PBS|accessdate=15 March 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt; Cardinal [[Christoph Schnborn]] later said that Bergoglio was elected following two supernatural signs, one in the conclave and hence confidential, and a Latin-American couple of friends of Schnborn who whispered Bergoglio's name in Schnborn's ear; Schnborn commented "if these people say Bergoglio, that's an indication of the Holy Spirit".&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|url=https://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/religion/the-pope/10056994/Pope-Francis-elected-after-supernatural-signs-in-the-Conclave-Cardinal.html|title=Pope Francis elected after supernatural 'signs' in the Conclave, says Cardinal|last=Bingham|first=John|date=14 May 2013|publisher=The Daily Telegraph|location=London}}&lt;/ref&gt;

Instead of accepting his cardinals' congratulations while seated on the [[papal throne]], Francis received them standing, reportedly an immediate sign of a changing approach to formalities at the Vatican.&lt;ref name="NewEuropeHabemus"&gt;{{cite news|url=http://www.neurope.eu/article/habemus-papam-new-pope-new-lifestyle-vatican|title=Habemus Papam: New Pope, new lifestyle in the Vatican|date=15 March 2013|publisher=New Europe|accessdate=15 March 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt; During his first appearance as pontiff on the balcony of [[Saint Peter's Basilica]], he wore a white [[cassock]], not the red, ermine-trimmed [[mozzetta]]&lt;ref name=NewEuropeHabemus/&gt;&lt;ref name="Uebbing"&gt;{{cite news|url=http://www.catholicnewsagency.com/news/pope-francis-personality-begins-to-change-routines/|title=Pope Francis' personality begins to change routines|last=Uebbing|first=David|publisher=Catholic News Agency|accessdate=15 March 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt; used by previous popes.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.dieter-philippi.de/en/ecclesiastical-fineries/the-mozzetta-of-the-pope|title=The Mozzetta of the Pope|last=Philippi|first=Dieter|publisher=Philippi Collection|accessdate=15 March 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt; He also wore the same iron [[pectoral cross]] that he had worn as Archbishop of Buenos Aires, rather than the gold one worn by his predecessors.&lt;ref name=Uebbing/&gt;

After being elected and choosing his name, his first act was bestowing the ''[[Urbi et Orbi]]'' blessing to thousands of pilgrims gathered in [[St. Peter's Square]]. Before blessing the crowd, he asked those in St. Peter's Square to pray for his predecessor, "the bishop emeritus of Rome" Pope Benedict XVI, and for himself as the new "bishop of Rome".&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|url=http://in.reuters.com/article/2013/03/13/pope-francis-blessing-idINDEE92C0FE20130313|title=Pope Francis delivers first blessing, asks world for prayers &amp;#124; Reuters|date=14 March 2013|publisher=Reuters|accessdate=19 March 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt;

Pope Francis held his [[papal inauguration]] on 19 March 2013 in [[St. Peter's Square]] in the [[Vatican City|Vatican]].&lt;ref name="directory"/&gt; He celebrated Mass in the presence of various political and religious leaders from around the world.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|url=http://www.bbc.co.uk/news/world-europe-21839069|title=Pope Francis in plea for poor as inauguration Mass held|date=19 March 2013|publisher=BBC News|accessdate=21 March 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt; In his homily Pope Francis focused on the [[Solemnity of Saint Joseph]], the liturgical day on which the Mass was celebrated.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|author=Pope Francis|url=http://www.vatican.va/holy_father/francesco/homilies/2013/documents/papa-francesco_20130319_omelia-inizio-pontificato_en.html|title=Homily of Pope Francis|date=19 March 2013|publisher=Holy See|accessdate=23 March 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt;

===Name===
[[File:Pope Francis among the people at St. Peter's Square - 12 May 2013.jpg|thumb|upright=1.25|In [[St. Peter's Square]]]]
At his first audience on 16 March 2013, Francis told journalists that he had chosen the name in honor of [[Francis of Assisi|Saint Francis of Assisi]], and had done so because he was especially concerned for the well-being of the poor.&lt;ref name="Pope Francis explains decision to take St Francis of Assisi's name"/&gt;&lt;ref name="New Pope Francis visits St. Mary Major, collects suitcases and pays bill at hotel"/&gt;&lt;ref&gt;Michael Martinez, [http://www.cnn.com/2013/03/13/world/pope-name/index.html?hpt=hp_t1 CNN Vatican analyst: Pope Francis' name choice 'precedent shattering'], [[CNN]] (13 March 2013). Retrieved 13 March 2013.&lt;/ref&gt; He explained that, as it was becoming clear during the conclave voting that he would be elected the new bishop of Rome, the Brazilian Cardinal [[Cludio Hummes]] had embraced him and whispered, "Don't forget the poor", which had made Bergoglio think of the saint.&lt;ref&gt;Laura Smith-Spark et al. : [https://web.archive.org/web/20130317035923/http://edition.cnn.com/2013/03/16/world/europe/vatican-new-pope/index.html?hpt=hp_t1 Pope Francis explains name, calls for church 'for the poor'] CNN,16 March 2013&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|url=http://www.bbc.co.uk/news/world-europe-21812545|title=Pope Francis wants 'poor Church for the poor'|date=16 March 2013|publisher=BBC News|accessdate=16 March 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt; Bergoglio had previously expressed his admiration for St. Francis, explaining that "He brought to Christianity an idea of poverty against the luxury, pride, vanity of the civil and ecclesiastical powers of the time. He changed history."&lt;ref name="bethune"&gt;Bethune, Brian, [http://www2.macleans.ca/2013/03/26/man-of-the-people-2/ "Pope Francis: How the first New World pontiff could save the church"], Maclean's, 26 March 2013, Retrieved 27 March 2013&lt;/ref&gt;

This is the first time that a pope has been named ''Francis''. On the day of his election, the Vatican clarified that his official papal name was "Francis", not "Francis I", i.e. no [[regnal number]] is used for him. A Vatican spokesman said that the name would become Francis I if and when there is a Francis II.&lt;ref name="New Pope Francis visits St. Mary Major, collects suitcases and pays bill at hotel"/&gt;&lt;ref name="Vatican: It's Pope Francis, not Pope Francis I"/&gt; It is the first time since [[Pope Lando]]'s 913914 reign that a serving pope holds a name not used by a predecessor.{{efn|[[Pope John Paul I]], elected in 1978, took a new combination of already used names, in honor of his two immediate predecessors, [[Pope John XXIII|John XXIII]] and [[Pope Paul VI|Paul VI]].&lt;ref&gt;{{cite book |last=Knowles |first=Leo |title=Modern Heroes of the Church|year=2003|publisher=Our Sunday Visitor Publishing|location=Huntington, IN |isbn=1-931709-46-7 |page=115|url=https://books.google.com/?id=lP3Iw8WV_MoC&amp;pg=PA115}}&lt;/ref&gt; }}

Francis also said that some cardinal-electors had jokingly suggested to him that he should choose either "Adrian", since [[Pope Adrian VI]] had been a reformer of the church, or "Clement" to settle the score with [[Pope Clement XIV]], who had [[Suppression of the Society of Jesus|suppressed the Jesuit order]].&lt;ref name=PapalName&gt;[http://www.vatican.va/holy_father/francesco/speeches/2013/march/documents/papa-francesco_20130316_rappresentanti-media_en.html Audience to Representatives of the Communications Media&amp;nbsp; Address of the Holy Father Pope Francis]&amp;nbsp; [[vatican.va]]&amp;nbsp; [[Paul VI Audience Hall]] Saturday, 16 March 2013&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;Marco R. della Cava, [https://www.usatoday.com/story/news/world/2013/03/16/pope-francis-press-conference/1992355/ Pope Francis charms media in first press address], ''USA Today'' (16 March 2013). Retrieved 16 March 2013.&lt;/ref&gt; In February 2014, it was reported that Bergoglio, had he been elected in 2005, would have chosen the pontifical name of "John XXIV" in honor of [[Pope John XXIII]]. It was said that he told Cardinal [[Francesco Marchisano]]: "John, I would have called myself John, like the Good Pope; I would have been completely inspired by him".&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://ncronline.org/blogs/ncr-today/francis-once-thought-taking-name-john-after-pope-john-xxiii|title=Francis once thought of taking the name John, after Pope John XXIII|date=11 February 2014|publisher=National Catholic Reporter|accessdate=26 May 2015}}&lt;/ref&gt;

===Curia===
[[File:Francis Inauguration fc10.jpg|thumb|Inauguration of Pope Francis, 19 March 2013]]
On 16 March 2013, Pope Francis asked all those in senior positions of the [[Roman Curia]] to provisionally continue in office.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|url=http://ncronline.org/blogs/ncr-today/francis-drops-first-hint-reform-may-be-real|title=Francis drops first hint that reform may be real|last=Allen, Jr.|first=John L.|date=16 March 2013|publisher=National Catholic Reporter|accessdate=17 March 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt; He named [[Alfred Xuereb]] as his personal secretary.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|url=http://www.maltatoday.com.mt/en/newsdetails/news/world/Gozitan-Mons-Alfred-Xuereb-appointed-Pope-Francis-secretary-20130318|title=Gozitan Mgr Alfred Xuereb appointed Pope's official secretary|last=Stagno-Navarra|first=Karl|date=18 March 2013|publisher=Malta Today|accessdate=21 March 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt; On 6 April he named [[Jos Rodrguez Carballo]] as secretary for the [[Congregation for Institutes of Consecrated Life and Societies of Apostolic Life]], a position that had been vacant for several months.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|url=http://ncronline.org/blogs/ncr-today/pope-appoints-franciscan-religious-congregation|title=Pope appoints Franciscan to religious congregation|last=McElwee|first=Joshua J.|date=6 April 2013|publisher=National Catholic Reporter|accessdate=7 April 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt; Francis abolished the bonuses paid to Vatican employees upon the election of a new pope, amounting to several million Euros, opting instead to donate the money to charity.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|url=http://www.upi.com/Top_News/World-News/2013/04/19/Pope-scraps-Vatican-staff-bonuses-directs-money-to-charity/UPI-14541366354800/|title=Pope scraps Vatican staff bonuses, directs money to charity|date=19 April 2013|publisher=UPI|accessdate=21 April 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt; He also abolished the 25,000 annual bonus paid to the cardinals serving on the Board of Supervisors for the [[Institute for the Works of Religion|Vatican bank]].&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|url=http://vaticaninsider.lastampa.it/en/the-vatican/detail/articolo/francesco-francis-francisco-24204/|title=Ior: Cuts to the cardinals' "earnings"|last=Galeazi|first=Giacomo|date=19 April 2013|publisher=Las Stampa: Vatican Insider|accessdate=21 April 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt;

On 13 April 2013, he named eight cardinals to a new [[Council of Cardinal Advisers]] to advise him on revising the organizational structure of the Roman Curia. The group included several known as critics of Vatican operations and only one member of the Curia.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|url=http://ncronline.org/blogs/ncr-today/pope-taps-eight-cardinals-lead-reform|title=Pope taps eight cardinals to lead reform|last=Allen, Jr.|first=John L.|date=13 April 2013|publisher=National Catholic Reporter|accessdate=14 April 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt; They are [[Giuseppe Bertello]], president of the [[President of the Pontifical Commission for Vatican City State|Vatican City State governorate]]; [[Francisco Javier Errazuriz Ossa]] from Chile; [[Oswald Gracias]] from India; [[Reinhard Marx]] from Germany; [[Laurent Monsengwo Pasinya]] from the Democratic Republic of the Congo; [[George Pell]] from Australia; [[Sen Patrick O'Malley|Sen O'Malley]] from the United States; and [[Oscar Andres Rodriguez Maradiaga]] from Honduras. He appointed Bishop [[Marcello Semeraro]] secretary for the group and scheduled its first meeting for 13 October.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|url=http://vaticaninsider.lastampa.it/en/the-vatican/detail/articolo/francesco-francis-francisco-24044/|title=Pope Francis sets up a group of eight cardinals to advise him|last=O'Connell|first=Gerard|date=13 April 2013|publisher=La Stampa: Vatican Insider|accessdate=13 April 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt;

===Early issues===
[[File:Pope Francis Travels.svg|thumb|upright=1.35| Map indicating [[List of pastoral visits of Pope Francis outside Italy|countries visited by Francis as pope]]]]
In March 2013, 21 British Catholic [[House of Lords|peers]] and [[House of Commons of the United Kingdom|Members of Parliament]] from all [[Political parties in the United Kingdom|parties]] asked Francis to allow married men in Great Britain to be ordained as priests, keeping celibacy as the rule for bishops. They asked it on the grounds that it would be anomalous that married Anglican priests can be received into the Catholic Church and ordained as priests, by means of either the [[Pastoral Provision]] of 20 June 1980 or the 2009 [[Anglican ordinariate]], but married Catholic men cannot do the same.&lt;ref name="teahan"&gt;Teahan, Madeleine, [http://www.catholicherald.co.uk/news/2013/03/27/catholic-mps-urge-pope-francis-to-allow-ordination-of-married-men/ "Catholic MPs urge Pope Francis to allow ordination of married men"], The Catholic Herald, 27 March 2013, Retrieved 27 March 2013&lt;/ref&gt;

[[Fouad Twal]], the [[Latin Patriarch of Jerusalem]], included a call in his 2013 Easter homily for the Pope to visit [[Jerusalem]].&lt;ref&gt;[http://www.globalpost.com/dispatch/news/afp/130331/jerusalem-prelate-urges-pope-visit-the-holy-city "Jerusalem prelate urges pope to visit holy city"], GlobalPost (from ''Agence France-Presse''), 31 March 2013, Retrieved 31 March 2013&lt;/ref&gt; [[Louis Raphal I Sako|Louis Raphael I]], the [[Chaldean Catholic Church|Chaldean Catholic Patriarch]], asked the Pope to visit the "embattled Christian community" in Iraq.&lt;ref name="iraq"&gt;[http://www.catholicculture.org/news/headlines/index.cfm?storyid=17405 "Chaldean prelate invites pope to visit Iraq"], catholicculture.org, 22 March 2013, Retrieved 31 March 2013&lt;/ref&gt;

On the first [[Maundy Thursday|Holy Thursday]] following his election, Francis washed and kissed the feet of ten male and two female juvenile offenders, not all Catholic, aged from 14 to 21, imprisoned at Rome's Casal del Marmo detention facility, telling them [[foot washing|the ritual of foot washing]] is a sign that he is at their service.&lt;ref name="muslimfeetwashing"&gt;Speciale, Alessandro, [https://www.washingtonpost.com/national/on-faith/pope-washes-feet-of-two-girls-two-muslims-at-youth-prison/2013/03/28/0a7c573e-97e5-11e2-b5b4-b63027b499de_story.html "Pope washes feet of two girls, two Muslims at youth prison"], ''Washington Post'' (''On Faith''), 29 March 2013, Retrieved 29 March 2013&lt;/ref&gt; This was the first time that a pope had included women in this ritual; although he had already done so when he was archbishop.&lt;ref name="muslimfeetwashing"/&gt; One of the male and one of the female prisoners were [[Muslim]].&lt;ref name="muslimfeetwashing" /&gt;&lt;ref&gt;Heller, Jill, [http://www.ibtimes.com/pope-francis-washes-muslim-womans-feet-holy-thursday-did-he-violate-catholic-church-canon-ahead# "Pope Francis Washes Muslim Woman's Feet On Holy Thursday: Did He Violate Catholic Church Canon Ahead Of Easter?"], ibtimes.com, 29 March 2013, Retrieved 30 March 2013&lt;/ref&gt;

On 31 March 2013 Francis used his first [[Urbi et Orbi|Easter homily]] to make a plea for peace throughout the world, specifically mentioning the Middle East, Africa, and North and South Korea.&lt;ref name="eastersermon"&gt;Lymon, Eric J., [https://www.usatoday.com/story/news/world/2013/03/31/easter-vatican-pope/2039617/ "Pope Francis makes pleas for peace on Easter Sunday"], Usa Today, 31 March 2013, Retrieved 31 March 2013&lt;/ref&gt; He also spoke out against those who give in to "easy gain" in a world filled with greed, and made a plea for humanity to become a better guardian of creation by protecting the environment.&lt;ref name="eastersermon"/&gt; He said that "[w]e ask the risen Jesus, who turns death into life, to change hatred into love, vengeance into forgiveness, war into peace."&lt;ref name="risenjesus"&gt;[http://www.bbc.co.uk/news/world-europe-21986185 "Pope Francis delivers Easter plea for peace"], BBC News, 31 March 2013, Retrieved 31 March 2013&lt;/ref&gt; Although the Vatican had prepared greetings in 65 languages, Francis chose not to read them.&lt;ref name="languages"/&gt; According to the Vatican, the pope "at least for now, feels at ease using Italian, the everyday language of the Holy See".&lt;ref&gt;[https://web.archive.org/web/20130401151028/http://www.latimes.com/news/world/worldnow/la-fg-wn-pope-francis-easter-mass-20130331%2C0%2C1763686.story "Pope Francis makes an Easter plea for peace"], Los Angeles Times (from AP), 31 March 2013, Retrieved 31 March 2013&lt;/ref&gt;

In 2013, Francis initially reaffirmed the [[Congregation for the Doctrine of the Faith]]'s program to [[Leadership Conference of Women Religious#Doctrinal issues|reform the U.S. Leadership Conference of Women Religious]],&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|url=http://www.catholicnewsagency.com/news/pope-backs-reform-of-us-sisters-leadership-conference/|title=Pope backs reform of US sisters' leadership conference|last=Uebbing|first=David|date=15 April 2013|publisher=Catholic News Agency|accessdate=19 April 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt; initiated under his predecessor, Pope Benedict XVI. ''[[The New York Times]]'' reported that the Vatican had formed the opinion in 2012 that the sisters' group was tinged with feminist influences, focused too much on ending social and economic injustice and not enough on stopping abortion, and permitted speakers at its meetings who questioned church doctrine.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2013/04/16/us/pope-upholds-reprimand-of-nuns-group.html|title=Pope Upholds Reprimand of American Nuns' Group|last=Goodstein|first=Laurie|date=15 April 2013|publisher=The New York Times|accessdate=27 May 2015}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.catholicnewsagency.com/news/pope-backs-reform-of-us-sisters-leadership-conference/|title=David Uebbing, "Pope backs reform of US sisters' leadership conference", '&amp;#39;Catholic News Agency'&amp;#39;, 15 April 2013|date=|publisher=Catholic News Agency|accessdate=23 June 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt; However, in April 2015 the investigation was brought to a close. The timing of the closure may have anticipated [[Pope Francis's visit to the United States|a visit by Francis to the U.S.]] in September 2015.&lt;ref&gt;[https://www.nytimes.com/2015/04/17/us/catholic-church-ends-takeover-of-leadership-conference-of-women-religious.html Vatican Ends Battle With U.S. Catholic Nuns' Group] The New York Times, 16 April 2015, Retrieved 27 May 2015&lt;/ref&gt;

On 12 May, Francis carried out his first [[canonization]]s of candidates approved for sainthood during the reign of Benedict XVI: the first Colombian saint, [[Laura of Saint Catherine of Siena]], the second female Mexican saint, [[Maria Guadalupe Garcia Zavala]], both of the 20th century, and the 813 15th-century [[Martyrs of Otranto]]. He said: "While we venerate the martyrs of Otranto, ask God to support the many Christians who still suffer from violence and give them the courage and fate and respond to evil with goodness." He also commented on abortion, saying legislation should be introduced to "protect all human beings from the first moment of their existence."&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.aljazeera.com/video/europe/2013/05/201351212314711566.html|title=Francis canonises first saints of his papacy|date=12 May 2013|publisher=Al Jazeera English|accessdate=}}&lt;/ref&gt;

===Consultation with Catholic laity===
A February 2014 survey by [[World Values Survey]] cited in ''[[The Washington Post]]'' and ''[[Time (magazine)|Time]]'' shows how the unity Pope Francis had created could be challenged. Although views about Francis personally were favorable, many Catholics disagreed with at least some of his teachings. The survey found that members of the Catholic Church are deeply divided over abortion, artificial contraception, divorce, the ordination of women, and married priests.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/national/pope-francis-faces-church-divided-over-doctrine-global-poll-of-catholics-finds/2014/02/08/e90ecef4-8f89-11e3-b227-12a45d109e03_story.html|title=Pope Francis faces church divided over doctrine, global poll of Catholics finds|last=Boorstein|first=Michelle|date=9 February 2014|publisher=The Washington Post|accessdate=4 October 2014}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|url=http://world.time.com/2014/02/09/poll-catholic-beliefs-at-odds-with-vatican-doctrine/|title=Poll: Catholic Beliefs at Odds With Vatican Doctrine|last=Frizell|first=Sam|date=9 February 2014|work=TIME.com|accessdate=4 October 2014}}&lt;/ref&gt; In the same month Pope Francis asked parishes to provide answers to an official questionnaire&lt;ref&gt;[https://web.archive.org/web/20141027095239/http://press.vatican.va/content/dam/salastampa/it/bollettino/documentazione-linkata/Documento-preparatorio-IIIAssGenStraod_ENG.pdf Vatican: Synod of Bishops  Extraordinary General Assembly  Pastoral Challenges to the Family in the Context of Evangelization  Preparatory Document, Vatican City 2013]. Includes questionnaire to be circulated to Churches.&lt;/ref&gt; described as a "much broader consultation than just a survey"&lt;ref name="bbc27060172"&gt;{{cite news|url=http://www.bbc.co.uk/news/uk-27060172|title=Roman Catholic Church refuses survey request|date=17 April 2014|work=BBC News|accessdate=4 October 2014}}&lt;/ref&gt; regarding opinions among the laity. He continued to assert [[Catholic doctrine]], in less dramatic tone than his recent predecessors, who maintained that the Catholic Church is not a democracy of popular opinion.&lt;ref name="Clement"&gt;{{cite web|url=http://news.gnom.es/news/pope-francis-faces-church-divided-over-doctrine-global-poll-of-catholics-finds|title=Pope Francis faces church divided over doctrine, global poll of Catholics finds|last=Clement|first=Scott|date=23 February 2014|publisher=National News Service|archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20140223020300/http://news.gnom.es/news/pope-francis-faces-church-divided-over-doctrine-global-poll-of-catholics-finds|archivedate=23 February 2014|accessdate=26 May 2015}}&lt;/ref&gt;

[[Linda Woodhead]] of [[Lancaster University]] wrote of the survey Francis initiated, "it's not a survey in any sense that a social scientist would recognize." Woodhead said that many ordinary Catholics would have difficulty understanding theological [[jargon]] there. Nonetheless, she suspected the survey might be influential.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.religiondispatches.org/archive/culture/7408/new_poll___faithful_catholics__an_endangered_species|title=New Poll: 'Faithful Catholics' an Endangered Species|date=12 December 2013|publisher=University of Southern California|accessdate=4 October 2014}}&lt;/ref&gt;

The [[Catholic Church in England and Wales]] {{As of|2014|4|lc=y}} had refused to publish results of this survey; a Church spokesman said a senior Vatican official had expressly asked for summaries to remain confidential, and that orders had come from the Pope that the information should not be made public until after October. This disappointed many reformers who hoped the laity would be more involved in decision-making. Some other Catholic churches, for example in [[Catholic Church in Germany|Germany]] and [[Catholic Church in Austria|Austria]], published summaries of the responses to the survey, which showed a wide gap between Church teaching and the behavior of ordinary Catholics.&lt;ref name="bbc27060172" /&gt;

In a column he wrote for the Vatican's semi-official newspaper ''[[L'Osservatore Romano]]'', the head Prefect of the [[Supreme Tribunal of the Apostolic Signatura]], US Cardinal [[Raymond Leo Burke]], who has a long-standing reputation as one of the church's most vocal conservative hard-liners, said that Pope Francis opposed both abortion and [[gay marriage]].&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/local/us-cardinal-raymond-burke-pope-francis-opposes-abortion-and-gay-marriage/2014/02/21/de5dbf52-9b36-11e3-975d-107dfef7b668_story.html|title=U.S. Cardinal Raymond Burke: Pope Francis opposes abortion and gay marriage|last=Gibson|first=David|date=21 February 2014|work=The Washington Post|accessdate=28 May 2015}}&lt;/ref&gt; The Vatican's chief spokesman, Father [[Federico Lombardi]], also noted in the Vatican Press Office during the 2014 consistory meetings that Pope Francis and Cardinal [[Walter Kasper]] would not change or redefine any dogmas pertaining to Church theology on doctrinal matters.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.romereports.com/pg155838-lombardi-no-cardinal-believes-in-changing-church-doctrine-en|title=Lombardi: No cardinal believes in changing Church doctrine|date=|publisher=Rome Reports|accessdate=24 May 2014|deadurl=yes|archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20140301012319/http://www.romereports.com/pg155838-lombardi-no-cardinal-believes-in-changing-church-doctrine-en|archivedate=1 March 2014|df=dmy-all}}&lt;/ref&gt;

===Institute for the Works of Religion===
In the first months of Francis's papacy, the [[Institute for the Works of Religion]], informally known as the Vatican Bank, said that it would become more transparent in its financial dealings&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.aljazeera.com/news/europe/2013/05/201351616303447140.html|title=Pope Francis condemns global 'cult of money'|date=16 May 2013|publisher=Al Jazeera English|accessdate=28 May 2015}}&lt;/ref&gt; There had long been allegations of corruption and [[money laundering]] connected with the bank.&lt;ref name="bank1"&gt;{{cite web|url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2013/jun/26/vatican-bank-pope-francis-commission|title=Vatican bank faces review by Pope Francis commission|last=Davies|first=Lizzy|date=26 June 2013|publisher=The Guardian|accessdate=26 May 2015}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref name="bank2"&gt;{{cite news|url=http://www.bbc.co.uk/news/world-europe-23094320|title=BBC News&amp;nbsp; Monsignor Nunzio Scarano held in Vatican bank inquiry|last=Willey|first=David|date=28 June 2013|publisher=BBC News|accessdate=18 July 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt; Francis appointed a commission to advise him about reform of the Bank,&lt;ref name=bank1/&gt;&lt;ref name=bank2/&gt; and the finance consulting firm [[Promontory Financial Group]] was assigned to carry out a comprehensive investigation of all customer contacts of the bank on these facts.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.news.va/en/news/update-on-the-case-of-mons-nunzio-scarano|title=Update on the case of Mons. Nunzio Scarano|date=12 July 2013|series=Justice and Peace|publisher=Vatican Radio|accessdate=6 August 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt; Because of this affair the [[Devil's advocate#Origin|Promoter of Justice]] at the [[Law of Vatican City|Vatican Tribunal]] applied a [[letter rogatory]] for the first time in the history of the Republic of Italy at the beginning of August 2013.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://en.radiovaticana.va/news/2013/08/03/monsignor_scarano:_vatican_forwards_request_to_italy/in2-716914|title=Monsignor Scarano: Vatican forwards request to Italy|date=3 August 2013|series=Justice and Peace|publisher=Vatican Radio|accessdate=6 August 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt; In January 2014 Francis replaced four of the five cardinal overseers of the Vatican Bank, who had been confirmed in their positions in the final days of Benedict XVI's papacy.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|url=http://ncronline.org/news/vatican/pope-replaces-cardinals-serving-vatican-bank-oversight-commission|title=Pope replaces cardinals serving on Vatican bank oversight commission|last=Glatz|first=Carol|date=15 January 2014|publisher=National Catholic Reporter|accessdate=18 January 2014}}&lt;/ref&gt; Lay experts and clerics were looking into how the bank was run. [[Ernst von Freyberg]] was put in charge. [[Moneyval]] feels more reform is needed, and Francis may be willing to close the bank if the reforms prove too difficult.&lt;ref name="Jones"&gt;{{cite web|url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2014/mar/13/pope-francis-report-card|title=12 months a pope: Francis's report card after a year at the top|last=Davies|first=Lizzy|work=the Guardian|accessdate=4 October 2014}}&lt;/ref&gt; There is uncertainty how far reforms can succeed.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2015/aug/13/can-pope-francis-clean-up-gods-bank|title=Can Pope Francis clean up God's bank?|last=Vallely|first=Paul|work=the Guardian}}&lt;/ref&gt;

===Papal documents===
On 29 June 2013, Pope Francis published his first [[encyclical]], titled ''[[Lumen fidei]]''.&lt;ref name="The Holy See"/&gt;  It is a [[collaborative writing]] with Benedict XVI and talks about faith, complementing Benedict's previous encyclicals on charity and hope.&lt;ref name=lumen/&gt;  He published his second one, entitled {{italics correction|''[[Laudato si']]''}}, on 18 June 2015, concerning care for the planet.&lt;ref name="Jim Yardley and Laurie Goodstein"/&gt; On 24 November 2013, he published his [[apostolic exhortation]] ''[[Evangelii gaudium]]'',&lt;ref name="Evangelii gaudium"/&gt; with his views on [[#Faith and evangelization|faith and evangelization]].&lt;ref name=egsummary/&gt; On 8 April 2016, Pope Francis published his second apostolic exhortation, ''[[Amoris laetitia]]'',&lt;ref name="Amoris laetitia"&gt;Pope Francis (8 April 2016), [http://w2.vatican.va/content/francesco/en/apost_exhortations/documents/papa-francesco_esortazione-ap_20160319_amoris-laetitia.html Amoris laetitia]. The Holy See. Retrieved 20 April 2016.&lt;/ref&gt; remarking on love within the family. Controversy arose at the end of 2016 when four cardinals formally asked Pope Francis for clarifications, particularly on the issue of giving communion to divorced and civilly remarried Catholics.&lt;ref&gt;{{Cite news|url=http://www.lastampa.it/2016/11/14/vaticaninsider/eng/the-vatican/four-cardinals-openly-challenge-francis-over-amoris-laetitia-62np8ZYXQkeXyBamk0M0jP/pagina.html|title=Four cardinals openly challenge Francis over "Amoris Laetitia"|last=McElwee|first=Josh|date=14 November 2016|newspaper=Vatican Insider|accessdate=|work=|via=}}&lt;/ref&gt;

His [[motu proprio]]s include  ''[[Ai nostri tempi]]'' and ''[[De concordia inter codices]]''. Francis issued another titled ''[[Maiorem hac dilectionem]]'' which created a new path towards canonization for certain causes.

He established two new Secretariats (top-level departments) in the Roman Curia: the [[Secretariat for the Economy]], and the [[Secretariat for Communications]]. He [[Matrimonial nullity trial reforms of Pope Francis|reformed]] the process for declaring [[Declaration of nullity|matrimonial nullity]].&lt;ref name=trials/&gt;

On 8 December 2017, Pope Francis signed a new apostolic constitution on ecclesiastical universities and faculties ''[[Veritatis gaudium]]'', published 29 January 2018.&lt;ref&gt;https://www.catholicnewsagency.com/news/pope-revamps-ecclesiastical-universities-in-new-apostolic-constitution-77172 Pope revamps ecclesiastical universities in new apostolic constitution], Catholic News Agency, accessed 29 January 2018.&lt;/ref&gt;

A further Apostolic Exhortation, ''[[Gaudete et exsultate]]'' (''Rejoice and be glad''), was published on 19 March 2018, dealing with "the [[Universal call to holiness|call to holiness]] in today's world" and countering contemporary versions of the [[Gnosticism|gnostic]] and [[Pelagianism|Pelagian]] [[Heresy in Christianity|heresies]] from "earlier Christian times".&lt;ref&gt;Pope Francis, [http://w2.vatican.va/content/francesco/en/apost_exhortations/documents/papa-francesco_esortazione-ap_20180319_gaudete-et-exsultate.html ''Gaudete et exsultate], 19 March 2018, accessed 29 April 2018&lt;/ref&gt;

===Clerical titles===
In January 2014, Pope Francis said that he would appoint fewer [[monsignor]]s and only assign those honored to the lowest of the three surviving ranks of monsignor, [[Chaplain of His Holiness]]. It would be awarded only to [[diocesan priest]]s at least 65 years old. During his 15 years as Archbishop of Buenos Aires, Pope Francis never sought the title for any of his priests. It is believed he associates it with clerical careerism and hierarchy, though he did not apply this restriction to clergy working in the Roman Curia or diplomatic corps, where careerism is an even greater concern.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|url=http://vaticaninsider.lastampa.it/en/the-vatican/detail/articolo/31027/|title=Pope abolishes honorary title of monsignor for diocesan priests under the age of 65|last=O'Connell|first=Gerard|date=4 January 2014|publisher=Vatican Insider|accessdate=4 January 2014}}&lt;/ref&gt;

===Canonizations and beatifications===
{{Main article|List of saints canonized by Pope Francis|List of people beatified by Pope Francis|List of people declared venerable by Pope Francis}}
[[File:Canonizao de Francisco e Jacinta Marto (13 de Maio de 2017).png|thumb|left|Pope Francis presides over the canonization of [[Francisco and Jacinta Marto]], in the [[Sanctuary of Ftima]], Portugal, in 2017]]
Pope Francis presided over the first canonizations of his pontificate on 12 May 2013 in which he canonized Antonio Primaldo and his 812 companions as well as the nuns Laura of Saint Catherine of Siena and Maria Guadalupe Garcia Zavalia  in this first canonization he surpassed the record of Pope John Paul II in canonizing the most saints in a pontificate.&lt;ref&gt;{{citeweb|url=http://www.aljazeera.com/video/europe/2013/05/201351212314711566.html|title=Francis canonises first saints of his papacy|date=12 May 2013|publisher=Al Jazeera English}}&lt;/ref&gt; Francis approved the equipollent canonization of [[Angela of Foligno]] the following 9 October and then the Jesuit [[Peter Faber]] the following 17 December.&lt;ref&gt;{{citeweb|url=https://www.catholicculture.org/news/headlines/index.cfm?storyid=20123|title=Vatican cardinal explains why Pope Francis canonized St. Angela of Foligno|publisher=Catholic Culture|date=7 January 2014|accessdate=14 October 2017}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{citeweb|url=https://www.catholicnewsagency.com/news/pope-francis-declares-sainthood-of-early-jesuit-peter-faber|title=Pope Francis declares sainthood of early Jesuit, Peter Faber|publisher=Catholic News Agency|date=17 December 2013|accessdate=14 October 2017}}&lt;/ref&gt;

The pope approved further equipollent canonizations on 3 April 2014 for the Jesuit [[Jos de Anchieta]] as well as the [[Ursulines|Ursuline]] nun [[Marie of the Incarnation (Ursuline)|Marie of the Incarnation]] and bishop [[Franois de Laval]].&lt;ref&gt;{{citeweb|url=http://www.catholicworldreport.com/2014/04/07/pope-francis-canonizes-three-new-saints-of-the-americas/|title=Pope Francis canonizes three new saints of the Americas|publisher=Catholic World Report|date=7 April 2014|accessdate=14 October 2017}}&lt;/ref&gt; Francis canonized his two predecessors John XXIII and John Paul II on 27 April 2014 and canonized six additional saints the following 23 November.&lt;ref&gt;{{citeweb|url=http://edition.cnn.com/2014/04/27/world/pope-canonization/index.html|publisher=CNN|title=Sainthood for John Paul II, John XXIII in canonization ceremony|date=27 April 2014|accessdate=14 October 2017}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{citeweb|publisher=Reuters|url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-pope-saints/pope-declares-sainthood-of-two-indians-four-italians-idUSKCN0J70KT20141124|title=Pope declares sainthood of two Indians, four Italians|date=24 November 2014|accessdate=14 October 2017}}&lt;/ref&gt; The pope canonized [[Joseph Vaz]] on his visit to Sri Lanka on 14 January 2015 and canonized a further four saints on the following 17 May; he canonized Junpero Serra on 23 September while visiting the United States and then canonized four saints on 18 October including the [[Louis Martin and Marie-Azlie Gurin|first married couple]] to be named as saints.&lt;ref&gt;{{citeweb|url=https://www.news.lk/fetures/item/5711-canonization-of-saint-joseph-vaz-the-first-sri-lankan-saint|title=Canonization of Saint Joseph Vaz, the first Sri Lankan Saint|publisher=News.lk|date=|accessdate=14 October 2017}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{citeweb|url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-pope-palestinians-saints/pope-francis-canonizes-two-Palestinian-nuns-idUSKBN0O208420150517|title=Pope Francis canonizes two Palestinian nuns|date=17 May 2015|publisher=Reuters|accessdate=14 October 2017}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{citeweb|url=http://edition.cnn.com/2015/09/23/us/pope-junipero-serra-canonization/index.html|title=Pope Francis canonizes controversial saint|publisher=CNN|date=23 September 2017|accessdate=14 October 2017}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{citeweb|url=http://www.catholicherald.co.uk/news/2015/10/19/pope-francis-canonises-the-martins/|title=Pope Francis canonises Louis and Zlie Martin|publisher=Catholic Herald|date=19 October 2015|accessdate=14 October 2017}}&lt;/ref&gt; Francis canonized [[Elisabeth Hesselblad|Maria Elisabeth Hesselblad]] and [[Stanislaus Papczyski]] on 5 June 2016 and then canonized [[Teresa of Calcutta]] on 4 September; he canonized seven additional saints on 16 October.&lt;ref&gt;{{citeweb|publisher=VOA News|date=5 June 2016|accessdate=14 October 2017|title=Pope Proclaims 2 New Saints in Canonization Mass|url=https://www.voanews.com/a/pope-new-saints/3362508.html}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{citeweb|title=Mother Teresa officially becomes a saint at canonization ceremony in Vatican City|date=5 September 2016|publisher=ABC News Australia|accessdate=14 October 2017|url=http://www.abc.net.au/news/2016-09-04/mother-teresa-canonised-at-ceremony-in-st-peters-cathedral/7813048}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=https://www.cbsnews.com/news/pope-francis-jose-gabriel-del-rosario-brochero-argentina-gaucho-priest-sainthood/|work=CBS News|date=16 October 2016|title=Pope Francis makes Argentina's "gaucho priest" and 6 others saints}}&lt;/ref&gt; The pope canonized the two child visionaries [[Francisco and Jacinta Marto]] during his visit to Ftima in mid-2017 and canonized 35 additional saints on 15 October.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=https://www.americamagazine.org/faith/2017/05/13/pope-francis-makes-history-and-canonizes-jacinta-and-francisco-two-child-saints |publisher=America Magazine |date=13 May 2017 |author=Gerard O'Connell |title=Pope Francis makes history and canonizes Jacinta and Francisco, two child saints |accessdate=23 May 2018}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=https://cruxnow.com/vatican/2017/10/16/pope-canonizes-35-new-saints-including-feminist-priest/|title=Pope canonizes 35 new saints including a 'feminist' priest|accessdate=27 October 2017|date=16 October 2017|publisher=Crux|author=Ins San Martn}}&lt;/ref&gt;

The pope has also continued the practice of having beatifications celebrated in the place of the individual's origin though has presided over beatifications himself on three occasions for [[Korean Martyrs|Paul Yun Ji-Chung and 123 companions]] on 16 August 2014, his predecessor Pope Paul VI on 19 October 2014 and two Colombian martyrs on 8 September 2017.&lt;ref&gt;{{citeweb|url=http://www.bbc.com/news/world-asia-28814553|title=Pope beatifies 124 South Korean Catholic martyrs|publisher=BBC News|date=16 August 2014|accessdate=14 October 2017}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{citeweb|publisher=The New York Times|date=19 October 2014|accessdate=14 October 2017|title=Pope Francis Beatifies an Earlier Reformer, Paul VI|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2014/10/20/world/europe/pope-francis-beatifies-pope-paul-vi.html|author=Elisabetta Povoledo}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{citeweb|publisher=Vatican Radio|accessdate=14 October 2017|date=8 September 2017|title=Pope in Colombia at Beatification Mass: 'Reconciliation is not an abstract word'|url=http://en.radiovaticana.va/news/2017/09/08/pope_in_colombia_at_beatification_mass_reconciliation_is_n/1335599}}&lt;/ref&gt; The pope has approved beatifications for a range of men and women including the likes of [[lvaro del Portillo]] of [[Opus Dei]] (27 September 2014), the martyred archbishop [[scar Romero]] (23 May 2015) and several large groups of [[Martyrs of the Spanish Civil War|Spanish martyrs]].&lt;ref&gt;{{citeweb|title=Oscar Romero beatification draws huge El Salvador crowds|publisher=BBC News|date=23 May 2015|accessdate=14 October 2017|url=http://www.bbc.com/news/world-latin-america-32859627}}&lt;/ref&gt;

Francis also confirmed his predecessor [[Pope John Paul I|John Paul I]] to be [[Venerable]] on 8 November 2017.&lt;ref&gt;{{citeweb|publisher=Catholic Herald|date=9 November 2017|accessdate=10 November 2017|author=Junno Arocho Esteves|title=Pope Francis officially declares John Paul I 'venerable'|url=http://www.catholicherald.co.uk/news/2017/11/09/pope-francis-officially-declares-john-paul-i-venerable/}}&lt;/ref&gt;

====Doctor of the Church====
On 21 February 2015, Francis signed a decree naming [[Gregory of Narek|Saint Gregory of Narek]] as the 36th [[Doctor of the Church]]; he formally conferred the title upon the saint at a ceremony held in Saint Peter's Basilica on 12 April 2015 with delegations from the [[Armenian Catholic Church]] and the [[Armenian Apostolic Church]] present.&lt;ref&gt;{{citeweb|url=http://en.radiovaticana.va/news/2015/04/13/newest_doctor_of_the_church_st_gregory_of_narek/1136368|title=Newest Doctor of the Church: St. Gregory of Narek|date=13 April 2015|publisher=[[Vatican Radio]]|accessdate=23 September 2017}}&lt;/ref&gt;

===Consistories===
{{Main article|Cardinals created by Francis}}
At the first [[Papal consistory|consistory]] of his papacy, held on 22 February 2014, Francis created 19 new cardinals. At the time of their elevation to that rank, 16 of these new cardinals were under eighty years of age and thus eligible to vote in a [[papal conclave]].&lt;ref&gt;[http://www.bbc.co.uk/news/world-europe-26301947 Pope Francis appoints 19 new cardinals in Rome ceremony], BBC News, 22 February 2014. Accessed 22 February 2014&lt;/ref&gt; The new appointees included prelates from South America, Africa, and Asia, including appointees in some of the world's poorest countries, such as [[Chibly Langlois]] from [[Haiti]] and [[Philippe Oudraogo (bishop)|Philippe Nakellentuba Ouedraogo]] from [[Burkina Faso]].&lt;ref name="Reuters"&gt;[https://www.reuters.com/article/2014/02/22/us-pope-consistory-benedict-idUSBREA1L07X20140222 Pope Francis inducts new cardinals as predecessor Benedict looks on], Reuters, 22 February 2014. Accessed 22 February 2014&lt;/ref&gt; The consistory was a rare occasion in which Francis and his predecessor, [[Benedict XVI]], appeared together in public.&lt;ref name="Reuters"/&gt;

Benedict XVI also attended the second consistory on 14 February 2015, at which Francis elevated 20 new cardinals, with 15 under the age of eighty and five over the age of eighty. The pope continued his practice of appointing cardinals from the peripheries, such as [[Charles Maung Bo]] of [[Myanmar]] and [[Soane Patita Paini Mafi]] of [[Tonga]].&lt;ref&gt;"[http://www.news.va/en/news/230499 Annuncio di Concistoro per la creazione di nuovi Cardinali]" NEWS.VA Official Vatican Network. 4 January 2015. Retrieved 3 February 2018.&lt;/ref&gt;

Francis presided over the third consistory of his papacy on 19 November 2016, elevating 17 new cardinals. Of that total number at the time of their elevation, 13 were under the age of eighty and four were over the age of eighty. Francis continued his previous practice of elevating cardinals from the peripheries with an emphasis again on Asia and Africa, such as [[Patrick D'Rozario]] from Bangladesh and [[Dieudonn Nzapalainga]] from the [[Central African Republic]], while also naming the first three American cardinals of his papacy and only one Curial appointment.&lt;ref&gt;{{Cite news|url=http://en.radiovaticana.va/news/2017/06/28/pope_francis_allocution_at_cardinals_creation_consistory/1321890|title=Pope Francis: Allocution at Consistory for Creation of Cardinals|access-date=2018-02-05|language=en}}&lt;/ref&gt;

The pope presided over a fourth consistory for the elevation of 5 new cardinals on the afternoon of 28 June 2017. Each of the five were under the age of eighty, and were thus eligible to vote in a papal conclave. This consistory was noteworthy for the fact that, with the pope continuing the trend of elevating cardinals from a diverse range of areas, no cardinals elevated are of the Roman Curia, and one was a mere auxiliary bishop.&lt;ref&gt;{{Cite web|url=http://m.ncregister.com/daily-news/francis-fifth-a-synod-humanae-vitae-milestone-and-more-decentralized-church#.WnfnHYY76Ec|title=Francis Fifth: A Synod, Humanae Vitae Milestone and More Decentralized Church|website=m.ncregister.com|access-date=2018-02-05}}&lt;/ref&gt;

===Year of Mercy===
[[File:A Szentv kapujnak megnyitsa 2015 - Opening of the Holy Door 2015 4.jpeg|thumb|left|upright=0.85|Pope Francis opens the Holy Door marking the beginning of the Extraordinary Jubilee of Mercy.]]
{{main article|Extraordinary Jubilee of Mercy}}
With his April 2015 [[papal bull]] of indiction, ''Misericordiae Vultus'' ([[Latin]]: "The Face of [[Mercy]]"), Francis inaugurated a Special [[Jubilee (Christianity)|Jubilee Year]] of Mercy, to run from 8 December 2015, [[Solemnity]] of the [[Immaculate Conception]] of the [[Blessed Virgin Mary]], to the last Sunday before [[Advent]] and the Solemnity of the [[Feast of Christ the King]] of the Universe on 20 November 2016.

The [[Holy Door]]s of the major basilicas of Rome (including the Great Door of St. Peter's) were opened, and special "Doors of Mercy" were opened at cathedrals and other major churches around the world, where the faithful can earn indulgences by fulfilling the usual conditions of prayer for the Pope's intentions, confession, and detachment from sin, and communion.&lt;ref name=opening/&gt; During Lent of that year, special 24-hour penance services will be celebrated, and during the year, special qualified and experienced priests called "Missionaries of Mercy" will be available in every diocese to forgive even severe, special-case sins normally reserved to the Holy See's [[Apostolic Penitentiary]].&lt;ref name=Misericordiae/&gt;&lt;ref name=time/&gt;

=== Criticisms ===
[[File:Assemble du Synode des vques sur la famille en 2014.jpg|thumb|left|upright=1.15|A session of the Synod of Bishops in October 2014]]
{{See also|Amoris Laetitia}}
Since 2016, criticisms against Pope Francis by some conservative Catholics intensified.&lt;ref&gt;{{Cite news|url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2017/mar/04/vatican-civil-war-conservatives-battle-francis-lent|title=Civil war in the Vatican as conservatives battle Francis for the soul of Catholicism|last=[[Catherine Pepinster|Pepinster]]|first=[[Catherine Pepinster|Catherine]]|date=4 March 2017|work=The Guardian|accessdate=5 March 2017|issn=0261-3077}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite February 2017|df=dmy-all}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{Cite news|url=https://cruxnow.com/commentary/2017/03/05/pope-francis-conservative-critics-may-right/|title=How Pope Francis and his conservative critics may both be right|last=Schneider|first=Matthew|date=5 March 2017|work=Crux|access-date=7 March 2017}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{Cite Guardian|access-date=2017-11-01|language=en-GB|issn=0261-3077}}&lt;/ref&gt; An unnamed group of "anti-reform" cardinals has been claimed to state that Francis's supposed openness to "modernity on sexual morality, communion for remarried Catholics and friendly relations with other religions have opened a gulf between progressives and traditionalists."&lt;ref&gt;{{Cite news|url=http://www.thetimes.co.uk/article/anti-reform-cardinals-want-the-pope-to-quit-z3h75h22v|title=Anti-reform cardinals 'want the Pope to quit'|last=Willan|first=Philip|date=2 March 2017|work=|accessdate=5 March 2017}}&lt;/ref&gt;  Other conservatives have criticized his administrative style which they assert the pontiff has "wielded" against conservative opponents."&lt;ref&gt;{{Cite news|url=http://www.spectator.co.uk/2017/01/why-more-and-more-priests-cant-stand-pope-francis/|title=Why more and more priests can't stand Pope Francis|last=Thompson|first=Daniel|date=14 January 2017|newspaper=The Spectator|access-date=4 February 2017|work=|language=en-US|via=}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{Cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2017/02/07/world/europe/vatican-steve-bannon-pope-francis.html|title=Steve Bannon Carries Battles to Another Influential Hub: The Vatican|last=Horowitz|first=Jason|date=7 February 2017|newspaper=The New York Times|access-date=7 February 2017|issn=0362-4331}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{Cite news|url=https://reginamag.com/wp-content/cache/all/rome-in-eye-of-storm//index.html|title=Rome in Eye of A Storm  Regina Magazine|last=Stevens|first=Harry|date=8 December 2016|newspaper=Regina Magazine|access-date=11 February 2017|work=|language=en-US|via=|deadurl=yes|archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170212000334/https://reginamag.com/wp-content/cache/all/rome-in-eye-of-storm//index.html|archivedate=12 February 2017|df=dmy-all}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.catholicculture.org/commentary/otn.cfm?ID=1197|title=The ideological purge at the Vatican|last=Lawler|first=Phil|date=25 January 2017|website=www.catholicculture.org|access-date=11 February 2017}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{Cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2015/08/13/opinion/uki-goni-peronist-roots-of-pope-francis-politics.html|title=The Peronist Roots of Pope Francis' Politics|last=Goi|first=Uki|date=12 August 2015|newspaper=The New York Times|access-date=7 February 2017|issn=0362-4331}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{Cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2016/09/28/opinion/has-pope-francis-failed.html|title=Has Pope Francis Failed?|last=Schmitz|first=Matthew|date=28 September 2016|newspaper=The New York Times|access-date=7 February 2017|issn=0362-4331}}&lt;/ref&gt;  Since 2017, Francis has also been contrasted with [[US President]] [[Donald Trump]],&lt;ref&gt;{{Cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2017/03/04/opinion/sunday/is-the-pope-the-anti-trump.html|title=Is the Pope the Anti-Trump?|last=Ivereigh|first=Austen|date=4 March 2017|work=The New York Times|access-date=7 March 2017|issn=0362-4331}}&lt;/ref&gt; elected that year, with some conservative critics drawing comparisons between the two.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/news/acts-of-faith/wp/2016/02/19/what-donald-trump-and-pope-francis-actually-have-in-common/|title=What Donald Trump and Pope Francis actually have in common|last=Schmitz|first=Matthew|date=19 February 2016|website=Washington Post|access-date=7 February 2017}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{Cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2017/02/15/opinion/the-trump-eras-catholic-mirror.html?|title=The Trump Era's Catholic Mirror|last=Douthat|first=Ross|date=15 February 2017|newspaper=The New York Times|access-date=16 February 2017|work=|issn=0362-4331|via=}}&lt;/ref&gt; During the [[United States presidential election, 2016|2016 United States presidential election]], Francis said of Trump, "A person who thinks only about building walls, wherever they may be, and not building bridges, is not Christian. This is not the gospel." Trump responded saying "For a religious leader to question a person's faith is disgraceful."&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web |url=http://www.latimes.com/world/la-fg-pope-on-trump-wall-20160218-story.html |title=Trump and Pope Francis clash over immigration, another extraordinary campaign twist |last1=Lauter |first1=David |last2=Bierman |first2=Noah |date=February 18, 2016 |publisher=''The Washington Post'' |access-date=April 20, 2018}}&lt;/ref&gt; [[Federico Lombardi]] defended the Pope's remarks, saying that they were not by any means "a personal attack, nor an indication of who to vote for".&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.dailymail.co.uk/news/article-3454720/Popes-comments-Trump-not-personal-attack-papal-spokesman.html|title=Pope backs down against Trump: Vatican says 'not a personal attack'|publisher=|accessdate=21 March 2017}}&lt;/ref&gt;


The Pope drew criticism in 2013 for appearing on the balcony of St. Peter's Basilica with [[Godfried Danneels]] in the Pope's initial presentation, as well as appointments he received from Francis.&lt;ref&gt;[http://blogs.spectator.co.uk/2015/10/three-things-you-need-to-know-about-pope-francis-and-the-cardinal-disgraced-in-a-sex-abuse-scandal/ "Three things you need to know about Pope Francis and the cardinal disgraced in a sex abuse scandal"], Damian Thompson. The Spectator. 8 October 2015. Retrieved 11 February 2017&lt;/ref&gt; Danneels had previously recommended silence on sex-crimes committed by priests. In 2014 his rehabilitation of Fr. Mauro Inzoli, who was defrocked in 2012 for sexually abusing minors, sparked controversy.&lt;ref&gt;[http://www.spectator.co.uk/2017/01/why-more-and-more-priests-cant-stand-pope-francis/ "Why more and more priests can't stand Pope Francis"], Damian Thompson. The Spectator. 14 January 2017. Retrieved 11 February 2017&lt;/ref&gt; In 2015, he was criticized for supporting Chilean bishop Juan Barros, who was accused over covering up sex-crimes against minors.&lt;ref&gt;[https://www.theguardian.com/world/2015/mar/31/vatican-juan-barros-chile-bishop-appointment-sex-abuse "Vatican supports Chilean bishop despite allegations of sex abuse cover-up"], Stephanie Kirchgaessner. The Guardian. 31 March 2015. Retrieved 11 February 2017&lt;/ref&gt; In February 2017, further criticism from clergy sex abuse survivors erupted when it was revealed that the Pope had quietly made the Church-recommended sentence for clergy convicted of sex abuse a lifetime of prayer rather than a recommendation to serve time in jail.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://abcnews.go.com/Health/wireStory/pope-quietly-trims-sanctions-sex-abusers-seeking-mercy-45732198|title=ABC News|first=ABC|last=News|publisher=|accessdate=21 March 2017}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.ibtimes.co.uk/pope-francis-reduces-penalties-paedophile-priests-lifetime-prayer-1608591|title=Pope Francis reduces penalties for paedophile priests to a lifetime of prayer|first=Priya|last=Joshi|date=25 February 2017|publisher=|accessdate=21 March 2017}}&lt;/ref&gt;

In the Venezuelan crisis, Francis has not openly denounced the acts of [[Nicols Maduro|Nicolas Maduro]], despite the reiterated requests made by the local bishops. Critics suggested that Francis might be holding back out of ideological sympathy for Maduro and his left-wing allies, such as [[Evo Morales]].&lt;ref&gt;{{Cite news|url=https://www.wsj.com/articles/venezuelas-crisis-looms-large-as-pope-visits-latin-america-1504603802|title=Venezuelas Crisis Looms Large as Pope Visits Latin America|last=Kurmanaev|first=Anatoly|date=2017-09-05|work=Wall Street Journal|access-date=2017-09-05|last2=Rocca|first2=Francis X.|language=en-US|issn=0099-9660}}&lt;/ref&gt;

On a theological level, controversy arose after the publication of the apostolic exhortation ''[[Amoris laetitia]]''. Four Cardinals ([[Raymond Leo Burke]], [[Carlo Caffarra]], [[Walter Brandmller]], and [[Joachim Meisner]]) formally asked Pope Francis for clarifications, particularly on the issue of giving communion to divorced and civilly remarried Catholics.&lt;ref&gt;{{Cite news|url=http://www.ncregister.com/daily-news/four-cardinals-formally-ask-pope-for-clarity-on-amoris-laetitia|title=Four Cardinals Formally Ask Pope for Clarity on Amoris Laetitia|work=National Catholic Register|access-date=2018-02-04}}&lt;/ref&gt; They submitted five "dubia" (doubts), and requested a yes or no answer. Francis declined to answera move which British Cardinal [[Vincent Nichols]] characterized as "absolutely right," noting that "to enter into that field is actually to step back from the very thing he wants to help us understand, that we have to respond to people and help them in their journey to God and to do so is not simply to apply a law."&lt;ref&gt;{{Cite news|url=http://www.americamagazine.org/politics-society/2017/03/08/cardinal-nichols-pope-francis-toughness-will-see-catholic-church|title=Cardinal Nichols: Pope Francis' 'toughness' will see the Catholic Church through reforms|last=O'Loughlin|first=Michael|date=8 March 2017|newspaper=America|access-date=8 March 2017|work=|language=en-US|via=}}&lt;/ref&gt;  Strong divergences of interpretation appeared among bishops and cardinals.&lt;ref&gt;{{Cite news|url=https://religionnews.com/2015/09/09/cardinal-burke-attacks-pope-francis-annulment-reforms/|title=Cardinal Burke attacks Pope Francis annulment reforms|work=Religion News Service|access-date=2018-02-04|language=en-US}}&lt;/ref&gt; Some bishops issued guidelines for their diocese insisting that divorced and civilly remarried Catholics remain ineligible for the sacraments of Reconciliation and the Eucharist unless they live in continence, while other bishops opened up the possibility of access to these sacraments.{{Citation needed|date=November 2017}} Cardinal [[Gerhard Ludwig Mller|Gerhard Mller]], prefect of the [[Congregation for the Doctrine of the Faith]], maintained that ''Amoris Laetitia'' should only be interpreted in line with doctrine. Therefore, according to Cardinal Mller, divorced and civilly remarried can have access to the Sacraments of Reconciliation and Communion only if they refrain from sexual relations.&lt;ref&gt;{{Cite news|url=https://cruxnow.com/commentary/2017/06/03/mullers-defense-amoris-laeitia-reads-church-tradition/|title=Mller's defense of 'Amoris Laeitia' reads it in Church tradition|date=3 June 2017|work=Crux|access-date=6 June 2017|language=en-US}}&lt;/ref&gt;{{better source|date=November 2017}} Pope Francis subsequently announced that [[dicastery]] prefects would be appointed for a single five-year term, and replaced Cardinal Mller at the end of his term in 2017 with [[Luis Ladaria Ferrer]].&lt;ref&gt;{{Cite news|url=http://www.catholicherald.co.uk/commentandblogs/2017/07/03/in-removing-cardinal-muller-pope-francis-is-sending-a-powerful-message/|title=The Pope is making clear there is now only one centre of power at the Vatican|date=3 July 2017|work=Catholic Herald|access-date=5 July 2017|language=en-US}}&lt;/ref&gt;{{better source|date=November 2017}}  Cardinal [[Carlo Caffarra]], one of the authors of the dubia, sustains that after ''Amoris laetitia'' "only a blind man could deny there's great confusion, uncertainty and insecurity in the Church."&lt;ref&gt;{{Cite news|url=https://cruxnow.com/global-church/2017/01/14/cardinal-says-blind-man-deny-confusion-caused-pope/|title=Cardinal says 'only blind man' could deny confusion caused by Pope|date=14 January 2017|newspaper=Crux|access-date=4 February 2017|language=en-US}}&lt;/ref&gt;

In February 2017, posters appeared around Rome featuring a stern-looking Pope Francis, complaining about Francis's actions against conservative Catholics, and challenging his reputation for mercy. According to vaticanist Ins San Martn this is "the first time in most Romans' memories that the city has seen posters in major public venues complaining about the policies of a given pope".&lt;ref&gt;{{Cite news|url=https://cruxnow.com/vatican/2017/02/04/rome-wakes-find-city-full-anti-pope-francis-posters/|title=Rome wakes up to find city full of anti-Pope Francis posters|last=San Martn|first=Ins|date=4 February 2017|newspaper=Crux|access-date=4 February 2017|work=|language=en-US|via=}}&lt;/ref&gt;  A week later, the Pope was targeted by a [[fake news]], which spoofed ''[[L'Osservatore Romano]]''.&lt;ref&gt;{{Cite news|url=https://cruxnow.com/vatican/2017/02/10/fake-vatican-newspaper-delivers-new-shot-pope-francis/|title=Fake Vatican newspaper delivers new shot at Pope Francis|last=San Martn|first=Ins|date=10 February 2017|newspaper=Crux|access-date=11 February 2017|work=|language=en-US|via=}}&lt;/ref&gt; In response, the [[Council of Cardinal Advisers]] appointed by the Pope voiced its "full support" to Francis.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.catholicnewsagency.com/news/amid-controversy-council-of-cardinals-backs-pope-francis-71879/|title=Amid controversy, council of cardinals backs Pope Francis|publisher=|accessdate=21 March 2017}}&lt;/ref&gt;  In March 2017, when Cardinal [[Donald Wuerl]] was asked about the Pope's critics, he concluded: "I think, there are just some people who can't bring themselves to move beyond where they are. These look at things through one lens only. But this pontificate and 'Amoris Laetitia' are multifaceted, and if you can only see them through one lens, you're never going to be able to appreciate this."&lt;ref&gt;{{Cite news|url=http://www.americamagazine.org/faith/2017/03/06/cardinal-wuerl-pope-francis-has-reconnected-church-vatican-ii|title=Cardinal Wuerl: Pope Francis has Reconnected the Church with Vatican II|last=O'Connell|first=Gerard|date=6 March 2017|newspaper=America|access-date=6 March 2017|work=|language=en-US|via=}}&lt;/ref&gt;

In July 2017 a group of conservative clergy, academics and laymen signed a document labeled as a "[[Correctio filialis de haeresibus propagatis|Filial Correction]]" of Pope Francis.&lt;ref name="cnn" /&gt; The twenty-five page document, which was made public in September after it received no reply, criticized the Pope for promoting what it described as seven heretical propositions through various words, actions and omissions during his pontificate.&lt;ref name="Correctio filialis de haeresibus propagatis"&gt;{{Cite web |url=https://drive.google.com/file/d/0B5FGuFFkfrDvME5seVJ3TkhrRkU/view |title=Correctio filialis de haeresibus propagatis}}&lt;/ref&gt;  

Capuchin Father [[Thomas Weinandy]], ex-doctrine chief of US Bishops, wrote a letter to Pope Francis on July 31, 2017, which he subsequently made public, in which he charged that Pope Francis is fostering "chronic confusion", "demeaning" the importance of doctrine, appointing bishops who "scandalize" believers with dubious "teaching and pastoral practice", giving prelates who object the impression they will be "marginalized or worse" if they speak out, and causing faithful Catholics to "lose confidence in their supreme shepherd".&lt;ref&gt;{{Cite news|url=https://cruxnow.com/vatican/2017/11/01/ex-bishops-doctrine-chief-says-darkness-coming-light-francis/|title=Ex-bishops doctrine chief says darkness coming to light under Francis|date=2017-11-01|work=Crux|access-date=2017-11-01|language=en-US}}&lt;/ref&gt;  Father Weinandy resigned as a consultant to the Committee on Doctrine of the [[United States Conference of Catholic Bishops]] (USCCB) on the day he publicized the letter, and Cardinal [[Daniel DiNardo]], President of the USCCB, responded with a statement in which he said, {{" '}}every good Christian ought to be more eager to put a good interpretation on a neighbor's statement than to condemn it.' This presupposition should be afforded all the more to the teaching of Our Holy Father."&lt;ref&gt;{{Cite |url=http://www.usccb.org/news/2017/17-203.cfm |title=U.S. Conference Of Catholic Bishops President On Dialogue Within The Church |work=USCCB |access-date=November 27, 2017}}&lt;/ref&gt;

==Teachings==
{{Main article|Theology of Pope Francis}}
{{Social teachings of the popes}}
[[File:Canonization 2014- The Canonization of Saint John XXIII and Saint John Paul II (14036966125).jpg|thumb|upright=0.9|right|Francis during the canonization of [[John XXIII]] and [[John Paul II]] on 27 April 2014]]
Francis told ''[[La Civilt Cattolica]]'' that the church does not need to speak constantly of the issues of abortion, artificial [[contraception]], and homosexuality. He thought that other issues, notably the duty to help those who are poor and marginalized, have been neglected. He added that the church had focused in trivial issues, and as such should not be so prone to condemn, and that priests should be more welcoming. He said the [[confessional]] should be used to motivate people to better themselves.&lt;ref name=Goodstein&gt;{{cite news |url= https://www.nytimes.com/2013/09/20/world/europe/pope-bluntly-faults-churchs-focus-on-gays-and-abortion.html?hp&amp;_r=0|title= Pope Says Church Is 'Obsessed' With Gays, Abortion and Birth Control|first= Laurie|last= Goodstein|date= 19 September 2013|publisher= The New York Times|accessdate=19 February 2015}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref name=BBC19thSept&gt;{{cite news|url=http://www.bbc.co.uk/news/world-europe-24166434 |title=BBC News  Pope Francis: Church too focused on gays and abortion |publisher=BBC News |date=19 September 2013 |accessdate=27 December 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|url=http://www.aljazeera.com/news/europe/2013/09/20139202523642396.html |title=Pope urges more understanding for gays  Europe |publisher=Al Jazeera English |date= 20 December 2013|accessdate=27 December 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|last=Migliaccio |first=Alessandra |url=https://www.bloomberg.com/news/2013-09-19/pope-says-church-should-stop-obsessing-over-gays-abortion.html |title=Pope Says Church Should Stop Obsessing Over Gays, Abortion |publisher=Bloomberg |date=19 September 2013 |accessdate=27 December 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt;

===Mercy===
{{See also|Mercy#Christianity}}Pope Francis said that the most powerful message of Jesus Christ is mercy.&lt;ref name="vatican.va"&gt;{{cite web |author=Pope Francis |url= http://w2.vatican.va/content/francesco/en/homilies/2013/documents/papa-francesco_20130317_omelia-santa-anna.html|title= Holy mass in the parish of St. Anna in the Vatican|date= 17 March 2013|publisher=Holy See |accessdate=19 February 2015}}&lt;/ref&gt; His motto, ''Miserando atque eligendo'', is about Jesus's mercy towards sinners. The phrase is taken from a homily of [[Bede|Saint Bede]], who commented that Jesus "saw [[Matthew the Apostle|the tax collector]] and, because he saw him ''through the eyes of mercy and chose him'', he said to him: 'Follow me{{' "}}.{{efn|Italics added to refer to English translation of the Latin motto}}&lt;ref name="Catholic News Service"/&gt; The motto is a reference to the moment when he found his vocation to the priesthood, at the age of 17. He started a day of student celebrations by going to confession.&lt;ref name="viewonline.fromdoppler.com"&gt;[http://viewonline.fromdoppler.com/pfie/eqaehB/c/a/a El Jesuita. Conversaciones con el cardenal Jorge Bergoglio, SJ.], Sergio Rubn y Francesca Ambrogetti, Vergara editor, pp. 4547. {{webarchive |url=https://web.archive.org/web/20130318045918/http://viewonline.fromdoppler.com/pfie/eqaehB/c/a/a |date=18 March 2013 }}&lt;/ref&gt;

As cardinal he thought Christian morality is not a titanic effort of the will, but a response to the mercy of God. It is not a matter of never falling down but of always getting up again. In this sense, he says Christian morality is a revolution.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.catholicculture.org/news/headlines/index.cfm?storyid=17312|title=The future Pope Francis: additional interviews and writings|work=catholicculture.org}}&lt;/ref&gt; The Gospel reading for the Sunday he was scheduled to give his first public address as pope was on Jesus's [[Jesus and the woman taken in adultery|forgiveness of the adulterous woman]]. This allowed him to discuss the principle that God never wearies of forgiving humans and to stress the importance of never tiring in asking for forgiveness.&lt;ref&gt;[http://www.zenit.org/en/articles/on-forgiveness On Forgiveness], Pope Francis, Vatican City, 17 March 2013.&lt;/ref&gt; Because of this emphasis, many have returned to God and to [[Sacrament of Penance &amp; Reconciliation (Catholic Church)|confession]], a result which has been called the "Pope Francis effect".&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.catholicreview.org/article/faith/vatican-news/pope-francis-top-ten-reasons-to-go-to-confession%7cPope|title=Catholic news from the Archdiocese of Baltimore and around the world|publisher=}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=https://www.catholicvote.org/the-pope-francis-effect-confession-boom-continues/|title=The Pope Francis Effect: Confession Boom Continues|work=CatholicVote.org}}&lt;/ref&gt; However, there seems to be no such effect in counteracting the free fall of vocations, among the Jesuits&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news |last=Reilly |first=Patrick |url=http://www.ncregister.com/blog/reilly/american-jesuits-are-in-a-free-fall-and-the-crisis-is-getting-worse |title=American Jesuits Are in a Free Fall, and the Crisis is Getting Worse |date=28 July 2016 |newspaper=[[National Catholic Register]] |accessdate=16 June 2017}}&lt;/ref&gt; and not only.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web |author=Pope Francis |title=Opening of the works of the 71st General Assembly of the Italian Episcopal Conference (C.E.I.) in the presence of the Holy Father, 20.05.2018 |url=http://webcache.googleusercontent.com/search?q=cache:qtAdP1uvpzAJ:press.vatican.va/content/salastampa/en/bollettino/pubblico/2018/05/20/180522d.html+%22The+first+thing+that+troubles+me+is+the+crisis+of+vocations.+And+it+is+our+paternity+that+is+at+stake+here%22%22this+concern,+rather,+this+haemorrhage+of+vocations%22 |work=vatican.va |location=New Synod Hall |date=20 May 2018 |accessdate=23 May 2018 |quote=The first thing that troubles me is the ''crisis of vocations''. And it is our paternity that is at stake here....this concern, rather, this haemorrhage of vocations.}}&lt;/ref&gt;

In March 2015, Pope Francis announced that the universal church would celebrate a Jubilee Year from 8 December 2015 to 20 November 2016, dedicated to the theme of God's mercy. The Vatican announced the pope would perform several acts to demonstrate the theme of God's mercy.&lt;ref&gt;[http://www.news.va/en/news/pope-francis-homily-with-announcement-of-year-of-m Pope Francis: homily with announcement of Year of Mercy]. Official Vatican Network (13 March 2015). Retrieved on 8 May 2015.&lt;/ref&gt;

Vatican spokesperson [[Greg Burke (journalist)|Greg Burke]] has said the Pope's emphasis on mercy applied to even those who are guilty of heinous crimes. One example is the case of Father Mauro Inzoli an Italian priest.
