The Inzoli case is one of several where Pope Francis overruled the recommendation of the Vaticans Congregation for the Doctrine of the Faith (CDF) reducing a sentence calling for him to be laicized.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.catholicherald.co.uk/news/2017/02/27/pope-reduces-sanctions-against-some-paedophile-priests/|title=Pope reduces sanctions against some paedophile priests|work=Catholic Herald}}&lt;/ref&gt;

In March 2018, Francis was quoted in ''[[la Repubblica]]'' as saying (in Italian) "Those who repent obtain Gods forgiveness and take their place among the ranks of those who contemplate him, but those who do not repent and cannot be forgiven disappear. A hell doesnt exist, the disappearance of sinning souls exists. The Vatican quickly called this a reconstruction by [[Eugenio Scalfari]] rather than a faithful transcription of Francis' words.&lt;ref&gt;[https://www.theguardian.com/world/2018/mar/30/vatican-scrambles-to-clarify-popes-denial-that-hell-exists "Vatican scrambles after pope appears to deny existence of hell", by Angela Giufridda, ''The Guardian'']&lt;/ref&gt; Scalfari later said he believed the Pope denied the existence of hell, but admitted he did not take notes during their chat, and may have misremembered Francis' words, having made mistakes about him before.&lt;ref&gt;[https://www.nytimes.com/2018/03/30/world/europe/pope-francis-hell-scalfari.html "Does Hell Exist? And Did the Pope Give an Answer?", by Jason Horowitz, ''The New York Times'']&lt;/ref&gt;

===Faith and evangelization===
{{See also|Evangelism}}

Pope Francis's first encyclical, "''Lumen Fidei''", was on faith and his first apostolic exhortation, "''Evangelii Gaudium''", was on the new evangelization. In both his first [[homily]] as pope and in his first address to the cardinals, Francis talked about walking in the presence of Jesus Christ and stressed the church's mission to announce him. In the audience with the cardinals, he emphasized the concept of "encounter with Jesus":
{{quote|Stimulated by the Year of Faith, all together, pastors and faithful, we will make an effort to respond faithfully to the eternal mission: to bring Jesus Christ to humanity, and to lead humanity to an encounter with Jesus Christ: the Way, the Truth, and the Life, truly present in the Church and, at the same time, in every person. This encounter makes us become new men in the mystery of [[Actual grace|Grace]], provoking in our hearts the Christian joy that is a hundredfold that given us by Christ to those who welcome Him into their lives.&lt;ref name="Greets"&gt;[http://www.news.va/en/news/pope-francis-greets-cardinal-full-text Pope Francis greets Cardinals: Full text], Vatican Today 15 March 2013.&lt;/ref&gt;}}

In his homily, he stressed that "if we do not profess Jesus Christ, things go wrong. We may become a charitable [[Non-governmental organization|NGO]], but not the Church, the [[Bride of Christ|Bride of the Lord]]." He went on to teach that "When we do not profess Jesus Christ, we profess the worldliness of the devil... when we profess Christ without the Cross, we are not disciples of the Lord, we are worldly".&lt;ref&gt;[http://www.vatican.va/holy_father/francesco/homilies/2013/documents/papa-francesco_20130314_omelia-cardinali_en.html "Missa Pro Ecclesia" With The Cardinal Electors: Homily Of The Holy Father Pope Francis] Vatican website, 14 March 2013&lt;/ref&gt; The theme of rejecting "spiritual worldliness", described as a [[leitmotif]] of his teachings even before he became pope,&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.catholicculture.org/commentary/otn.cfm?id=975 |title=The early signs are clear. Pope Francis is a reformer |publisher=Catholicculture.org |date=15 March 2013 |accessdate=19 March 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt; was emphasized in his first apostolic exhortation. Understanding this worldliness as "putting oneself at the center", he said that it is the "greatest danger for the Church, for us, who are in the Church".&lt;ref&gt;[http://www.catholicculture.org/news/headlines/index.cfm?storyid=17308 "The future Pope Francis on apostolic courage and the danger of 'spiritual worldliness'"], ''Catholic Culture'', 14 March 2013.&lt;/ref&gt;

On the other hand, in October 2013, during a notable interview with the founder of ''[[la Repubblica]]'' newspaper [[Eugenio Scalfari]], Francis said: "I believe in God, not in a Catholic God, there is no Catholic God", and "[[Proselytism]] is solemn nonsense, it makes no sense. We need to get to know each other, listen to each other and improve our knowledge of the world around us".&lt;ref name="Scalfari"&gt;{{cite news |last=Scalfari |first=Eugenio |authorlink=Eugenio Scalfari |title=The Pope: how the Church will change |url=http://www.repubblica.it/cultura/2013/10/01/news/pope_s_conversation_with_scalfari_english-67643118/ |newspaper=[[la Repubblica]] |date=1 October 2013 |accessdate=22 June 2017}}&lt;/ref&gt;

===Environment===
[[File:John Zizioulas presents the encyclical Laudato si' at the press conference in Rome.webm|thumb| [[John Zizioulas]], [[w:Eastern Orthodoxy|Eastern Orthodox]] [[Metropolitan bishop|metropolitan]] of [[Bergama|Pergamon]], presents the encyclical ''Laudato si{{'}}'' at the [[b:Development Cooperation Handbook/Interviews/Press Conference Presentation Laudato si'|Press conference]] in Rome.]]
{{See also|Christian views on environmentalism}}After his election Francis said, "Here too, it helps me to think of the name of Francis [of Assisi], who teaches us profound respect for the whole of creation and the protection of our [[Natural environment|environment]], which all too often, instead of using for the good, we exploit greedily, to one another's detriment.".&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url= http://www.rtcc.org/2014/05/08/un-to-back-pope-francis-statement-on-human-ecology/|title= UN to back Pope Francis statement on "human ecology"|first= Sophie|last= Yeo|date= 8 May 2014|publisher= Responding to Climate Change|accessdate= 15 May 2015|deadurl= yes|archiveurl= https://web.archive.org/web/20150507172037/http://www.rtcc.org/2014/05/08/un-to-back-pope-francis-statement-on-human-ecology/|archivedate= 7 May 2015|df= dmy-all}}&lt;/ref&gt; At the [[University of Molise]] he described [[Environmental quality|environmental]] concerns as a great contemporary challenge and voiced opposition to [[deforestation]]. He believes that development should respect what Christians see as creation, and that exploiting the earth is sinful.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web |url= https://www.theatlantic.com/international/archive/2014/07/pope-franciss-radical-rethinking-of-environmentalism/374300/|title= Pope Francis's Radical Environmentalism|author= Tara Isabella Burton|date= 11 July 2014|magazine= [[The Atlantic]]|accessdate=28 May 2015}}&lt;/ref&gt; Francis told the Second International Conference on Nutrition, held in Rome by the [[Food and Agriculture Organization]],&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web |url= http://www.fao.org/news/story/en/item/178668/icode/|title= Pope Francis: Starvation in a world of plenty "scandalous"|date= 20 June 2013|publisher= Food and Agriculture Organization of the United Nations|accessdate=28 May 2015}}&lt;/ref&gt; that a lack of protection for the ecology may generate problems.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news |url= https://www.independent.co.uk/news/world/europe/pope-francis-says-greed-will-destroy-the-world-9875913.html|title= Pope Francis says greed will 'destroy the world'|author= Zachary Davies Boren|date= 21 November 2014|newspaper= [[The Independent]]|accessdate=11 February 2015|location=London}}&lt;/ref&gt; Francis plans a meeting with leaders of main religions to increase awareness of the state of the climate.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news |url= https://www.independent.co.uk/news/people/pope-francis-to-issue-climate-change-call-to-arms-for-worlds-catholics-in-measures-that-will-anger-vatican-conservatives-9947357.html|title= Pope Francis to issue climate change call to arms for world's Catholics in measures that will anger Vatican conservatives|first= Adam|last= Withnall|date= 28 December 2014|newspaper= [[The Independent]]|accessdate=28 May 2015|location=London}}&lt;/ref&gt;

On 18 June 2015, Pope Francis issued a [[papal encyclical]] called ''[[Laudato si']]'' on [[climate change]], care for the environment, and sustainable development.&lt;ref name="Jim Yardley and Laurie Goodstein"/&gt; The encyclical, although dated 24 May 2015,&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web |title=Francis: Encyclicals |url=http://w2.vatican.va/content/francesco/en/encyclicals/index.html#encyclicals |publisher=Holy See |accessdate=18 June 2015}}&lt;/ref&gt; was officially made public on 18 June 2015. The encyclical sets apart the basic human needs and appetites. Francis considers that the former are small and non-negotiable, and that the latter are potentially unlimited. Although he asks for the use of [[renewable energy]] instead of conventional fuels, he thinks that it would not be enough unless society turns down the unlimited appetites of consumerism.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web |url= https://www.theguardian.com/commentisfree/2015/jun/18/guardian-view-on-laudato-si-pope-francis-cultural-revolution|title= The Guardian view on Laudato Si': Pope Francis calls for a cultural revolution|date= 18 June 2015|publisher= The Guardian|accessdate=27 July 2015}}&lt;/ref&gt; This project was opposed by Vatican conservatives, Catholic conservatives, and the US evangelical movement.&lt;ref name="climate"&gt;{{cite web |url= https://www.theguardian.com/world/2014/dec/27/pope-francis-edict-climate-change-us-rightwing|title= Pope Francis's edict on climate change will anger deniers and US churches|first= John|last= Vidal|date= 27 December 2014|newspaper=[[The Guardian]]|accessdate=11 February 2015}}&lt;/ref&gt; In the encyclical, Francis states "The Earth, our home, is beginning to look like an immense pile of filth."&lt;ref&gt;[https://www.theguardian.com/commentisfree/2015/jun/18/pope-francis-encyclical-extract Pope Francis: The Earth, our home, is beginning to look like an immense pile of filth]. ''The Guardian.'' 18 June 2015.&lt;/ref&gt;

As he prepared for the encyclical, Francis sponsored a [[Pontifical Academy of Sciences]] summit meeting in April 2015 that focused on the relationships connecting poverty, economic development, and climate change. The meeting included presentations and discussions by scientists, religious leaders, and economists. The [[United Nations]] secretary general, [[Ban Ki-moon]], who is urging world leaders to approve a climate-change accord in Paris at the [[2015 United Nations Climate Change Conference]] in December, delivered the keynote address.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news |title=Vatican official calls for moral awakening on global warming |first=Stephanie|last=Kirchgaessner |url=https://www.theguardian.com/environment/2015/apr/28/vatican-climate-change-summit-to-highlight-moral-duty-for-action |newspaper=[[The Guardian]] |date=28 April 2015 |accessdate=18 June 2015}}&lt;/ref&gt;

===Poverty===
[[File:Pope Francis at Vargihna.jpg|thumb|upright=1.25|Pope Francis visits a [[favela]] in Brazil during [[World Youth Day 2013]]]]
{{See also|Christian views on poverty and wealth}}
While he has said that the greatest poverty is "the lack of Christ,"&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.catholicnewsagency.com/news/lack-of-christ-the-greatest-poverty-pope-tells-movement/|title=Lack of Christ the 'greatest poverty,' Pope tells movement|publisher=|accessdate=21 March 2017}}&lt;/ref&gt; and the "only one real kind of poverty" is "not living as children of God and brothers and sisters in Christ",&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://w2.vatican.va/content/francesco/en/messages/lent/documents/papa-francesco_20131226_messaggio-quaresima2014.html|title=Lent 2014: He became poor, so that by his poverty you might become rich (cf. 2 Cor 8:9) - Francis|publisher=Holy See |accessdate=21 March 2017}}&lt;/ref&gt; Francis has also been very outspoken against material poverty. At a meeting of Latin American bishops in 2007, Bergoglio said that, despite the economic growth, poverty had not been reduced in the continent, and asked for a better [[income distribution]].&lt;ref name=AllenPap/&gt; On 30 September 2009, Bergoglio spoke at a conference organized by the [[Universidad del Salvador|Argentina City Postgraduate School (EPOCA)]] at the [[Alvear Palace Hotel]] in which he quoted the 1992 "Documento de Santo Domingo"&lt;ref&gt;{{cite conference |url=http://www.celam.org/conferencias/Documento_Conclusivo_Santo_Domingo.pdf |title=Documento de Santo Domingo |author=Latin American Episcopal Conference |year=1992 |conference=Cuarta Conferencia General del Episcopado Latinoamericano |conferenceurl=http://www.celam.org/ |booktitle=Nueva evangelizacin, promocin humana, cultura cristiana : documento de consulta : IV Conferencia General del Episcopado Latinoamericano, Santo Domingo, Repblica Dominicana, 1992, Conclusiones |publisher=CELAM |location=Bogot |format=PDF |oclc=29289158 |accessdate=9 March 2013 |language=Spanish |trans-title=Santo Domingo Document }}&lt;/ref&gt; by the [[Latin American Episcopal Conference]], saying "[[extreme poverty]] and unjust economic structures that cause great [[economic inequality|inequalities]]" are violations of [[human rights]].&lt;ref&gt;{{cite book |last1=Bergoglio |first1=Jorge Mario |title=Seminario : las deudas sociales de nuestro tiempo : la deuda social segn la doctrina de la iglesia |trans-title=Seminar : social debts of our time : the social debt according to the doctrine of the church |type=presented seminar |series=Posgrado internacional del bicentenario. Polticas pblicas, soluciones para la crisis de nuestro tiempo. |date=30 September 2009 |publisher=EPOCA-USAL |location=Buenos Aires |language=Spanish |isbn= |oclc=665073169}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web |url=http://www.lanacion.com.ar/1181036-bergoglio-los-derechos-humanos-tambien-se-violan-con-la-pobreza |title=Bergoglio: "Los derechos humanos tambin se violan con la pobreza" |last1=Rouillon |first1=Jorge |date=1 October 2009 |work=[[La Nacin]] |language=Spanish |trans-title=Bergoglio: "Human rights are also violated in poverty" |accessdate=9 March 2013 |quote=Cit a los obispos latinoamericanos que en 1992 dijeron que "los derechos humanos se violan no slo por el terrorismo, la represin, los asesinatos, sino tambin por condiciones de extrema pobreza y estructuras econmicas injustas que originan grandes desigualdades".}}&lt;/ref&gt; He went on to describe social debt as "immoral, unjust, and illegitimate".&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|title=Extreme poverty is also a violation of human rights, says Argentinean cardinal |url=http://www.catholicnewsagency.com/news/extreme_poverty_is_also_a_violation_of_human_rights_says_argentinean_cardinal/ |agency=Catholic News Agency|accessdate=13 March 2013|date=1 October 2009}}&lt;/ref&gt;

During a 48-hour public servant strike in Buenos Aires, Argentina, Bergoglio criticized unequal treatment of the judiciary to poor and rich people.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|title=Argentines protest against pay cuts|url=http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/americas/1481313.stm|accessdate=13 March 2013|date=8 August 2001|work=BBC News}}&lt;/ref&gt; In 2002, during [[19982002 Argentine great depression|an economic crisis]], Bergoglio harshly criticized those in power, saying, "[l]et's not tolerate the sad spectacle of those who no longer know how to lie and contradict themselves to hold onto their privileges, their rapaciousness, and their ill-earned wealth".&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|title=Argentina's pope stood up to power, but has his critics|url=https://www.reuters.com/article/2013/03/14/us-pope-bergoglio-idUSBRE92D16J20130314|work=Reuters|accessdate=15 March 2013|first1=Helen |last1=Popper|last2=Karina |first2=Grazina|date=14 March 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt; During a May 2010 Mass celebrated by twenty bishops commemorating the [[Argentina Bicentennial]] in front of the [[Basilica of Our Lady of Lujn|basilica of Lujn]], an important Catholic institution and destination of pilgrimage, Bergoglio criticized the reduced social concern over poverty and exhorted Catholics to ask the [[Our Lady of Lujn|Virgin of Lujn]] to "take care of our motherland, particularly those who are most forgotten".&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.lanacion.com.ar/1262602-bergoglio-critico-a-los-que-no-tienen-en-cuenta-a-los-mas-pobres |title=Bergoglio critic a "los que no tienen en cuenta a los ms pobres" |publisher=La Nacin |accessdate=13 March 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt; In line with the [[Catholic Church and AIDS|Catholic Church's efforts to care for AIDS victims]], in 2001 he visited a hospice where he washed and kissed the feet of twelve AIDS patients.&lt;ref name=AllenPap&gt;{{cite news|last=Allen, Jr.|first=John L.|title=Profile: New pope, Jesuit Bergoglio, was runner-up in 2005 conclave|url=http://ncronline.org/blogs/ncr-today/papabile-day-men-who-could-be-pope-13|accessdate=13 March 2013|publisher=National Catholic Reporter|date=3 March 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt; As Pope Francis he spoke out over the [[2013 Savar building collapse#Worldwide criticism|collapse of ''Rana Plaza'' garment factory]] in April 2013, which killed over a thousand people, and condemned the low pay workers received.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web |url= https://www.theguardian.com/world/2013/may/01/bangladesh-factory-pope-slave-labour|title= Bangladesh factory collapse: pope condemns 'slave labour' conditions|date= 1 May 2013|publisher= The Guardian|accessdate=28 May 2015}}&lt;/ref&gt;

Pope Francis urged world leaders to prevent excessive monetary ambitions, which he said had become similar to an [[idolatry]] of money, and urged them to provide more welfare aid.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|url=http://www.bbc.co.uk/news/world-europe-22551125 |title=Pope Francis hits out at global 'cult of money' |publisher= BBC News |date=16 May 2013 |accessdate=23 June 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt; Dealing with the [[Great Recession]], the pope criticized unbridled capitalism, considering that it judged human beings purely by their ability to consume goods and made people miserable.&lt;ref&gt;Squires, Nick (18 May 2013). [http://www.theage.com.au/world/pope-blames-tyranny-of-capitalism-for-making-people-miserable-20130517-2jru9.html#ixzz2TZDGtjRA Pope blames tyranny of capitalism for making people miserable]. ''[[The Age]].'' Retrieved 18 May 2013.&lt;/ref&gt; He said that social inequality and increasing [[poverty]] is caused by [[neoliberalism]],&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web |url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2013/mar/14/new-pope-francis-in-his-own-words|title=Pope Francis  in his own words|author=&lt;!--Not stated--&gt; |date=14 March 2013 |website=[[The Guardian]] |publisher= |access-date=4 June 2017 |quote="The socioeconomic crisis and the resulting increase in poverty has its origins in policies inspired by forms of neoliberalism that consider profit and the laws of the market as absolute parameters above the dignity of people or of peoples."}}&lt;/ref&gt; and preferred economic systems with a higher intervention by the state.&lt;ref name= LizzyDavies&gt;{{cite news|author=Lizzy Davies in Rome |url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2013/may/17/pope-francis-attacks-cult-money |title=Pope Francis attacks 'cult of money' in reform call |publisher=The Guardian |date=17 May 2013 |accessdate=23 June 2013 |location=London}}&lt;/ref&gt; During a May 2014 meeting with U.N. Secretary General [[Ban Ki-moon]], Francis called on the United Nations to encourage a better income distribution.&lt;ref&gt;Philip Pullella (9 May 2014). [https://www.reuters.com/article/2014/05/09/us-pope-un-idUSKBN0DP0WU20140509 U.N. should encourage redistribution of wealth, pope says]. ''[[Reuters]].'' Retrieved 10 May 2014.&lt;/ref&gt; In 2015, he declared that the poor and downtrodden of the world should have "sacred rights" of labor, lodging, and land, and denounced the [[austerity]] imposed by global financial institutions, referring to it as the "new colonialism".&lt;ref&gt;[https://www.theguardian.com/world/2015/jul/10/poor-must-change-new-colonialism-of-economic-order-says-pope-francis Unbridled capitalism is the 'dung of the devil', says Pope Francis]. ''The Guardian'', 9 July 2015.&lt;/ref&gt;

Pope Francis deplores [[modern slavery]] and, together with a diverse group of leaders from other religions, he signed a declaration promising to inspire action worldwide in an effort to eliminate slavery by 2020. Both Pope Francis and the declaration described slavery as a [[crime against humanity]].&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news |url= http://edition.cnn.com/2014/12/02/world/europe/pope-modern-day-slavery/|title= Pope Francis: Modern slavery is 'becoming worse and worse every day'|first= Mick|last= Krever|date= 2 December 2014|publisher= CNN|accessdate=28 May 2015}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news |url= http://www.smh.com.au/world/australian-grace-forrest-inspires-pope-francis-and-other-world-religious-leaders-to-sign-pledge-to-eradicate-slavery-by-2020-20141202-11ytpw.html|title= Australian Grace Forrest inspires Pope Francis and other world religious leaders to sign pledge to eradicate slavery by 2020|first= Nick|last= Miller|date= 3 December 2014|publisher= The Sydney Morning Herald|accessdate=28 May 2015}}&lt;/ref&gt; During his new year mass in 2015 Francis pressed people from all cultures and religions to combat human trafficking and modern slavery according to their responsibilities. Francis said all human beings are brothers and sisters and all have a right to be free.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web |url= http://www.abc.net.au/news/2015-01-02/pope-francis-urges-people-to-fight-modern-slavery/5996584|title= Pope Francis urges people to unite to fight modern slavery and seek peace in first mass of 2015|date= 1 January 2015|publisher= ABC|accessdate=28 May 2015}}&lt;/ref&gt;

Chancellor of Germany [[Angela Merkel]] consulted Francis on 18 May 2013, and later the same day called for more stringent controls of [[financial market]]s.&lt;ref name="huffingtonpost.com"&gt;{{cite news |url= http://uk.reuters.com/article/2013/05/18/uk-pope-personal-idUKBRE94H0CS20130518|title= Church must help the poorest, not dissect theology, pope says|first= Philip|last= Pullella|date= 18 May 2013|publisher= Reuters|accessdate=28 May 2015}}&lt;/ref&gt; Francis has referred many times to the [[Eurozone crisis]] that affect [[Greek government-debt crisis|Greece]] and Catholic Southern European nations.&lt;ref name="NYT52513"/&gt; Nevertheless, Pope Francis considers that starvation and homeless people are bigger problems than the financial crises.&lt;ref name="huffingtonpost.com"/&gt; [[George Haley]] of [[New Haven University]] said that Francis thinks that capitalism should reduce income disparity, and proposed that he used the diplomatic influence of the Vatican to suggest changes in national economies.&lt;ref name="cnbc.com"/&gt; Rohit Arora is concerned that Francis has not come up with any specific way to solve income inequality and believes if the pope is serious he should do so. Joseph Pastore believes the wealth of the Catholic Church prevents Francis from taking a polarizing position and is unsure how far Francis can reform the Church.&lt;ref name="cnbc.com"&gt;{{cite news|first=Mark|last=Koba |url=https://www.cnbc.com/id/100931792 |title=A blunt Pope Francis targets free market economics |publisher=CNBC |date=6 August 2013 |accessdate=27 December 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt;

Pope Francis denounced the "autonomy of the marketplace" and "financial speculation" as tyranny in his 84-page [[apostolic exhortation]] ''[[Evangelii gaudium]]:''

{{quote|Just as the commandment "Thou shalt not kill" sets a clear limit in order to safeguard the value of human life, today we also have to say "thou shalt not" to an economy of exclusion and inequality. Such an economy kills.&amp;nbsp;... A new tyranny is thus born, invisible and often virtual, which unilaterally and relentlessly imposes its own laws and rules. To all this we can add widespread corruption and self-serving tax evasion, which has taken on worldwide dimensions. The thirst for power and possessions knows no limits.&lt;ref&gt;Joshua Holland (26 November 2013). [http://billmoyers.com/2013/11/26/pope-francis-calls-unfettered-capitalism-tyranny/ Pope Francis Calls Unfettered Capitalism 'Tyranny']. ''[[Moyers &amp; Company]].'' Retrieved 26 November 2013.&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;[http://rt.com/news/pope-francis-capitalism-tyranny-324/ 'Not to share wealth with poor is to steal': Pope slams capitalism as 'new tyranny']. ''[[RT (TV network)|RT]],'' 26 November 2013.&lt;/ref&gt;}}

Pope Francis's views were called [[Marxist]] by [[Rush Limbaugh]] and other conservatives as a result of his critique of capitalism with absolute market autonomy.&lt;ref name="marxno"/&gt; Pope Francis responded that "Marxist ideology is wrong. But I have met many Marxists in my life who are good people, so I don't feel offended  there is nothing in the exhortation that cannot be found in the social doctrine of the church."&lt;ref name="marxno"&gt;{{cite web |url= https://www.theguardian.com/world/2013/dec/15/pope-francis-defends-criticism-of-capitalism-not-marxist|title= Pope says he is not a Marxist, but defends criticism of capitalism|first= Lizzy|last= Davies |date= 15 December 2013|publisher= The Guardian|accessdate=28 May 2015}}&lt;/ref&gt; He later postulated that the Communists "stole" the flag of Christianity as "the flag of the poor is Christian. Poverty is at the center of the Gospel."&lt;ref&gt;[http://rt.com/news/169272-pope-francis-communism-christianity/ Pope Francis: Communists 'stole' the flag of Christianity]. ''[[RT (TV network)|RT]],'' 30 June 2014.&lt;/ref&gt;

===Liberation theology===
{{See also|Liberation theology}}Francis opposed the Marxist versions of liberation theology followed by the "'progressive' group of [Jesuit] theologians living out in base communities".&lt;ref&gt;{{Citation | last = Ivereigh| first = Austen | author-link = Austen Ivereigh | publication-date = 2014 | title = The Great Reformer: Francis and the Making of a Radical Pope | edition = Kindle | publisher = Henry Holt and Co. | publication-place = New York | at = locations 18871888 | isbn = 978-1-62779-158-8 }}&lt;/ref&gt; As he wrote in the preface to a book on the Catholic Church in Latin America, ''Una apuesta por Amrica Latina'' (A Commitment to Latin America) by [[Guzmn Carriquiry Lecour]], the proponents of liberation theology were unable to reformulate it after the collapse of Marxism, and it thus became an anachronism.&lt;ref name = Gregg&gt;{{Citation | last = Gregg | first = Samuel | title = Pope Francis and Liberation Theology | publisher = National Review | date = 28 May 2013 | url = http://www.nationalreview.com/corner/349432/pope-francis-and-liberation-theology |dead-url=yes |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20130603101516/http://www.nationalreview.com/corner/349432/pope-francis-and-liberation-theology |archive-date=3 June 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref name=Surprises&gt;{{Citation | title = Pope Francis, the Pope of Surprises | journal = Personal Update | issue = 126 | publisher = Family &amp; Life | location = Dublin | date = 2 June 2013 | url = http://www.prolife.ie/personal-update-issue-description/pope-francis-pope-surprises | deadurl = yes | archiveurl = https://web.archive.org/web/20150528200640/http://www.prolife.ie/personal-update-issue-description/pope-francis-pope-surprises | archivedate = 28 May 2015 | df = dmy-all }}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|last = Phillips | first = Francis | url=http://www.catholicherald.co.uk/commentandblogs/2013/06/14/pope-francis-was-all-too-familiar-with-liberation-theology-thats-why-he-opposed-it/|title=Pope Francis was all too familiar with Liberation Theology. That's why he opposed it | publisher =  Catholic Herald | date =  14 June 2013 |accessdate=4 October 2014}}&lt;/ref&gt; His theologian of reference was [[Juan Carlos Scannone]], a fellow Jesuit who had developed a theology centered on the "religious devotion of the common people".&lt;ref name = Gregg/&gt;&lt;ref name = Surprises/&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://chiesa.espresso.repubblica.it/articolo/1350519?eng=y |title=Bergoglio, a Revolutionary His Own Way |language=it |publisher=Chiesa |date=16 May 2013 |accessdate=23 June 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt; [[File:VISITA PAPA FRANCISCO I (19473235041).jpg|thumb|Thousands welcomed Francis in [[Guayaquil]], [[Ecuador]], 6 July 2015]]
Historian Roberto Bosca at the [[Austral University (Argentina)|Austral University]] in Buenos Aires says that Pope Francis supported liberation theology's preferential option for the poor, although "in a nonideological fashion".&lt;ref name = Gregg/&gt;&lt;ref name=Allen2013&gt;{{cite web|last=Allen|first=John L., Jr.|title=Hard questions about Francis in Argentina and a lesson from Chile|url=http://ncronline.org/blogs/all-things-catholic/hard-questions-about-francis-argentina-and-lesson-chile|work=National Catholic Reporter|date=12 April 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt; Before becoming Pope, Cardinal Bergoglio described liberation theology's preferential option for the poor as part of a long Christian tradition rooted in the Gospels.&lt;ref&gt;Transcript of 2010 judicial inquiry, "[http://www.abuelas.org.ar/material/documentos/BERGOGLIO2.pdf Bergoglio Declara ante el TOF N&lt;sup&gt;o&lt;/sup&gt; 5] {{webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20130611191146/http://www.abuelas.org.ar/material/documentos/BERGOGLIO2.pdf |date=11 June 2013 }}," translated in {{Citation | last = Ivereigh| first = Austen | author-link = Austen Ivereigh | publication-date = 2014 | title = The Great Reformer: Francis and the Making of a Radical Pope | edition = Kindle | publisher = Henry Holt and Co. | publication-place = New York | at = locations 18971903 | isbn = 978-1-62779-158-8 | quote = The option for the poor comes from the first centuries of Christianity. It's the Gospel itself. If you were to read one of the sermons of the first [[Church Fathers|fathers of the Church]], from the second or third centuries, about how you should treat the poor, you'd say it was [[Maoism|Maoist]] or [[Trotskyism|Trotskyist]]. The Church has always had the honor of this preferential option for the poor. At the Second Vatican Council the Church was redefined as the People of God and this idea really took off at the Second Conference of the Latin-American bishops in Medelln.}}&lt;/ref&gt; Bergoglio's opposition focused on the [[Montoneros]], a terrorist group similar to the European [[Red Brigades]] that caused nearly 6,000 deaths. Montoneros claimed that they ascribed to liberation theology, and sought support from the Church. Bosca considers that Bergoglio's opposition to the liberation theology "wasn't opposition to liberation theology in itself or the option for the poor", but opposition to the possible official Catholic support to the Montoneros.&lt;ref name=Allen2013/&gt;

Despite his caution about elements of liberation theology, Francis met with [[Gustavo Gutirrez]], who is usually regarded as its founder. Gutirrez had co-authored a book with [[Gerhard Ludwig Mller]], prefect of the [[Congregation for the Doctrine of the Faith]]. The Vatican's semiofficial newspaper ''[[L'Osservatore Romano]]'' said at the time that the liberation theology should not continue to be ignored.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news |url= https://www.washingtonpost.com/national/on-faith/liberation-theology-finds-new-welcome-in-pope-francis-vatican/2013/09/09/5265002e-198a-11e3-80ac-96205cacb45a_story.html|title= Liberation theology finds new welcome in Pope Francis' Vatican|first= Alessandro|last= Speciale|date= 9 September 2013|publisher= The Washington Post|accessdate=11 February 2015}}&lt;/ref&gt;

Pope Francis's beatification of [[Roman Catholic Archdiocese of San Salvador#Archbishops|Archbishop of San Salvador]] [[scar Romero]], who was assassinated in March 1980 as he said mass, as a martyr to the church is seen as Francis's strong support for the poor and those who defend that stance.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news |url= http://www.latimes.com/world/mexico-americas/la-fg-pope-direction-20150528-story.html#page=1|title= Romero beatification signals Pope Francis' plan for Catholic Church|first= Tracy|last= Wilkinson|date= 28 May 2015|publisher= Los Angeles Times|accessdate=28 May 2015}}&lt;/ref&gt;

===Abortion===
{{See also|Catholic Church and abortion}}
Throughout his papacy, Pope Francis has been a vocal opponent of both the practice and legality of abortion. In May 2013, Francis unexpectedly participated in Italy's [[pro-life]] march in Rome, asking its participants to protect human life "from the moment of conception".&lt;ref name="fivemyths"/&gt; Also, as the mostly Catholic country of Ireland was preparing legislation to legalize abortion, Francis sent a message to the Irish asking them to protect the lives of both the unborn and vulnerable people.&lt;ref name="fivemyths"&gt;{{cite web|last=Doino Jr. |first=William |url=http://www.firstthings.com/onthesquare/2013/07/five-myths-about-pope-francis/william-doino-jr|title=Five Myths About Pope Francis |publisher=First Things |date=22 July 2013 |accessdate=3 November 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt; Also in May 2013, during a Wednesday audience Francis officially blessed the pro-life march in [[Szczecin]], Poland, one of Europe's largest pro-life events and, speaking in Italian, encouraged the Poles to defend the unborn. He maintained that human life should be respected all the way from conception to natural death.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://wpolityce.pl/wydarzenia/53620-papiez-pozdrowil-organizatorow-marszu-dla-zycia-ze-szczecina-niech-ta-inicjatywa-przypomina-wszystkim-o-potrzebie-szacunku-dla-zycia|title=Papie pozdrowi organizatorw Marszu dla ycia ze Szczecina. "Niech ta inicjatywa przypomina wszystkim o potrzebie szacunku dla ycia"s |publisher=Wpolityce |date=15 May 2013 |accessdate=3 November 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt;

At a September 2013 meeting with Catholic gynecologists, Francis condemned abortion saying that: "Every child that isn't born, but is unjustly condemned to be aborted, has the face of Jesus Christ, has the face of the Lord."&lt;ref name="abortion"&gt;{{cite news|url=http://www.cbsnews.com/8301-202_162-57603897/pope-francis-denounces-abortion-after-decrying-churchs-focus-on-rules/|title=Pope Francis denounces abortion after decrying church's focus on rules |publisher=CBS News |date=20 September 2013 |accessdate=3 November 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt; He advised the gynecologists to invoke the [[Conscience clause (medical)|conscience clause]] to refuse to perform abortions, if so requested.&lt;ref name="abortion"/&gt;

Francis also thought, as a Cardinal, that the church should support those women who carry on with their pregnancy despite being [[single parent]]s, rejecting the option to abort. He maintained that, in those cases, priests should not refuse to [[Baptism|baptize]] those children.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|publisher=ABC News|title=Francis Becomes First Latin American Pope
|url=http://abcnews.go.com/International/francis-latin-american-pope/story?id=18722276|first=Russell|last=Goldman|date=13 March 2013|accessdate=16 February 2015}}&lt;/ref&gt; During a [[Baptism of the Lord]] Mass in the [[Sistine Chapel]], Pope Francis baptised the baby of a couple in a [[civil marriage]].&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|last1=Kington|first1=Tom|title=Let them drink milk: Pope encourages mums to breastfeed in Sistine Chapel|url=https://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/worldnews/the-pope/10566752/Let-them-drink-milk-Pope-encourages-mums-to-breastfeed-in-Sistine-Chapel.html|accessdate=14 February 2017|work=[[The Daily Telegraph]]|date=12 January 2014}}&lt;/ref&gt;

During the [[Extraordinary Jubilee of Mercy]], Francis "grant to all priests, in virtue of their ministry, the faculty to absolve those who have committed the sin of procured abortion", a provision which he extended indefinitely in his Apostolic Letter ''Misericordia et Misera'' issued on 20 November 2016.&lt;ref&gt;[http://w2.vatican.va/content/francesco/en/apost_letters/documents/papa-francesco-lettera-ap_20161120_misericordia-et-misera.html Misericordia et Misera], paragraph 12, published 20 November 2016, accessed 20 April 2017&lt;/ref&gt; Francis appealed to all priests to grant forgiveness to women who had undergone an abortion, as well as anyone who had been involved in completing the procedure. While Francis reiterated that the sin of abortion (an act punishable with automatic excommunication) is "a grave sin", he affirmed that "there is no sin that God's mercy cannot reach and wipe away when it finds a repentant heart."&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|last1=Povoledo|first1=Elisabetta|last2=Stack|first2=Liam|title=Pope Francis Extends Priests' Ability to Forgive Abortion|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2016/11/21/world/europe/pope-francis-abortion-priests.html?_r=0|accessdate=3 March 2017|work=[[The New York Times]]|date=21 November 2016}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref name="auto"&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.cnn.com/2016/11/21/europe/pope-francis-absolve-abortion/index.html|title=Pope extends power to forgive abortion|first1=Tim |last1=Hume|first2=Cristiana |last2=Moisescu|first3=Daniel |last3=Burke|publisher=CNN}}&lt;/ref&gt;

Kate D'Annunzio, of [[Rachel's Vineyard]], a [[pro-life]] group which ministers to women who have experienced abortions, said that Francis had clarified that priests have the ability to both forgive abortions and welcome women back into the church, stating; "The Church has had the ability to forgive these women, but many of these women had difficulty forgiving themselves. This outreach by the Pope is saying 'Don't isolate yourselves, come back to the church.'"&lt;ref name="auto"/&gt; Jon O'Brien, the president of U.S. [[pro-choice]] Catholic dissident advocacy group [[Catholics for Choice]], praised the pope's effort, and said "it showed that Francis understood the deep chasm that exists between ordinary Catholics {{en dash}} who turn to abortion and birth control with the same frequency as people of other faiths {{en dash}} and their clergy."&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|last1=Kirchgaessner|first1=Stephanie|title=Pope Francis cements priests' power to forgive abortion|url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2016/nov/21/pope-francis-makes-priests-ability-to-absolve-abortion-permanent-church-forgiveness-sin|accessdate=3 March 2017|work=[[The Guardian]]|date=21 November 2016}}&lt;/ref&gt;

===Ordination of women===
{{See also|Catholic Church doctrine on the ordination of women}}
Francis has often spoken about the importance of [[women in the Catholic Church]]. He considers that they have a special role in spreading the faith to their children and grandchildren. He also considers that, although the [[Resurrection appearances of Jesus|first witnesses]] of the [[resurrection of Jesus]] were women, their significance was ignored because in [[Jewish law]], only males are [[credible witness]]es.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|title=Pope Francis stresses "fundamental importance" of women in Catholic Church|url=http://uk.reuters.com/article/2013/04/03/uk-pope-women-idUKBRE9320L120130403 |accessdate=21 April 2013|publisher=Reuters |last=O'Leary|first=Naomi|date=3 April 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|last=Fox|first=Thomas C.|title=Francis talks about women and the faith|url=http://ncronline.org/blogs/ncr-today/francis-talks-about-women-and-faith|accessdate=21 April 2013|publisher=[[National Catholic Reporter]]|date=3 April 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt;

Francis has addressed the subject of the [[ordination of women]] a number of times.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|title=Audience: The fundamental role of women in the Church|url=http://en.radiovaticana.va/news/2013/04/03/audience:_the_fundamental_role_of_women_in_the_church_/en1-679206|accessdate=21 April 2013|publisher=[[Vatican Radio]]|date=3 April 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt; Francis has ruled out the possibility of female priests, stating that this has been the longtime stance of the Church, and that "[[Pope John Paul II|John Paul II]] made the Church's stance [[Ordinatio Sacerdotalis|definitive]]. The door is closed."&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web |url= http://www.sydneycatholic.org/news/latest_news/2013/2013731_119.shtml|title= Pope Francis Talks to Press About Benedict XVI, Vatican Bank and 'Gay Lobby'|date= 13 July 2013|publisher= Catholic Communications, [[Sydney Archdiocese]]|accessdate=11 February 2015}}&lt;/ref&gt; Francis ruled out female cardinals in December 2013.&lt;ref name="CSN16/12/2013"&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.cnsnews.com/news/article/barbara-boland/pope-francis-there-will-be-no-women-cardinals|title=Pope Francis: There Will Be No Women Cardinals|work=[[CNS News]]|accessdate=4 October 2014}}&lt;/ref&gt;

On the other hand, Francis has been noncommittal about whether women should lead more in administration and pastoral activities.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2014/jun/29/pope-francis-woman-from-rib-avoids-pledge-reform-catholic-church|title=Pope Francis jokes 'woman was from a rib' as he avoids vow to reform church|first=John|last=Hooper|work=the Guardian|accessdate=4 October 2014}}&lt;/ref&gt;

Erin Saiz Hanna of the [[Women's Ordination Conference]] has accused Francis of a [[selective use of evidence]]. She mentioned that the [[Pontifical Biblical Commission]] had once concluded that there were no scriptural or theological problems with ordaining women, and cited the attitude of Jesus towards women and their leadership in the [[Early Christianity|early church]]. She also suggested that his rejection to the ordination of women may be at odds with his tolerance of [[gay priests]], mentioned in the same interview.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web |url= http://www.womensordination.org/content/view/453/42/ |archiveurl= https://web.archive.org/web/20130807183208/http://www.womensordination.org/content/view/453/42/ |archivedate= 7 August 2013|title= Pope Francis slams door on women's ordination|author= Erin Saiz Hanna|date= 29 July 2013|publisher= Women's Ordination Conference|accessdate=31 May 2015}}&lt;/ref&gt;

===Clergy===
[[File:Saludo en el Vaticano.JPG|thumb|Bishop Gabriel Barba and Pope Francis]]
Francis has criticized the perceived hunger for power of some sectors of the curia, which come at the expense of a proper religious life. He thinks that gossip is a danger to the reputation of people, and that the presence of cliques within organizations is a threat to both the individual and the organization.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web |url= http://www.salon.com/2014/12/22/pope_francis_slams_vatican_clergy_suffers_from_spiritual_alzheimers/|title= Pope Francis slams Vatican: Clergy suffers from "spiritual Alzheimer's"|first= Joanna|last= Rothkopf|date= 22 December 2014|publisher= Salon|accessdate=16 February 2015}}&lt;/ref&gt; Francis thinks that priests should be in contact with the people as much as possible and avoid isolation. He also suggests that priests should encourage people to be optimistic.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web |url= http://www.thecatholictelegraph.com/pope-francis-priests-should-be-shepherds-living-with-the-smell-of-the-sheep/13439|title= Pope Francis: Priests should be 'shepherds living with the smell of the sheep'|first= Carol|last= Glatz|date= |publisher= The Catholic Telegraph|accessdate=16 February 2015}}&lt;/ref&gt; He has been supported by Rome bishops, priests, deacons, and seminarians from the English-speaking world who attended the second international conference of the Confraternities of Catholic Clergy.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web |url= http://en.radiovaticana.va/news/2015/01/14/priests_answer_the_popes_call_to_evangelisation/1118154|title= International Clergy Conference participants commit themselves to Pope Francis' call to evangelisation|date= 14 January 2015|publisher= Vatican Radio|accessdate=16 February 2015}}&lt;/ref&gt;

In September 2013, Pope Francis approved the excommunication of Australian priest Greg Reynolds, the first during Francis's papacy. Reynolds was accused of heresy and sacrilegious treatment of the consecrated host. His public preaching contradicting church teaching was also referenced in the letter of excommunication. A letter sent by the Archbishop of Melbourne, [[Denis Hart]], to the priests of his diocese cited Reynolds's support for the ordination of women and "his public celebration of the Eucharist when he did not hold faculties to act publicly as a priest". Reynolds said that his support of [[same-sex marriage]] was also a factor, though not mentioned.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|last=Allen |first=John L. |url=http://ncronline.org/news/global/australian-priest-advocate-womens-ordination-excommunicated |title=Australian priest, advocate for women's ordination excommunicated |publisher=National Catholic Reporter  |date=10 August 2012 |accessdate=27 December 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt;

In response to the [[Catholic Church sexual abuse cases]], Francis created the [[Pontifical Commission for the Protection of Minors]]. In the past, priests who committed abuses were removed by bishops, but bishops were rarely held accountable. This tribunal was created to prevent cover-ups of abuse cases; offenders would be dealt with by the [[Congregation for the Doctrine of the Faith]].&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news |url= https://www.washingtonpost.com/news/acts-of-faith/wp/2015/06/10/pope-francis-approves-a-new-process-for-governing-bishop-accountability-in-abuse-cases/|title= Pope Francis approves new tribunal to judge bishops accused of covering up sex abuse|author1=Michelle Boorstein  |author2=Abby Ohlheiser |lastauthoramp=yes |date= 10 June 2015|publisher= The Washington Post|accessdate=12 August 2015}}&lt;/ref&gt; Barbara Blaine, president of the organization [[Survivors Network of those Abused by Priests]], considered that it may not be effective.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news |url= https://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/worldnews/europe/italy/11665254/Pope-Francis-creates-Vatican-tribunal-to-judge-bishops-accused-of-covering-up-sex-abuse.html|title= Pope Francis creates Vatican tribunal to judge bishops accused of covering up sex abuse|first= Nick|last= Squires|date= 10 June 2015|publisher= The Telegraph|accessdate=12 August 2015|location=London}}&lt;/ref&gt;

====Priestly celibacy====
As a cardinal, Bergoglio's views regarding the [[Clerical celibacy (Catholic Church)|celibacy of priests]] were recorded in the book ''[[On Heaven and Earth]]'', a record of conversations conducted with [[Abraham Skorka]], a Buenos Aires rabbi and rector of the [[Latin American Rabbinical Seminary]].&lt;ref name="gibson"&gt;Gibson, David, [https://www.usatoday.com/story/news/world/2013/03/20/pope-francis-celibacy-sex-abuse/2004151/ "Book reveals new pope's views on celibacy, abuse, crisis"], USA Today (from Religion News Service), 20 March 2013, Retrieved 21 March 2013&lt;/ref&gt; He says that celibacy is a matter of discipline rather than faith, and that tradition and experience would advise to keep it.&lt;ref name="celibacy"&gt;Connor, Tracy, [http://worldnews.nbcnews.com/_news/2013/03/20/17386717-pope-francis-spoke-of-being-dazzled-by-girl-possible-change-of-celibacy-rule?lite "Pope Francis spoke of being 'dazzled' by girl, possible change of celibacy rule"], NBC News, 21 March 2013, Retrieved 21 March 2013&lt;/ref&gt; He noted that the Byzantine, Ukrainian, Russian, and Greek Catholic Churches allow married men to be ordained priests, but not bishops.&lt;ref name="celibacy"/&gt;{{efn|Both in the [[Eastern Catholic Churches]] and in the [[Eastern Orthodox Churches]], married men can be ordained to the priesthood, but priests cannot marry after having been ordained. See [http://www.vatican.va/holy_father/john_paul_ii/apost_constitutions/documents/hf_jp-ii_apc_19901018_codex-can-eccl-orient-2_lt.html#TITULUS_XVI Code of Canons of the Eastern Churches, canon 795]}} He said that many of those in Western Catholicism who are pushing for more discussion about the issue do so from a position of pragmatism, based on a loss of manpower.&lt;ref name="celibacy"/&gt; He states that "If, hypothetically, Western Catholicism were to review the issue of celibacy, I think it would do so for cultural reasons (as in the East), not so much as a universal option."&lt;ref name="celibacy"/&gt; He emphasized that, in the meantime, the rule must be strictly adhered to, and any priest who cannot obey it should leave the ministry.&lt;ref name="celibacy"/&gt; The ''National Catholic Reporter's'' Vatican analyst, [[Thomas J. Reese]], also a Jesuit, praised Bergoglio's use of conditional language.&lt;ref name="gibson"/&gt; He said that phrases like "for the moment" and "for now" are "not the kind of qualifications one normally hears when bishops and cardinals discuss celibacy."&lt;ref name="gibson"/&gt;

===Contraception and family planning===
The initial reports that Francis considered that the use of methods intended for contraception with the purpose of preventing disease might be permissible&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|last=Rice-Oxley|first=Mark|title=Pope Francis: the humble pontiff with practical approach to poverty |url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2013/mar/13/jorge-mario-bergoglio-pope-poverty|accessdate=15 April 2013|publisher=The Guardian (UK)|date=13 March 2013|location=London}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|last=Feiden|first=Douglas|title=Pope Francis, the new leader of the Catholic Church, praised by many for practicing what he preaches, his humble nature and his empathy for the poor |url=http://www.nydailynews.com/news/world/popebio-article-1.1287994|accessdate=15 April 2013|publisher=New York Daily News |date=13 March 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt; were disputed by others who said he was "unwaveringly orthodox on matters of sexual morality".&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|last=Allen, Jr.|first=John L.|title=New pope, Jesuit Bergoglio, was runner-up in 2005 conclave |url=http://ncronline.org/blogs/ncr-today/papabile-day-men-who-could-be-pope-13|accessdate=15 April 2013|publisher=National Catholic Reporter|date=3 March 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt; Before becoming Pope he opposed the free distribution of contraceptives when it was introduced by the Kirchner government.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|title=Argentina's Bergoglio becomes Pope Francis |url=http://news.blogs.cnn.com/2013/03/13/cardinals-elect-new-pope/|accessdate=15 April 2013|publisher=CNN|date=13 March 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt; Francis emphasized that [[contraception]] involves "destruction of the family through the privation of children."&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://w2.vatican.va/content/francesco/es/speeches/2015/january/documents/papa-francesco_20150116_srilanka-filippine-incontro-famiglie.html|title=Sri Lanka  Filipinas: Encuentro con las familias en el Mall of Asia Arena (Manila, 16 de enero de 2015) |author=Pope Francis |date=|publisher=Holy See |accessdate=29 October 2016}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web |url= http://opinion.inquirer.net/82016/the-popes-most-insistent-message|title= Pope's most insistent message|date= 26 January 2015|publisher= Philippine Daily Inquirer|accessdate=17 August 2016}}&lt;/ref&gt;  At the same time, Francis teaches that "responsible parenthood" is important, and suggested to have about three children in a family, and added that Christians do not need to breed in excess.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web |url= http://www.bbc.com/news/world-asia-30890989|title= Pope Francis: No Catholic need to breed like 'rabbits'|date= 19 January 2015|publisher= BBC News|accessdate=31 May 2015}}&lt;/ref&gt;

Francis encourages [[natural family planning]] such as avoiding [[sexual intercourse]] when the woman is fertile.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news |url= https://www.reuters.com/article/2015/01/19/us-pope-airplane-idUSKBN0KS1WY20150119|title= Pope says birth control ban doesn't mean breed 'like rabbits'|first= Philip|last= Pullella|date= 19 January 2015|publisher= Reuters|accessdate=1 June 2015}}&lt;/ref&gt;

===LGBT issues===
{{See also|Homosexuality and the Catholic Church}}
As bishop and Pope, Francis restated the [[Homosexuality and the Catholic Church|Church's principle]]: that homosexual practice is intrinsically immoral, but that every homosexual person deserves respect and love.&lt;ref name=inflight&gt;{{cite news | url=http://www.bbc.co.uk/news/world-europe-23489702 | title=Pope Francis: Who am I to judge gay people? | publisher=BBC | date=29 July 2013 | accessdate=4 August 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web |url=http://www.catholic.org/hf/faith/story.php?id=50111 |title=NEW POPE: Who is this man named Bergoglio? |publisher=Catholic Online |accessdate=13 March 2013 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20130317025209/http://www.catholic.org/hf/faith/story.php?id=50111 |archivedate=17 March 2013 |df=dmy-all }}&lt;/ref&gt; He opposes [[same-sex marriage]], including the 2010 [[Same-sex marriage in Argentina|bill to introduce it in Argentina]].&lt;ref name=pentin&gt;{{cite news|last=Pentin|first=Edward|title=Cardinal Bergoglio Hits Out at Same-Sex Marriage|url=http://www.ncregister.com/blog/edward-pentin/cardinal_bergoglio_hits_out_at_same-sex_marriage|accessdate=14 March 2013|publisher=National Catholic Register|date=8 July 2010}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref name=cbc20130318&gt;{{cite news |title=Clashing Pope Francis, Argentine president meet in Vatican |url=http://www.cbc.ca/news/canada/sudbury/story/2013/03/18/wrd-pope-francis-meets-argentine-president.html|accessdate=18 March 2013|publisher=CBC News|date=18 March 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt; In July 2010, while the law was under consideration, he wrote a letter to Argentina's cloistered nuns in which he said the Argentine [[nuclear family]] could be seriously harmed. He thought that children would face discrimination and lose the development that a father and mother give.&lt;ref name=pentin/&gt;&lt;ref name=feder&gt;{{cite news|last=Feder|first=J. Lester|title=Pope Francis Brings Lessons of Argentina's Marriage Fight To Rome|url=https://www.buzzfeed.com/lesterfeder/pope-francis-brings-lessons-of-argentinas-marriage-fight-to|accessdate=14 March 2013|publisher=Buzzfeed|date=13 March 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web |url=http://worldnews.nbcnews.com/_news/2013/03/13/17299920-meet-the-new-pope-francis-is-humble-leader-who-takes-the-bus-to-work?lite|title=Meet the new pope: Francis is humble leader who takes the bus to work|first=Erin|last=McClam|work=[[NBC News]]|date=13 March 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt;
{{quote|Let's not be nave: This is not a simple political fight; it is a destructive proposal to God's plan. This is not a mere legislative proposal (that's just its form), but a move by the father of lies that seeks to confuse and deceive the children of God&amp;nbsp;... Let's look to St. Joseph, Mary, and the Child to ask fervently that they defend the Argentine family in this moment... May they support, defend, and accompany us in this war of God.}}
After ''[[L'Osservatore Romano]]'' reported this, several priests expressed their support for the law and one was defrocked.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|title=El cura suspendido: "A la Iglesia le preocupa ms la cama de los argentinos que su mesa|language=Spanish|url=http://www.perfil.com/contenidos/2010/07/13/noticia_0011.html|accessdate=19 March 2013|publisher=Perfil|date=13 July 2010|deadurl=yes|archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20130518112007/http://www.perfil.com/contenidos/2010/07/13/noticia_0011.html|archivedate=18 May 2013|df=dmy-all}}&lt;/ref&gt; Observers believe that the church's opposition and Bergoglio's language worked in favor of the law's passage and that in response, Catholic officials adopted a more conciliatory tone in later debates on social issues such as parental [[surrogacy]].&lt;ref&gt;{{sp}}{{cite news|last=De Vedia|first=Mariano|title=La carta de Bergoglio, un error estratgico|url=http://www.lanacion.com.ar/1285258-la-carta-de-bergoglio-un-error-estrategico|accessdate=14 March 2013|date=16 July 2010|language=Spanish}}&lt;/ref&gt;

Rubin, Bergoglio's biographer, said that while taking a strong stand against same-sex marriage, Bergoglio raised the possibility in 2010 with his bishops in Argentina that they support the idea of [[civil union]]s as a compromise position.&lt;ref name=pragmatist&gt;{{cite news |last1=Romero |first1=Simon |last2=Schmall|first2=Emily|title=On Gay Unions, a Pragmatist Before He Was a Pope |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2013/03/20/world/americas/pope-francis-old-colleagues-recall-pragmatic-streak.html|accessdate=27 March 2013|publisher=New York Times|date=19 March 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt; According to one news report by ''The New York Times'', a majority of the bishops voted to overrule him.&lt;ref name="pragmatist"/&gt; Miguel Woites, the director of the Catholic News Agency of Argentina, denied that Bergoglio ever made such a proposal,&lt;ref name="Catholic News Agency"&gt;{{cite news|title=Claims that Pope supported gay civil unions disputed |url=http://www.catholicnewsagency.com/news/claims-that-pope-supported-gay-civil-unions-disputed/|accessdate=4 April 2013|publisher=Catholic News Agency|date=22 March 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt; but additional sources, including two Argentine journalists and two senior officials of the Argentine bishops conference, supported Rubin's account.&lt;ref name=hardquestions&gt;{{cite news|last=Allen, Jr.|first=John L.|title=Hard questions about Francis in Argentina and a lesson from Chile|url=http://ncronline.org/blogs/all-things-catholic/hard-questions-about-francis-argentina-and-lesson-chile|accessdate=12 April 2013|publisher=National Catholic Reporter|date=12 April 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt;

In an interview on 28 July 2013, when discussing homosexuals (both in general and their place in the clergy) and answering a question as to whether there was a "gay lobby" in the Vatican, the pontiff said, "If someone is gay and is searching for the Lord and has good will, then who am I to judge him? The Catechism of the Catholic Church explains this in a beautiful way, saying...: 'no one should marginalize these people for this, they must be integrated into society'."&lt;ref name="Pope Full declerations"&gt;{{cite web |url= https://w2.vatican.va/content/francesco/en/speeches/2013/july/documents/papa-francesco_20130728_gmg-conferenza-stampa.html|title= Press Conference of Pope Francis during the return flight|date= 28 July 2013 |publisher=Holy See |accessdate=3 June 2015}}&lt;/ref&gt; According to two [[gay right]]s activists, Marcelo Mrquez and Andrs Albertsen, Bergoglio expressed support for the spiritual needs of "homosexual people" and willingness to support "measured actions" on their behalf in private conversations with them.&lt;ref name="closed doors"&gt;Romo, Rafael, and Rodriguez, Jose Manuel, [http://www.cnn.com/2013/03/20/world/americas/argentina-pope-civil-unions "Behind closed doors, pope supported civil unions in Argentina, activist says"], CNN, 21 March 2013, Retrieved 27 March 2013.&lt;/ref&gt; These remarks have been seen as an encouraging change of tone from the papacy, so much so that the American [[LGBT]] magazine ''[[The Advocate]]'' named Pope Francis their Person of the Year for 2013.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|title=The Advocate's Person of the Year 2013|url=http://www.advocate.com/year-review/2013/12/16/advocates-person-year-pope-francis|publisher=The Advocate Magazine|first=Lucas|last=Grindley|date=16 December 2013|accessdate=3 June 2015}}&lt;/ref&gt;

On 5 January 2014, the Vatican denied that the Pontiff supports [[gay union]]s.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|last=Pullella |first=Philip |url=http://worldnews.nbcnews.com/_news/2014/01/05/22188840-vatican-denies-pope-is-open-to-recognition-of-gay-civil-unions |title=Vatican denies pope is open to recognition of gay civil unions  World News |publisher=NBC News |date=5 January 2014 |accessdate=24 May 2014}}&lt;/ref&gt; In response to various Italian [[tabloid journalism|tabloid]] articles released in the media, Vatican spokesman Father [[Federico Lombardi]] cited that various media misinterpretations are "paradoxical" and manipulative in misusing Pope Francis's words noted in response to children growing up in non-traditional families.&lt;ref name=latimes.com&gt;{{cite news|last=Kington|first=Tom|title=Vatican says pope's comments on gay couples don't mark policy change|url=http://www.latimes.com/world/worldnow/la-fg-wn-vatican-pope-francis-gay-couples-20140105,0,1567038.story#axzz2pbK7AwFg|publisher=Los Angeles Times|date=5 January 2014}}&lt;/ref&gt; ''The New York Times'' considers that Bergoglio may have supported gay unions in Argentina only as a negotiated compromise, but that his context as a Pope is very different.&lt;ref name="pragmatist"/&gt; In 2015, Pope Francis declared that "the family is threatened by growing efforts on the part of some to redefine the very institution of marriage" and suggested that same-sex marriage "disfigures God's plan for creation".&lt;ref name="Ben Tufft"&gt;{{cite news|url=https://www.independent.co.uk/news/people/news/pope-francis-warns-that-samesex-marriage-threatens-the-family-and-disfigures-gods-plan-for-creation-9986028.html|title=Pope Francis warns that same-sex marriage 'threatens the family' and 'disfigures God's plan for creation'|date=18 January 2015|first=Ben|last=Tufft|work=The Independent|location=London}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref name="Michele Richinick"&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.msnbc.com/msnbc/pope-francis-suggests-gay-marriage-threatens-traditional-families|title=Pope Francis suggests gay marriage threatens traditional families|work=MSNBC|first=Michele|last=Richinick|date=16 January 2015}}&lt;/ref&gt; The Pontiff supported the [[Slovak same-sex marriage referendum, 2015|Slovak referendum]] on banning gay marriage and gay adoption in an address to St. Peter's Square, stating: "I wish to express my appreciation to the entire Slovak church, encouraging everyone to continue their efforts in defense of the family, the vital cell of society."&lt;ref name="J Lester Feder"&gt;{{cite web|title=Pope Endorses Referendum Denying Marriage And Adoption Rights To Same-Sex Couples|url=https://www.buzzfeed.com/lesterfeder/pope-endorses-referendum-denying-marriage-and-adoption-right|author=J Lester Feder|work=Buzzfeed}}&lt;br/&gt;As quoted by {{cite web|url=http://www.advocate.com/politics/religion/2015/02/05/pope-has-kind-words-backers-anti-equality-measures-slovakia|title=Pope Has Kind Words for Backers of Anti-Equality Measures in Slovakia|first=Trudy|last=Ring|date=5 February 2015|work=The Advocate}}&lt;/ref&gt;  In October 2015, priest and Vatican theologian Priest [[Krzysztof Charamsa]] was stripped of his posts after announcing he was homosexual and denouncing the Church for "persecuting" and causing "immeasurable suffering" to homosexuals.&lt;ref&gt;Wyatt, Caroline ''Gay priest decries 'inhuman' treatment of homosexual Catholics'', 23 October 2015; http://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-34654581&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;Philipson, ALice ''Church Makes Life Hell For Homosexuals Says Priest'', The Telegraph 28 October 2015; https://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/worldnews/europe/vaticancityandholysee/11960356/Church-makes-life-hell-for-homosexuals-says-priest.html&lt;/ref&gt;

On 2 October 2016, Pope Francis spoke in favor of pastoral care for and including [[transgender]] Catholics in the church, stating priests should "accompany them spiritually" and that they should never be turned away, even if they have undergone [[gender transition]] and [[sex reassignment surgery|sex-reassignment operations]].&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.catholicnews.com/services/englishnews/2016/gay-transgender-people-deserve-pastoral-care-pope-says.cfm|title=Gay &amp; Transgender People Deserve Pastoral Care, Pope Says|author=Cindy Wooden|date=2 October 2016|work=[[Catholic News Service]]|accessdate=9 January 2017}}&lt;/ref&gt; He spoke out against "Gender Theory", that is the concept that [[gender identity]] is not definite and can change, being taught in schools and referred to it as "ideological colonization" and said it was one of the threats against traditional marriage and is destructive to children.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/news/acts-of-faith/wp/2016/10/02/pope-francis-urges-pastoral-care-for-gay-transgender-people-draws-line-between-ministry-and-indoctrination/|title=Pope Francis Urges Pastoral Care For Gay &amp; Transgender People, Draws Line Between Ministry and Indoctrination|author=Nicole Winfield|date=2 October 2016|work=[[The Washington Post]]|accessdate=9 January 2017}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|url=http://www.cnn.com/2016/10/02/world/pope-transgender-comments/|title=Pope warns of 'ideological colonization' in transgender teachings|author=John Newsome|date=4 October 2016|work=[[CNN]]|accessdate=9 January 2017}}&lt;/ref&gt; [[New Ways Ministry]] and [[DignityUSA]], two LGBT Catholic Advocacy groups, both spoke out against Pope Francis's statements regarding gender identity, calling it "dangerous ignorance" of the issue.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2016/08/04/world/europe/pope-francis-remarks-disappoint-gay-and-transgender-groups.html|title=Pope Francis Remarks Disappoint Gay and Transgender Groups|author=Mike McPhate|date=3 August 2016|work=[[The New York Times]]|accessdate=9 January 2017}}&lt;/ref&gt;

Francis once held an audience with a Spanish transgender man, who had transitioned from female to male, and his wife.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.advocate.com/religion/2016/10/03/pope-francis-says-jesus-would-not-abandon-transgender-people|title=Pope Francis Says Jesus Would Not Abandon Transgender People|date=3 October 2016|work=[[The Advocate]]|accessdate=9 January 2017}}&lt;/ref&gt;

In April 2018 Pope Francis met with Juan Carlos Cruz, a survivor of [[Karadima case|sexual abuse by Chilean priest Fernando Karadima]].&lt;ref&gt;https://www.cbsnews.com/news/pope-francis-tells-gay-man-god-made-you-like-this/&lt;/ref&gt; Cruz discussed with Francis in detail how his sexual orientation was used by Latin American media and news outlets to discredit his report of abuse and label him as a pervert and liar.&lt;ref&gt;https://www.advocate.com/religion/2018/5/20/pope-gay-man-god-made-you&lt;/ref&gt; In a private conversation between the two Francis reportedly said to Cruz, whom identifies as homosexual, in regards to his sexuality, "You know Juan Carlos, that does not matter. God made you like this. God loves you like this. The Pope loves you like this and you should love yourself and not worry about what people say."&lt;ref&gt;https://www.cnn.com/2018/05/21/europe/pope-francis-gay-comments-intl/index.html?utm_source=twCNN&amp;utm_term=image&amp;utm_content=2018-05-21T09%3A41%3A21&amp;utm_medium=social&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;https://www.theguardian.com/world/2018/may/20/pope-juan-carlos-cruz&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;https://www.teenvogue.com/story/pope-francis-reportedly-told-a-gay-man-god-made-you-like-this&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;https://www.americamagazine.org/faith/2018/05/21/lgbt-community-cheers-pope-francis-god-made-you-remark&lt;/ref&gt;

===Religious persecution===
Francis condemned persecution of religious minorities in [[Iraq]] including [[Persecution of Christians by ISIL|some Christian victims]]. He did not mention the [[Islamic State of Iraq and the Levant]] specifically but is believed to have referred to it. Francis mentioned children dying of hunger and thirst, kidnapped women, massacres, and violence of all kinds. In the opinion of Francis war and hatred cannot be carried out in the name of God. Francis thanked brave people bringing aid to those driven from their homes. He confidently expects an effective solution to stop those crimes and return the area to the [[rule of law]]&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web |url= https://www.theguardian.com/world/2014/aug/10/pope-francis-iraq-isis-islamic-state-religious-minorities-violence|title= Pope Francis: Isis violence against minorities in Iraq must be stopped|first= John|last= Hooper|date= 10 August 2014|publisher= ''[[The Guardian]]''|archiveurl= https://web.archive.org/web/20150719192628/http://www.theguardian.com/world/2014/aug/10/pope-francis-iraq-isis-islamic-state-religious-minorities-violence|archivedate= 19 July 2015|deadurl= no|accessdate= 3 June 2015}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|url=https://www.usatoday.com/story/news/world/2014/08/10/pope-iraq/13860361/ |title=Pope condemns religious persecution in Iraq |first=Katharine |last=Lackey |date=10 August 2014 |publisher=''[[USA Today]]'' |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6aNBKiiqD?url=http://www.usatoday.com/story/news/world/2014/08/10/pope-iraq/13860361/ |archivedate=29 July 2015 |deadurl=no |accessdate=3 June 2015 |df= }}&lt;/ref&gt; and, in a break with Vatican tradition, supports the use of force to stop Islamic militants from attacking religious minorities in Iraq.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web |url= http://www.businessinsider.com/pope-francis-endorses-use-of-force-against-isis-in-iraq-2014-8?IR=T|title= Pope Francis Endorses Use Of Force Against ISIS In Iraq|first= Nicole|last= Winfield|date= 18 August 2014|publisher= ''[[Business Insider]]''|archiveurl= https://web.archive.org/web/20140822013237/http://www.businessinsider.com/pope-francis-endorses-use-of-force-against-isis-in-iraq-2014-8?IR=T|archivedate= 22 August 2014|deadurl= no|accessdate= 3 June 2015}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news |url= http://www.nydailynews.com/news/world/pope-supports-force-islamic-extremists-article-1.1907547|title= Pope Francis supports use of force to stop Islamic extremists from attacking religious minorities in Iraq|first= Joel|last= Siegel|date= 19 August 2014|publisher= ''[[Daily News (New York)|Daily News]]''|archiveurl= https://web.archive.org/web/20150316210708/http://www.nydailynews.com/news/world/pope-supports-force-islamic-extremists-article-1.1907547|archivedate= 16 March 2015|deadurl= no|accessdate= 3 June 2015}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web |url= http://www.ibtimes.com/pope-endorses-use-force-us-airstrikes-stop-isis-amid-plans-visit-iraq-1661732|title= Pope Endorses Use Of Force, US Airstrikes To Stop ISIS Amid Plans To Visit Iraq|first= Rebecka|last= Schumann|date= 18 August 2014|publisher= ''[[International Business Times]]''|archiveurl= https://web.archive.org/web/20140827092539/http://www.ibtimes.com/pope-endorses-use-force-us-airstrikes-stop-isis-amid-plans-visit-iraq-1661732|archivedate= 27 August 2014|deadurl= no|accessdate=3 June 2015}}&lt;/ref&gt;

On 9 April 2017 following the [[2017 Palm Sunday church bombings]] at the [[Saint Mark's Coptic Orthodox Cathedral (Alexandria)|Cathedral of St. Mark]] in [[Alexandria]] and the Church of St. George in [[Tanta]], killing at least 40 people and injuring dozens more, Pope Francis said "We pray for the victims of the attack carried out today, this morning, in Cairo, in a Coptic church." He expressed his "deep condolences" for Coptic Orthodox Christians and for Egypt and called [[Pope Tawadros II]], who had escaped the attack, his "brother".&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2017/04/09/world/middleeast/explosion-egypt-coptic-christian-church.html|title=Egypt Declares State of Emergency, as Attacks Undercut Promise of Security|first1=Magdy|last1=Samaan|first2=Declan|last2=Walsh|date=9 April 2017|publisher=|via=NYTimes.com}}&lt;/ref&gt;

===Capital punishment and life imprisonment===
Pope Francis proposed the abolition of both [[capital punishment]] and [[life imprisonment]] in a meeting with representatives of the [[International Association of Penal Law]]. He thinks that states should find another way to protect people from aggression, and includes deaths caused by [[police brutality]] and [[extrajudicial punishment]]. He affirmed that the Church accepts it when there are no other options to protect the people, but considers that nowadays such cases may be minimal or even nonexistent. He also thinks that life imprisonment, recently removed from the Vatican penal code, is just a variation of the death penalty.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url= http://www.catholicnews.com/data/stories/cns/1404377.htm|archive-url= https://archive.is/20141024002736/http://www.catholicnews.com/data/stories/cns/1404377.htm|dead-url= yes|archive-date= 24 October 2014|title= Pope Francis calls for abolishing death penalty and life imprisonment|author= Francis X. Rocca|date= 23 October 2014|publisher= Catholic News Service|accessdate= 19 February 2015}}&lt;/ref&gt;

===Ecumenism with other Christians===
In October 2013, during the above-mentioned interview with Eugenio Scalfari, Francis said: "I believe in God, not in a Catholic God, there is no Catholic God".&lt;ref name="Scalfari"/&gt; In another interview with ''[[La Stampa]]'', Pope Francis emphasized his commitment to [[ecumenism]], stating: "For me, ecumenism is a priority. Today, we have the ecumenism of blood. In some countries they kill Christians because they [[cross necklace|wear a cross]] or have a Bible, and before killing them they don't ask if they're Anglicans, Lutherans, Catholics or Orthodox. The blood is mixed."&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://vaticaninsider.lastampa.it/en/the-vatican/detail/articolo/francesco-francisco-francis-ecumenismo-ecumenism-31594/|title=Pope Francis' ecumenism  Vatican Insider|last=Tornielli|first=Andrea|date=28 January 2014|publisher=[[Vatican Insider]]|accessdate=27 September 2015}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|url=https://www.economist.com/blogs/erasmus/2015/02/pope-francis-and-copts|title=Blood and ecumenism|last=C|first=B|date=17 February 2015|publisher=The Economist|accessdate=27 September 2015}}&lt;/ref&gt; During the [[Week of Prayer for Christian Unity]], Pope Francis addressed the attendees of the ''John 17 Movement'' gathering opining that "[[Schism|Division]] is the work of the [[Devil in Christianity|Father of Lies]]" and that he "knows that Christians are disciples of Christ: that they are one, that they are brothers! He doesn't care if they are Evangelicals, or Orthodox, Lutherans, Catholics or Apostolic... he doesn't care! They are Christians. And that blood (of martyrdom) unites. Today, dear brothers and sisters, we are living an 'ecumenism of blood'. This must encourage us to do what we are doing today: to pray, to dialogue together, to shorten the distance between us, to strengthen our bonds of brotherhood."&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.catholicherald.co.uk/news/2015/05/25/the-devil-knows-christians-are-one-says-pope-francis/|title=The devil knows Christians are one, says Pope Francis|last=Wooden|first=Cindy|date=25 May 2015|publisher=[[The Catholic Herald]]|accessdate=27 September 2015}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://en.radiovaticana.va/news/2015/05/24/pope_sends_greetings_for_us_christian_unity_event/1146375|title=Pope sends greetings for US Christian Unity event Vatican Radio|date=24 May 2015|publisher=[[Vatican Radio ]]|accessdate=27 September 2015}}&lt;/ref&gt; During the 2016 [[Octave of Christian Unity]], Pope Francis "asked forgiveness for the way Catholics had treated other Christian believers over the years, and also invited Catholics to pardon those who had persecuted them."&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.japantimes.co.jp/news/2016/01/26/world/social-issues-world/pope-asks-non-catholic-christians-forgiveness-irks-call-common-prayer/#.VqlUEiorKhf|title=500 years after Reformation, pope knocks on Lutherans' door|date=26 January 2016|publisher=[[The Japan Times]]|accessdate=27 January 2016|quote=At a service Monday in Rome, Francis asked forgiveness for the way Catholics had treated other Christian believers over the years, and also invited Catholics to pardon those who had persecuted them.}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.catholicnews.com/services/englishnews/2016/pope-asks-mercy-pardon-for-ways-christians-have-harmed-one-another.cfm|title=Pope asks mercy, pardon for ways Christians have harmed one another|last=Wooden|first=Cindy|date=25 January 2016|publisher=[[Catholic News Service]]|language=English|accessdate=27 January 2016|quote=After walking across the threshold of the [[Holy Door]] with an Orthodox metropolitan and an Anglican archbishop, Pope Francis invoked God's mercy upon divided Christians and apologized for times that Catholics may have hurt members of other denominations. "As bishop of Rome and pastor of the Catholic Church, I want to beg for mercy and forgiveness for un-Gospel-like behavior on the part of Catholics against Christians of other churches," the pope said Jan. 25 at a prayer service concluding the Week of Prayer for Christian Unity. "We ask most of all for forgiveness for the sin of our divisions, which are an open wound on the body of Christ," Pope Francis said. "At the same time, I ask all my Catholic brothers and sisters to forgive if, today or in the past, they were hurt by other Christians," he said. "We cannot erase what happened, but we do not want to allow the burden of past faults to continue to poison our relationships."}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.msn.com/en-us/news/world/pope-asks-protestants-for-forgiveness-for-persecution/ar-BBoGlPv?ocid=spartanntp|title=Pope asks Protestants for forgiveness for persecution|last=Pullella|first=Philip|date=25 January 2016|publisher=[[MSN]]|language=English|accessdate=27 January 2016|quote=Pope Francis asked Protestants and other Christian Churches for forgiveness for past persecution by Catholics as the Vatican announced on Monday he would visit Sweden later in the year to mark the 500th anniversary of the Reformation. Speaking at an annual vespers service in St. Paul's Basilica in Rome attended by representatives of other religions, he asked "forgiveness for the un-gospel like behavior by Catholics towards Christians of other Churches." He also asked Catholics to forgive those who had persecuted them.|deadurl=yes|archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160203183522/http://www.msn.com/en-us/news/world/pope-asks-protestants-for-forgiveness-for-persecution/ar-BBoGlPv?ocid=spartanntp|archivedate=3 February 2016|df=dmy-all}}&lt;/ref&gt;

====Independent Catholicism====
In October 2014, Pope Francis met for the first time with a delegation of the [[Old Catholic Church]]'s Bishops' Conference of the [[Union of Utrecht (Old Catholic)|Union of Utrecht]], led by the Archbishop of Utrecht and President of the International Old Catholic Bishops Conference [[Joris Vercammen]].&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.catholicnewsagency.com/news/pope-francis-reaches-out-to-schismatic-old-catholic-church-28251/|title=Pope Francis reaches out to schismatic Old Catholic Church|publisher=|accessdate=21 March 2017}}&lt;/ref&gt; The Pope reflected on the shared ecumenical journey of the two churches since their 18th-century schism over the issue of [[papal primacy]]. The Pope called for Catholics and [[Independent Catholicism|Independent Catholics]] to "persevere in dialogue and to walk, pray and work together in a deeper spirit of conversion" and said there are "many areas in which Catholics and Old Catholics can collaborate in tackling the profound spiritual crisis affecting individuals and societies, especially in Europe."&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://en.radiovaticana.va/news/2014/10/30/pope_meets_with_leaders_of_old_catholic_bishops_conference/1109760|title=Pope meets with leaders of Old Catholic Bishops Conference|publisher=|accessdate=21 March 2017}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.news.va/en/news/pope-meets-with-leaders-of-old-catholic-bishops-co|title=Pope meets with leaders of Old Catholic Bishops Conference|publisher=|accessdate=21 March 2017}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=https://w2.vatican.va/content/francesco/en/speeches/2014/october/documents/papa-francesco_20141030_vescovi-veterocattolici.html|title=To a delegation of the Old Catholic Bishops' Conference of the Union of Utrecht (30 October 2014) - Francis |publisher=Holy See |accessdate=21 March 2017}}&lt;/ref&gt;

====Eastern Orthodoxy====
