[[File:Pope Franciscus &amp; Patriarch Bartholomew I in the Church of the Holy Sepulchre in Jerusalem (1).JPG|thumb|upright=1.25|Francis with [[Patriarch Bartholomew I of Constantinople|Patriarch Bartholomew I]] in the [[Church of the Holy Sepulchre]], during his 2014 pilgrimage to the [[Holy Land]]]]
Bergoglio is recognized for his efforts "to further close the nearly 1,000-year estrangement with the [[Eastern Orthodox Churches]]".&lt;ref name="orthodox"&gt;Ritter, Karl, [http://www.huffingtonpost.com/2013/03/15/pope-francis-jews_n_2883560.html?icid=maing-grid7|main5|dl19|sec3_lnk3%26pLid%3D284812 "Pope Francis reaches out to Jews"], huffingtonpost.com, 16 March 2013, Retrieved 16 March 2013&lt;/ref&gt; Antoni Sevruk, rector of the Russian Orthodox Church of Saint Catherine the Great Martyr in Rome, said that Bergoglio "often visited Orthodox services in the Russian Orthodox Annunciation Cathedral in Buenos Aires" and is known as an advocate on behalf of the Orthodox Church in dealing with Argentina's government.&lt;ref&gt;Faustova Milena, [http://english.ruvr.ru/2013_03_16/Orthodox-flock-of-Rome-hopes-are-high-for-the-new-Pope/ "Orthodox flock of Rome: hopes are high for the new pope"], Radio, the Voice of Russia (english.ruvr.ru), 16 March 2013, Retrieved 16 March 2013.&lt;/ref&gt;

Bergoglio's positive relationship with the Eastern Orthodox Churches is reflected in the fact that [[Patriarch Bartholomew I of Constantinople]] attended his installation.&lt;ref name="patriarch"&gt;Demacopoulos, George E., [http://www.archons.org/news/detail.asp?id=619 "The extraordinary historical significance of His Holiness' presence at Pope Francis' installation as Bishop of Rome"], Archon News (Order of St. Andrew the Apostle), 19 March 2013, Retrieved 19 March 2013&lt;/ref&gt; This is the first time since the [[EastWest Schism|Great Schism]] of 1054 that the Orthodox [[Ecumenical Patriarch of Constantinople]], a position considered [[first among equals]] in the Eastern [[Orthodox Church organization]], has attended a papal installation.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news |title= Our Eastern Brothers |first= Alton J. |last= Pelowski |journal= Columbia |date= May 2013 |pages= 2023 |url = http://www.kofc.org/un/en/columbia/detail/2013_05_eastern.html}}&lt;/ref&gt; Orthodox leaders state that Bartholomew's decision to attend the ceremony shows that the relationship between the Orthodox and Catholic Churches is a priority of his, but they also note that Francis's "well-documented work for social justice and his insistence that globalization is detrimental to the poor" may have created a "renewed opportunity" for the two Church communities to "work collectively on issues of mutual concern".&lt;ref name="patriarch" /&gt;{{efn|One source says that the [[gospel]] was chanted in Greek during the pope's inauguration Mass in recognition of Bartholomew's historic attendance,&lt;ref name="patriarch"/&gt; but the Vatican News Service paraphrased [[Federico Lombardi]] of the Vatican Press Office as explaining that "[t]he Gospel will be proclaimed in Greek, ''as at the highest solemnities'', to show that the universal Church is made up of the great traditions of the East and the West." (emphasis added)&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news |title=Tomorrow, Mass of Inauguration of Bishop of Rome's Petrine Ministry|url=http://www.news.va/en/news/tomorrow-mass-of-inauguration-of-bishop-of-romes-p|accessdate=24 March 2013|publisher=Vatican News Service|date=18 March 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt;}}

In 2013, Pope Francis received [[Patriarch Theodore II of Alexandria|Theodore II]], [[List of Greek Orthodox Patriarchs of Alexandria|Pope and Patriarch of Alexandria and All Africa]], the leader of the [[Greek Orthodox Church of Alexandria]], in the Vatican.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.copticcatholicpatriarchate.net/ProvaJ/index.php/20-varieties/95-pope-receives-greek-orthodox-patriarch-of-alexandria-and-all-africa|title=Pope receives Greek Orthodox Patriarch of Alexandria and All Africa|first=Mariam|last=Kamil|publisher=}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.news.va/en/news/pope-receives-greek-orthodox-patriarch-of-alexandr|title=Pope receives Greek Orthodox Patriarch of Alexandria and All Africa|publisher=}}&lt;/ref&gt;

On 12 February 2016, Pope Francis and [[Patriarch Kirill of Moscow]], head of the [[Russian Orthodox Church]], met in Havana, Cuba, issuing the [[Joint Declaration of Pope Francis and Patriarch Kirill]], calling for restored Christian unity between the two churches. This was reported as the first such high-level meeting between the two churches since the [[EastWest Schism|Great Schism]] of 1054.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|url=http://www.bbc.co.uk/news/world-latin-america-35565085|title=Unity call as Pope Francis holds historic talks with Russian Orthodox Patriarch|publisher=BBC|date=12 February 2016|access-date=13 February 2016}}&lt;/ref&gt;

On April 28, 2017, Pope Francis participated in an ecumenical prayer service in Cairo, Egypt, with Pope Theodoros II, Eastern Orthodox Patriarch of Alexandria and all Africa, Ecumenical Patriarch Bartholomew, and Coptic Orthodox Pope Tawadros II.  This historic event appears to be the first time that the three Christian popes and the ecumenical patriarch have met together.  (Joshua J. McElwee (2017).  "In Egypt, Francis appeals for peace."  "National Catholic Reporter."  May 19-June 1, 2017.  p. 6)

====Oriental Orthodoxy====
In May 2013, Pope Francis met with [[Pope Tawadros II of Alexandria]] in the Vatican. The meeting coincided with the 40th anniversary of the first visit by a [[Pope of the Coptic Orthodox Church of Alexandria]] to the Vatican; when [[Pope Shenouda III of Alexandria]] met with [[Pope Paul VI]] on 10 May 1973.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.news.va/en/news/pope-francis-welcomes-egypts-coptic-orthodox-pope|title=Pope Francis welcomes Egypt's Coptic Orthodox Pope Tawadros|publisher=|accessdate=21 March 2017}}&lt;/ref&gt; Francis reflected on the close relationship between the Catholic Church and the [[Coptic Orthodox Church of Alexandria]], saying that the visit "strengthens the bonds of friendship and brotherhood that already exist between the See of Peter and the See of Mark" and praised the Commission for Theological Dialogue for preparing ground for dialogue between the Catholic Church and [[Oriental Orthodox]] churches. Pope Francis also acknowledged the two churches shared beliefs in the Trinity, the divinity of Christ, Marian devotion, apostolic traditions, and the seven sacraments.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.catholic.org/news/international/europe/story.php?id=50996|title=Historic Meeting between Pope Francis and Coptic Patriarch, Tawadros II, Fosters Christian Unity - Europe - International - News - Catholic Online|first=Michael|last=Terheyden|publisher=|accessdate=21 March 2017}}&lt;/ref&gt; In May 2016, Pope Francis sent a letter to Tawadros II, acknowledging their shared commitment to holiness and defending the dignity of human life and celebrating friendship between Catholics and Coptic Orthodox Christians. The Pope said, "we are able even now to make visible the communion uniting us."&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.catholicnewsagency.com/news/we-have-a-common-witness-pope-francis-tells-coptic-orthodox-patriarch-43850/|title=We have a common witness, Pope Francis tells Coptic Orthodox patriarch|publisher=|accessdate=21 March 2017}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://aleteia.org/2016/05/11/blood-and-water-unite-catholics-and-copts-pope-francis-tells-egyptian-church/|title=Blood and Water Unite Catholics and Copts, Pope Francis Tells Egyptian Church|date=11 May 2016|publisher=|accessdate=21 March 2017}}&lt;/ref&gt;

In June 2015, Pope Francis met with [[Ignatius Aphrem II|Moran Mor Ignatius Aphrem II]], [[List of Syriac Orthodox Patriarchs of Antioch|Patriarch]] of the [[Syriac Orthodox Church]].&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://en.radiovaticana.va/news/2015/06/16/pope_francis_to_receive_syrian_orthodox_patriarch/1151885|title=Pope Francis to receive Syrian Orthodox Patriarch|publisher=|accessdate=21 March 2017}}&lt;/ref&gt; The two primates discussed their desire to work toward [[full communion]] between their two churches, stating that Antioch and Rome are the only two Apostolic Sees where St. Peter the Apostle had preached. They also expressed an eagerness to celebrate Easter on a common date, as Catholics and Oriental Orthodox have separate days for Easter.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=https://www.ncronline.org/blogs/francis-chronicles/pope-orthodox-patriarch-express-commitment-unity|title=Pope, Orthodox patriarch express commitment for unity|date=19 June 2015|publisher=|accessdate=21 March 2017}}&lt;/ref&gt;

During his [[List of pastoral visits of Pope Francis outside Italy#Armenia (24 to 26 June 2016)|papal visit to Armenia in 2016]], Pope Francis prayed inside [[Etchmiadzin Cathedral]], the mother church of the [[Armenian Apostolic Church]] and the oldest state-built church in the world, alongside the [[Catholicos of All Armenians]], [[Karekin II]].&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=https://www.ncronline.org/news/vatican/francis-and-armenian-orthodox-patriarch-say-churches-are-one-prayer-action|title=Francis and Armenian Orthodox patriarch say churches are one in prayer, action|date=26 June 2016|publisher=}}&lt;/ref&gt; During the prayer service, the Pope asked for and received a blessing from Catholicos Karekin II.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.americamagazine.org/content/dispatches/pope-francis-prays-full-unity-armenian-apostolic-church|title=Pope Francis Prays for Full Unity with Armenian Apostolic Church|date=26 June 2016|publisher=}}&lt;/ref&gt; The Pope spoke about the Christian faith of the Armenian people and how [[Armenia]] became the first nation to accept Christianity as its official religion, even while persecutions under Emperor [[Diocletian]] were prevalent in the Roman Empire. The Pope also gave thanks for the relationship between the Catholic Church and the Armenian Apostolic Church and the steps they have taken "for the sake of coming to share fully in the Eucharistic banquet."&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://en.radiovaticana.va/news/2016/06/24/pope_francis_prays_in_armenian_apostolic_cathedral/1239643|title=Pope Francis prays in Armenian Apostolic Cathedral|publisher=}}&lt;/ref&gt;

In February 2017, the Pope met with Coptic bishops at the Vatican to discuss the violence against and [[persecution of Christians in the Middle East]].&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.middleeasteye.net/news/pope-francis-visit-egypt-meet-imam-persecuted-copts-732429106|title=Egypt: Pope Francis to meet with persecuted Coptic Christians|publisher=|accessdate=21 March 2017}}&lt;/ref&gt;

====Anglicanism====
[[Gregory Venables]], [[Anglican Bishop of Argentina]] and former Primate of the [[Anglican Church of the Southern Cone of America]], said that Cardinal Bergoglio had told him very clearly that the [[personal ordinariate]]s established within the Catholic Church for groups of former Anglicans was "quite unnecessary" and that the Catholic Church needed Anglicans as Anglicans. A spokesman for the ordinariates said the words were those of Venables, not the Pope.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|last=Affairs |first=Religious |url=https://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/religion/the-pope/9933614/Pope-Francis-dismissed-Anglican-branch-as-quite-unnecessary.html |title=The Telegraph newspaper: Pope Francis 'dismissed Anglican branch as quite unnecessary', 31 May 2013 |publisher=The Daily Telegraph |date= 15 March 2013|accessdate=23 June 2013 |location=London}}&lt;/ref&gt; Pope Francis met for the first time the [[Archbishop of Canterbury]], [[Justin Welby]], when he visited the Vatican, on 14 June 2013. The Roman Pontiff said that they both shared the same concerns for social justice, peace and the promotion of Christian values, in matters like marriage.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|url=https://www.independent.co.uk/news/uk/home-news/pope-francis-meets-archbishop-of-canterbury-justin-welby-in-rome-8659481.html|title=Pope Francis meets Archbishop of Canterbury Justin Welby in Rome|date=14 June 2013|work=The Independent|accessdate=20 May 2016}}&lt;/ref&gt; The second meeting took place at the Vatican, on 16 June 2014, with Pope Francis and Justin Welby recommitting themselves to work against modern slavery and human trafficking.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.archbishopofcanterbury.org/articles.php/5344/archbishop-meets-pope-francis-in-rome|title=Archbishop meets Pope Francis in Rome|publisher=|accessdate=20 May 2016}}&lt;/ref&gt; Pope Francis has expressed his support for the [[Anglican realignment]], sending through his personal friend, Gregory Venables, a message to the Archbishop [[Foley Beach]] of the [[Anglican Church in North America]], a newly formed church outside of the Anglican Communion and not officially recognized by the [[Archbishop of Canterbury]], with his "personal greetings and congratulations as he leads his church in the very important job of revival" and asking Venables to embrace him on his behalf. It was presented during Archbishop Beach's enthronement, which took place at the Church of the Apostles in [[Atlanta]], [[Georgia (U.S. state)|Georgia]], on 9 October 2014.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.anglican.ink/article/papal-greetings-newest-anglican-archbishop#sthash.8JhUVxDn.j016j3Ms.dpbs|title=Papal greetings for newest Anglican archbishop|publisher=|accessdate=20 May 2016}}&lt;/ref&gt;

====Lutheranism====
On 31 October 2016, Pope Francis commemorated the 499th anniversary of the [[Reformation]] with Lutherans in Sweden. This event opened the 500th year{{efn|31 October 2016 is the 499th anniversary of the start of the Reformation.}} since the Reformation began with Martin Luther posting his [[Ninety-Five Theses]] in [[Wittenberg]] in 1517.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=https://www.npr.org/sections/parallels/2016/10/28/499587801/pope-francis-reaches-out-to-honor-the-man-who-splintered-christianity|title=The Pope Commemorates The Reformation That Split Western Christianity|author=Paggioli, Sylvia|date=|work=npr.org|accessdate=29 October 2016}}&lt;/ref&gt; The Pope visited the 950 year old [[Lund Cathedral]], located in Sweden's southernmost and originally Danish province of [[Scania]]. He celebrated an ecumenical liturgy together with the president of the [[Lutheran World Federation]] Bishop Dr. [[Munib Younan]]. Pope Francis expressed his shared desire with leaders of the [[Church of Sweden]] to achieve full communion, but said more ecumenical work needed to be done in order to work towards communion.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2016/11/01/world/europe/pope-francis-in-sweden-urges-catholic-lutheran-reconciliation.html|title=Pope Francis, in Sweden, Urges Catholic-Lutheran Reconciliation|first=Christina|last=Anderson|date=31 October 2016|publisher=|via=NYTimes.com}}&lt;/ref&gt; The two churches called for focusing on what unites their faith rather than what separates them from each other (Pope Francis previously made a similar treaty with the Orthodox Church.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.catholicherald.co.uk/news/2016/01/25/pope-francis-to-visit-sweden-for-reformation-commemoration/|title=Pope Francis to visit Sweden for Reformation commemoration - CatholicHerald.co.uk|date=25 January 2016|publisher=|accessdate=21 March 2017}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=https://www.lutheranworld.org/|title=The Lutheran World Federation|publisher=|accessdate=21 March 2017}}&lt;/ref&gt;) The following day the Pope conducted a Catholic mass at a football stadium in [[Malm]].&lt;ref&gt;Both the Ecumenical commemoration and the Catholical mass were aired live and commentated at Swedish national, commercial free, television distributor, SVT&lt;/ref&gt;

In 2013, [[Mark Hanson]], then presiding bishop of the [[Evangelical Lutheran Church in America]] (ELCA), greeted the news of Bergoglio's election with a public statement that praised his work with [[Lutheran]]s in Argentina.&lt;ref name="lutherans"&gt;[https://web.archive.org/web/20130325082649/http://www.elca.org/Who-We-Are/Our-Three-Expressions/Churchwide-Organization/Communication-Services/News/Releases.aspx?a=5281 "New pope has ties to Lutherans, says ELCA presiding bishop,"] ELCA news service, 13 March 2013, Retrieved 16 March 2013.&lt;/ref&gt;

==== Methodism ====
On 14 December 2014, Pope Francis became the first pope to host a [[General of The Salvation Army]], the international leader of the [[Holiness movement|Evangelical Methodist]] denomination [[The Salvation Army]], in a private audience in the Vatican when he met with [[Andr Cox]]. The pope said that "Catholics and Salvationists, together with other Christians, recognise that those in need have a special place in God's heart", as a result they often "meet at the same peripheries of society".&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.news.va/en/news/pope-says-salvationists-and-catholics-meet-at-peri|title=Pope says Salvationists and Catholics meet at peripheries of society|publisher=}}&lt;/ref&gt;

During his [[Pope Francis' visit to the Philippines|papal visit to the Philippines]] in 2015, the Pope met with [[Chief Justice of the Supreme Court of the Philippines|Chief Justice]] [[Reynato Puno]], a [[United Methodist]] layman, along with nine other religious leaders and peace advocates to discuss humanitarian relief.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|author= |url=http://www.umc.org/news-and-media/united-methodist-layman-to-meet-pope-francis |title=United Methodist layman to meet Pope Francis &amp;#124; The United Methodist Church |website=Umc.org |date= |accessdate=21 March 2017}}&lt;/ref&gt;

In 2016, Pope Francis met with members of the [[World Methodist Council]], the Methodist Council of Europe, and the [[Methodist Church in Britain]], who were in Rome for the opening of the Methodist Ecumenical Office there.&lt;ref name="radiovaticana.va"&gt;{{cite web|url=http://en.radiovaticana.va/news/2016/04/07/catholics,_methodists_walking_together_in_service_to_world/1220987|title=Catholics and Methodists: Walking together in service to the world|publisher=|accessdate=21 March 2017}}&lt;/ref&gt; The Pope called for Catholics and Methodists to unite in their Christian beliefs and in service to others.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=https://cruxnow.com/church/2016/04/08/catholics-and-methodists-can-learn-from-one-another-pope-says/|title=Catholics and Methodists can learn from one another, pope says|date=8 April 2016|publisher=|accessdate=21 March 2017}}&lt;/ref&gt; Pope Francis referred to Catholics and Methodists as "truly brothers and sisters" and, reflecting on the words of the Anglican priest and founder of Methodism [[John Wesley]] in his ''Letter to a Roman Catholic'', quoted "if we cannot as yet think alike in all things, at least we may love alike."&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://en.radiovaticana.va/news/2016/04/07/pope_francis_addresses_methodist_guests_full_text/1220885|title=Pope Francis addresses Methodist guests: full text|publisher=|accessdate=21 March 2017}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref name="radiovaticana.va"/&gt;

Also in 2016, Pope Francis met with Gottfried Locher, the President of the [[Federation of Swiss Protestant Churches]] to speak about "ecumenism and Protestantism in Europe." The Federation of Swiss Protestant Churches is made up of [[Calvinist]], [[Theology of Huldrych Zwingli|Zwinglian]], and Methodist churches.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://en.radiovaticana.va/news/2016/03/05/pope_meets_with_swiss_protestant_leader/1213171|title=Pope meets with Swiss Protestant leader|publisher=}}&lt;/ref&gt;

====Evangelicalism====
[[Evangelical Christian]] leaders, including Argentine [[Luis Palau]], welcomed the news of Bergoglio's election as Pope based on his relations with [[Evangelicalism|Evangelical Protestants]], noting that Bergoglio's financial manager for the Archdiocese of Buenos Aires was an Evangelical Christian whom Bergoglio refers to as a friend.&lt;ref name="evangelicals"&gt;Stefan, Melissa, [http://www.christianitytoday.com/ct/2013/march-web-only/luis-palau-pope-francis-drinks-mate-evangelicals-bergoglio.html?paging=off "Luis Palau: Why it matters that Pope Francis drinks mate with Evangelicals]," ''Christianity Today'', 14 March 2013, Retrieved 15 March 2013.&lt;/ref&gt; Palau recounted how Bergoglio would not only relax and "drink [[Mate (drink)|mate]]" with that friend, but would also read the Bible and pray with him, based on what Bergoglio called a relationship of friendship and trust.&lt;ref name="evangelicals" /&gt; Palau described Bergoglio's approach to relationships with Evangelicals as one of "building bridges and showing respect, knowing the differences, but majoring on what we can agree on: on the divinity of Jesus, his virgin birth, his resurrection, the second coming."&lt;ref name="evangelicals" /&gt; As a result of Bergoglio's election, Palau predicted that "tensions will be eased."&lt;ref name="evangelicals" /&gt;

Juan Pablo Bongarr, president of the Argentine Bible Society, recounted that Bergoglio not only met with Evangelicals and prayed with them, he also asked them to pray ''for'' him.&lt;ref name="weber"&gt;Weber, Jeremy, [http://www.christianitytoday.com/ct/2013/march-web-only/argentine-evangelicals-say-bergoglio-as-pope-francis-is-ans.html "Argentine Evangelicals say Bergoglio as Pope Francis 'answer to our prayers'"], ''Christianity Today'', 14 March 2013, Retrieved 16 March 2013.&lt;/ref&gt; Bongarr noted that Bergoglio would frequently end a conversation with the request, "Pastor, pray for me."&lt;ref name="weber" /&gt; Additionally, Bongarr told the story of a weekly worship meeting of charismatic pastors in Buenos Aires, which Bergoglio attended: "He mounted the platform and called for pastors to pray for him. He knelt in front of nearly 6,000 people, and [the Protestant leaders there] laid hands and prayed."&lt;ref name="weber" /&gt;

Other Evangelical Christian leaders agreed that Bergoglio's relationships in Argentina made him "situated to better understand Protestantism" than had his predecessor Pope Benedict, "who often referred to Protestantism as a 'sect' of Christianity".&lt;ref name="christianitytoday"&gt;Moon, Ruth, [http://www.christianitytoday.com/ct/2013/march-web-only/why-pope-francis-excites-most-evangelical-leaders-bergoglio.html "Why Pope Francis excites (most) Evangelical leaders,"] Christianity Today, 14 March 2013, Retrieved 15 March 2013.&lt;/ref&gt; Noting that the divide between Catholicism and Protestantism is often present among members of the same families in Argentina, and is therefore an extremely important human issue, Evangelical author Chris Castaldo said that Francis could set the tone for more compassionate conversations among families about the differences between Protestantism and Catholicism.&lt;ref name="christianitytoday" /&gt;

====Mormonism====
In November 2014, three top [[Mormonism|Mormon]] leaders attended the Vatican's "Humanum: An International Interreligious Colloquium on the Complementarity of Man and Woman"; the [[Presiding Bishop (LDS Church)|Presiding Bishop]] of [[the Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints]] [[Grald Causs]], the First Counselor in the [[First Presidency (LDS Church)|First Presidency]] of the LDS Church [[Henry B. Eyring]], and [[L. Tom Perry]], a member of the [[Quorum of the Twelve Apostles (LDS Church)|Quorum of the Twelve Apostles]]. Catholic and Mormon leaders reaffirmed their shared beliefs in the centrality of marriage and families in society.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=https://www.lds.org/church/news/three-leaders-represented-lds-views-on-family-at-vatican?lang=eng|title=Three Leaders Represented LDS Views on Family at Vatican - Church News and Events|publisher=}}&lt;/ref&gt; Pope Francis shook hands with Henry B. Eyring, who was one of the 30 speakers chosen for the event.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.deseretnews.com/article/865614617/LDS-leader-to-join-Vatican-conference-on-complementary-union-of-man-and-woman.html|title=LDS leader to join Vatican conference on 'complementary union of man and woman'|first=Tad|last=Walch|date=3 November 2014|publisher=}}&lt;/ref&gt; The interaction was the first time a Pope and a Latter-day Saint leader had met face-to-face.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.sltrib.com/lifestyle/faith/1836619-155/eyring-marriage-pope-address-conference-environments|title=Pope, Mormon leader make history with a handshake|first=Peggy |last=Fletcher Stack |publisher=The Salt Lake Tribune}}&lt;/ref&gt;

===Interfaith dialogue===
[[File:Pope Francis visit Bethlehem.jpg|thumb|Pope Francis in [[Bethlehem]], [[State of Palestine|Palestine]], 25 May 2014]]
Bergoglio has written about his commitment to open and respectful [[interfaith dialogue]] as a way for all parties engaged in that dialogue to learn from one another.&lt;ref name="interfaith"&gt;Lefebure, Leo D., [http://www.parliamentofreligions.org/news/index.php/tag/rabbi-abraham-skorka/ "Pope Francis and Interreligious Relations,"] {{webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20131017165755/http://www.parliamentofreligions.org/news/index.php/tag/rabbi-abraham-skorka/ |date=17 October 2013 }} parliamentofreligions.org, Retrieved 16 March 2013&lt;/ref&gt; In the 2011 book that records his conversations with Rabbi [[Abraham Skorka]], ''[[On Heaven and Earth]]'', Bergoglio said:

{{quote|Dialogue is born from an attitude of respect for the other person, from a conviction that the other person has something good to say. It assumes that there is room in the heart for the person's point of view, opinion, and proposal. Dialogue entails a cordial reception, not a prior condemnation. In order to dialogue it is necessary to know how to lower the defenses, open the doors of the house, and offer human warmth.&lt;ref name="interfaith"/&gt;}}

Religious leaders in Buenos Aires have mentioned that Bergoglio promoted interfaith ceremonies at the [[Buenos Aires Metropolitan Cathedral]].&lt;ref name="ceremonies"&gt;[http://www.foxnews.com/world/2013/03/18/argentine-jews-hope-pope-francis-will-continue-interfaith-dialogue-promoted-as/ "Argentine Jews praise Pope Francis for interfaith dialogue"], foxnews.com (from AP), 18 March 2013, Retrieved 19 March 2013&lt;/ref&gt; For example, in November 2012 he brought leaders of the Jewish, Muslim, Evangelical, and Orthodox Christian faiths together to pray for a peaceful solution to the [[List of modern conflicts in the Middle East|Middle East conflicts]].&lt;ref name="ceremonies" /&gt; Rabbi [[Alejandro Avruj]] praised Bergoglio's interest in interfaith dialogue and his commitment to mend religious divisions.&lt;ref name="ceremonies" /&gt;

Shortly after his election, the pope called for more interreligious dialogue as a way of "building bridges" and establishing "true links of friendship between all people".&lt;ref name="interfaithdialogue" /&gt; He added that it was crucial "to intensify outreach to nonbelievers, so that the differences which divide and hurt us may never prevail".&lt;ref name="interfaithdialogue" /&gt; He said that his title of "pontiff" means "builder of bridges", and that it was his wish that "the dialogue between us should help to build bridges connecting all people, in such a way that everyone can see in the other not an enemy, not a rival, but a brother or sister to be welcomed and embraced."&lt;ref name="interfaithdialogue" /&gt;

On 24 May 2014, Pope Francis arrived in [[Jordan]], at the start of a tour of the Middle East, "aiming to boost ties with Muslims and Jews as well as easing an age-old rift within Christianity".&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.aljazeera.com/news/middleeast/2014/05/pope-francis-begins-middle-east-tour-201452431846597709.html |title=Pope Francis begins Middle East tour  Middle East |publisher=Al Jazeera English |date= |accessdate=24 May 2014}}&lt;/ref&gt;

In a 2016 survey, Francis was viewed favourably by almost two thirds of Jews, as well as majorities of Protestants and the irreligious; minorities of Buddhists and Muslims had favourable views of him.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|last1=Wyatt|first1=Caroline|title=Pope Francis's reforms polarise the Vatican|url=http://www.bbc.co.uk/news/world-europe-35869656|accessdate=27 March 2016|publisher=BBC News|date=27 March 2016}}&lt;/ref&gt;

====Judaism====
[[File:Franciscus kotel.jpg|thumb|Francis praying at the [[Western Wall]] in [[Jerusalem]] on his 2014 visit to the Holy Land]]
Bergoglio has close ties to the [[History of the Jews in Argentina|Jewish community of Argentina]], and attended [[Rosh Hashanah]] (Jewish new year) services in 2007 at a synagogue in Buenos Aires. He told the Jewish congregation during his visit that he went to the synagogue to examine his heart, "like a pilgrim, together with you, my elder brothers".&lt;ref name="jta"&gt;{{cite news|title=New pope, Jorge Mario Bergoglio of Argentina, has Jewish connections|url= http://www.jta.org/2013/03/13/news-opinion/world/new-pope-jorge-mario-bergoglio-of-argentina-has-jewish-connections|accessdate=15 May 2015|publisher=Jewish Telegraphic Agency|date=13 March 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt; After the 1994 [[AMIA bombing]] of a [[Jewish Community Center]] that killed 85 people, Bergoglio was the first public figure to sign a petition condemning the attack and calling for justice. Jewish community leaders around the world noted that his words and actions "showed solidarity with the Jewish community" in the aftermath of this attack.&lt;ref name="jta" /&gt;

A former head of the [[World Jewish Congress]], [[Israel Singer]], reported that he worked with Bergoglio in the early 2000s, distributing aid to the poor as part of a joint JewishCatholic program called "[[Tzedak]]". Singer noted that he was impressed with Bergoglio's modesty, remembering that "if everyone sat in chairs with handles [arms], he would sit in the one without."&lt;ref name="jta" /&gt; Bergoglio also co-hosted a ''[[Kristallnacht]]'' memorial ceremony at the [[Buenos Aires Metropolitan Cathedral]] in 2012,&lt;ref name="jta" /&gt; and joined a group of clerics from a number of different religions to light candles in a 2012 synagogue ceremony on the occasion of the Jewish festival of [[Hanukkah]].&lt;ref&gt;[http://www.algemeiner.com/2013/03/14/new-popes-relationship-with-jews-lit-menorah-during-2012-hanukkah-celebration-in-argentina-video/ "New Pope's Relationship with Jews: Lit menorah during 2012 Hanukkah celebration in Argentina" (VIDEO)], algemeiner.com, 16 March 2013, Retrieved 16 March 2013. The newscaster in this Argentinian television video notes that Bergoglio was the "guest of honor" and includes names and images of some of the other religious representatives who participated.&lt;/ref&gt;

Pope Francis blessed the cornerstone for the building of the museum devoted to [[Rescue of Jews by Poles during the Holocaust|wartime Polish rescuers of Jews]] which is being built in the Polish village of [[Markowa]]; where the family of [[Jzef and Wiktoria Ulma]], who are now [[Servants of God]] as the Vatican is studying their cause for sainthood, were shot by the Germans for hiding their Jewish neighbors.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.thenews.pl/1/9/Artykul/153688,Foundation-stone-laid-at-Polish-righteous-museum/|title=Foundation stone laid at Polish righteous museum|work=Polskie Radio dla Zagranicy}}&lt;/ref&gt;

[[Abraham Skorka]], the rector of the [[Latin-American Rabbinical Seminary]] in Buenos Aires, and Bergoglio published their conversations on religious and philosophical subjects as ''Sobre el cielo y la tierra'' (''[[On Heaven and Earth]]'').&lt;ref name="jerusalempost"&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.jpost.com/Opinion/Editorials/Article.aspx?id=306508 |title=''Francis and the Jews'' in ''Jerusalem Post'' 14 March 2013 |publisher=Jpost.com |date=14 March 2013 |accessdate=19 March 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt; An editorial in Israel's ''[[Jerusalem Post]]'' notes that "Unlike John Paul II, who as a child had positive memories of the Jews of his native Poland but due to the Holocaust had no Jewish community to interact with in Poland as an adult, Pope Francis has maintained a sustained and very positive relationship with a living, breathing [Jewish] community in Buenos Aires."&lt;ref name="jerusalempost" /&gt;

One of the pope's first official actions was writing a letter to Rabbi [[Riccardo Di Segni]], the [[Chief Rabbi]] of Rome, inviting him to the papal installation and sharing his hope of collaboration between the Catholic and Jewish communities.&lt;ref name="romerabbi"&gt;Goldman, Ari L., [http://www.thejewishweek.com/news/international-news/romes-chief-rabbi-spotlight "Rome's chief rabbi in the spotlight"], ''The Jewish Week'', 28 March 2013, Retrieved 1 April 2013&lt;/ref&gt; Addressing representatives of Jewish organizations and communities, Francis said that, "due to our common roots [a] Christian cannot be [[Antisemitism|anti-Semitic]]!"&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|last=West|first=Ed|title=Pope Francis condemns anti-Semitism|url=http://www.catholicherald.co.uk/news/2013/06/24/pope-francis-condems-anti-semitism/|accessdate=2 July 2013|publisher=Catholic Herald|date=24 June 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt;

Francis had a warm relationship with [[President of Israel|Israeli President]] [[Shimon Peres]], who visited the pope in April 2013 and invited him to Israel.&lt;ref name=rome/&gt; Francis traveled to Israel in May 2014 and met with Peres at the presidential residence.&lt;ref name=rome/&gt; During his trip, Francis invited both Peres and Palestinian president [[Mahmoud Abbas]] to join him in Rome to "pray for peace",&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web |url=https://www.telegraph.co.uk/telegraphtv/10854328/Pope-invites-Israeli-and-Palestinian-leaders-for-Vatican-peace-prayers.html|title=Pope invites Israeli and Palestinian leaders for Vatican peace prayers|date=25 May 2014|accessdate=7 July 2017|work=[[The Daily Telegraph|The Telegraph]]}}&lt;/ref&gt; which Peres and Abbas did in June 2014.&lt;ref name=rome/&gt; After leaving the presidency, Peres visited Francis again in Rome in September 2014 and June 2016.&lt;ref name=rome&gt;{{cite web |url=http://www.romereports.com/2016/09/28/remembering-pope-francis-encounters-with-shimon-peres|title=Remembering Pope Francis' encounters with Shimon Peres|date=28 September 2016|accessdate=7 July 2017|work=Rome Reports}}&lt;/ref&gt;

====Islam====
[[Islam in Argentina|Muslim leaders in Buenos Aires]] welcomed the news of Bergoglio's election as pope, noting that he "always showed himself as a friend of the Islamic community", and a person whose position is "pro-dialogue".&lt;ref name="islam"&gt;[http://www.buenosairesherald.com/article/126369/pope-francis-a-friend-of-the-islamic-community "Pope Francis 'a friend of the Islamic community"], Buenos Aires Herald, 14 March 2013. Retrieved 14 March 2013&lt;/ref&gt; They praised Bergoglio's close ties with Muslim groups and noted his comments when Pope Benedict's 2006 [[Regensburg lecture]] was interpreted by many as denigrating Islam. According to them, Bergoglio immediately distanced himself from Benedict's language and said that statements which provoked outrage with Muslims would "serve to destroy in 20 seconds the careful construction of a relationship with Islam that Pope John Paul II built over the last 20 years."&lt;ref name="muslim"&gt;Ghosh, Palash, [http://www.ibtimes.com/pope-francis-friend-muslims-1130225 "Pope Francis: A friend to Muslims?"], ''International Business Times,'' 15 March 2013, Retrieved 16 March 2013.&lt;/ref&gt;

Bergoglio visited both a mosque and an Islamic school in Argentina; visits that the Director for the Diffusion of Islam, Sheik Mohsen Ali, called actions that strengthened the relationship between the Catholic and Islamic communities.&lt;ref name="islam" /&gt; Sumer Noufouri, Secretary General of the Islamic Center of the Argentine Republic (CIRA), added that for Muslims, Bergoglio's past actions make his election as pope a cause of "joy and expectation of strengthening dialogue between religions".&lt;ref name="islam" /&gt; Noufouri said that the relationship between CIRA and Bergoglio over the course of a decade had helped to build up ChristianMuslim dialogue in a way that was "really significant in the history of monotheistic relations in Argentina".&lt;ref name="islam" /&gt;

[[Ahmed el-Tayeb]], [[Grand Imam of al-Azhar]] and president of Egypt's [[Al-Azhar University]], sent congratulations after the pope's election.&lt;ref name="asia"&gt;{{cite news|title=Tawadros II thanks cardinals and Pope Francis for the "blessed choice"|url=http://www.asianews.it/news-en/Tawadros-II-thanks-cardinals-and-Pope-Francis-for-the-blessed-choice-27405.html|accessdate=14 April 2013|publisher=Asia News|date=15 March 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt; Al-Tayeb had "broken off relations with the Vatican" during Benedict XVI's time as pope; his message of congratulations also included the request that "Islam asks for respect from the new pontiff".&lt;ref name="asia" /&gt;

Shortly after his election, in a meeting with ambassadors from the 180 countries accredited with the Holy See, Pope Francis called for more interreligious dialogue"particularly with Islam".&lt;ref name="interfaithdialogue"&gt;Povoleto, Elisabetta, [https://www.nytimes.com/2013/03/23/world/europe/pope-francis-urges-more-interreligious-dialogue.html?_r=0 "Pope Francis Urges More Interreligious Dialogue"], ''New York Times'', 22 March 2013, Retrieved 26 March 2013&lt;/ref&gt; He also expressed gratitude that "so many civil and religious leaders from the Islamic world" had attended his installation Mass.&lt;ref name="interfaithdialogue" /&gt; An editorial in the Saudi Arabian paper ''[[Saudi Gazette]]'' strongly welcomed the pope's call for increased interfaith dialogue, stressing that while the pope was "reiterating a position he has always maintained", his public call as pope for increased dialogue with Islam "comes as a breath of fresh air at a time when much of the Western world is experiencing a nasty outbreak of [[Islamophobia]]".&lt;ref name="saudigazette"&gt;[http://www.saudigazette.com.sa/index.cfm?method=home.regcon&amp;contentid=20130325158320 "Pope's call for interfaith amity"] {{webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20131003020927/http://www.saudigazette.com.sa/index.cfm?method=home.regcon&amp;contentid=20130325158320 |date=3 October 2013 }}, ''Saudi Gazette'', 25 March 2013, Retrieved 26 March 2013&lt;/ref&gt;

In 2016, Pope Francis met with Ahmed el-Tayeb at the Vatican, the first meeting since 2000 between the Grand Imam of al-Azhar and the leader of the world's Catholics.&lt;ref name="meetingahmed"&gt;{{cite news | url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2016/may/24/pope-francis-embraces-senior-imam-sheikh-tayeb | title='Our meeting is the message': Pope Francis embraces senior imam | date=24 May 2016 | agency=[[theguardian.com]] | accessdate=24 May 2016}}&lt;/ref&gt;

In the aftermath of the [[2016 Normandy church attack]], whereby two Islamic terrorists affiliated with [[ISIS]] murdered the 85-year-old Catholic priest [[Jacques Hamel]] by slitting his throat, Bergoglio made public statements saying, "It's not right to identify Islam with violence. It's not right and it's not true [...] If I speak of Islamic violence, then I have to speak of Catholic violence."&lt;ref name="bbcpape"/&gt; According to the [[BBC]], this received a French backlash on social media, as the hashtag ''#PasMonPape'' ("Not My Pope") became the number one trend on [[Twitter]] in France.&lt;ref name="bbcpape"&gt;{{cite news | url=http://www.bbc.co.uk/news/blogs-trending-36954425 | title='Not my Pope' hashtag highlights French divisions| date=2 August 2016| agency=BBC| accessdate=5 August 2017}}&lt;/ref&gt;

==== Buddhism ====
In 2014, Pope Francis declined to meet with [[Tenzin Gyatso]], the 14th [[Dalai Lama]], after the Dalai Lama, who was visiting Rome, had requested a papal audience. Vatican officials assured the press and Buddhist leaders that Pope Francis held the Dalai Lama "in very high regard", but was concerned that the meeting of the two spiritual leaders could jeopardize the [[ChinaHoly See relations|Vatican's efforts to improve their relationship with China]].&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-30455187|title=Pope declines Dalai Lama meeting in Rome|date=12 December 2014|publisher=|via=www.bbc.com}}&lt;/ref&gt;  In speaking critically of the progress of the negotiations, in October 2017 [[Joseph Zen|Cardinal Joseph Zen]], former bishop of Hong Kong, said the Pope "does not understand the Communist Party at all" and that the Chinese Communist Party government had failed to make any concessions.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|url=https://www.hongkongfp.com/2017/10/06/pope-francis-not-understand-chinese-communist-party-says-hong-kong-cardinal-joseph-zen/|title=Pope Francis does not understand the Chinese Communist Party, says Hong Kong Cardinal Joseph Zen|date=6 October 2017|last=Cheng|first=Kris|newspaper=Hong Kong Free Press|access-date=7 October 2017}}&lt;/ref&gt;

In January 2015 during the [[Holy SeeSri Lanka relations|papal visit to Sri Lanka]], Pope Francis made an unscheduled stop at a Buddhist temple in [[Colombo, Sri Lanka|Colombo]] where he was shown sacred Buddhist relics that are normally only viewed once a year, and listened to singing and devotional music.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2015/jan/14/pope-francis-sri-lankan-buddhist-temple|title=Pope Francis changes schedule to visit Sri Lankan Buddhist temple|date=14 January 2015|publisher=Associated Press|via=The Guardian}}&lt;/ref&gt; Earlier that week, Francis had met with Buddhist, Hindu, Muslim and Christian leaders in Sri Lanka and said "religious beliefs must never be allowed to be abused in the cause of violence and war."&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=https://cruxnow.com/church/2015/01/14/pope-francis-makes-surprise-visit-to-buddhist-temple/|title=Pope Francis makes surprise visit to Buddhist temple|date=14 January 2015|publisher=}}&lt;/ref&gt;

On 24 June 2015, dialogue between [[Buddhism|Buddhist]] and Catholic religious and social leaders began in the Vatican, hosted by the Pontifical Council for Interreligious Dialogue and the United States Conference of Catholic Bishops. Pope Francis attended the meeting, where he spoke in favor of Buddhists and Catholics working together to address social problems.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.patheos.com/blogs/americanbuddhist/2015/06/pope-francis-beaming-as-he-leaves-meeting-with-american-buddhist-leaders.html|title=Pope Francis "Beaming" as he leaves meeting with American Buddhist leaders|date=26 June 2015|publisher=}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://en.radiovaticana.va/news/2015/06/23/us_buddhists,_catholics_begin_new_interreligious_dialogue_/1153525|title=Buddhists, Catholics begin new dialogue on 'suffering, liberation, fraternity'|publisher=}}&lt;/ref&gt; Pope Francis received a Buddhist blessing while at the meeting.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.romereports.com/2015/06/24/pope-francis-meets-with-buddhist-leaders-oethese-small-gestures-are-seeds-of-peace|title=Pope Francis meets with Buddhist leaders: "these small gestures are seeds of peace"|publisher=|deadurl=yes|archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20161101111227/http://www.romereports.com/2015/06/24/pope-francis-meets-with-buddhist-leaders-oethese-small-gestures-are-seeds-of-peace|archivedate=1 November 2016|df=dmy-all}}&lt;/ref&gt;

===Attitudes about non-believers===
Speaking to journalists and media employees on 16 March 2013, Pope Francis said he would bless everyone silently, "given that many of you do not belong to the Catholic Church, and others are not believers."&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|last=Donadio|first=Rachel |title=With Blessing, Pope Shows an Openness to Other Faiths|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2013/03/17/world/europe/with-blessing-pope-shows-an-openness-to-other-faiths.html|accessdate=17 April 2013|publisher=New York Times|date=16 March 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt;
In his papal address on 20 March, he said the "attempt to eliminate God and the Divine from the horizon of humanity" resulted in violence, but described as well his feelings about nonbelievers: "[W]e also sense our closeness to all those men and women who, although not identifying themselves as followers of any religious tradition, are nonetheless searching for truth, goodness and beauty, the truth, goodness and beauty of God. They are our valued allies in the commitment to defending human dignity, in building a peaceful coexistence between peoples and in safeguarding and caring for creation."&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|title=Address of the Holy Father Pope Francis|url=http://www.vatican.va/holy_father/francesco/speeches/2013/march/documents/papa-francesco_20130320_delegati-fraterni_en.html|accessdate=15 April 2013|publisher=Holy See|date=20 March 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|last=Speciale|first=Alessandro|title=Pope Francis says atheists can be 'allies' for the church|url=https://articles.washingtonpost.com/2013-03-20/national/37864118_1_atheists-and-believers-spiritual-leader-muslim-leaders|accessdate=15 April 2013|publisher=Washington Post|date=20 March 2013|deadurl=yes|archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20130621220805/http://articles.washingtonpost.com/2013-03-20/national/37864118_1_atheists-and-believers-spiritual-leader-muslim-leaders|archivedate=21 June 2013|df=dmy-all}}&lt;/ref&gt;

Some atheists hoped Francis would prove to be progressive on issues like poverty and social inequality,&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|last=Duke|first=Barry|title=Pope Francis extends a hand of friendship to atheists, even though we're disastrous for the world|url=http://freethinker.co.uk/2013/03/26/pope-francis-extends-a-hand-of-friendship-to-atheists-even-though-were-disastrous-for-the-world/|accessdate=15 April 2013|publisher=The Freethinker|date=26 March 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt; while others were more skeptical that he would be "interested in a partnership of equals".&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|last=Wilde|first=Sara Lin|title=Pope Francis Reaches Out To the 'Nones': Can We Be The Pope's Allies?|url=http://www.patheos.com/blogs/friendlyatheist/2013/03/22/pope-francis-reaches-out-to-the-nones-can-we-be-the-popes-allies/|accessdate=15 April 2013|publisher=Patheos|date=22 March 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt; In May 2013, Francis said all who do good can be [[Redemption (theology)#Christianity|redeemed]] through Jesus, including atheists. Francis said God "has redeemed all of us, all of us, with the Blood of Christ: all of us, not just Catholics. Everyone! Even the atheists. Everyone!"&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news |url= https://www.washingtonpost.com/national/on-faith/pope-francis-god-redeemed-everyone-not-just-catholics/2013/05/22/f90da324-c311-11e2-9642-a56177f1cdf7_story.html|title= Pope Francis: God redeemed everyone, 'not just Catholics'|first= David|last= Gibson|date= 22 May 2013|publisher= ''The Washington Post''|accessdate=26 May 2015}}&lt;/ref&gt; Amid the ensuant controversy, [[Carl E. Olson]] said Francis's words were fundamental Christian teaching dating back to the Apostle Paul&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web |url=http://www.catholicworldreport.com/Blog/2276/pope_francis_teaches_that_everyone_is_saved_wow_hold_on_wait_a_second.aspx |title=Pope Francis teaches that everyone is saved! Wow! (Hold on. Wait a second.) |last1=Olson |first1=Carl E. |date=23 May 2013 |website=[[Catholic World Report]] |access-date=25 January 2016 |quote=If he indeed 'rocked' the minds of some Catholics, it only suggests that they aren't paying attention to Scripture and Church teaching.}}&lt;/ref&gt; and Fr. Dwight Longenecker wrote, "Unfortunately for those who wish to paint Pope Francis as a lovable liberal, in fact, the Pope is simply affirming certain truths that any somewhat knowledgable Catholic will uphold."&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web |url=http://www.patheos.com/blogs/standingonmyhead/2013/05/did-pope-francis-preach-salvation-by-works.html |title=Did Pope Francis Preach Salvation by Works?? |last1=Longenecker |first1=Dwight |date=23 May 2013  |publisher=Patheos |access-date=25 January 2016 |quote=[Francis] explains that it does no good to exclude and scapegoat atheists or other non believers. Instead they too should be expected to do good and that is where we encounter them and the dialogue begins. This is too much for some, and the Pope is being accused of [[Pelagianism]] and [[Universalism]]. (Salvation by works and 'Everyone will be saved.')}}&lt;/ref&gt; A spokesman for the Vatican, Father [[Thomas Rosica]], issued an "explanatory note" that non-Catholics who "know" the Catholic Church but do not convert "cannot be saved", and only those who "sincerely seek Godcan attain eternal salvation".&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.washingtontimes.com/news/2013/may/30/not-so-fast-vatican-contradicts-comment-pope-franc/ |title=Not so fast: Vatican says Pope Francis got it wrong, atheists do go to hell|publisher=The Washington Times|author= Cheryl K. Chumley|date=30 May 2013 |accessdate=23 June 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt; [[Hendrik Hertzberg]] criticised Rosica in ''[[The New Yorker]]'' magazine, and speculated that there may be major internal disagreement between supporters and opponents of [[Vatican II]] in the Catholic Church.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|last=Hertzberg |first=Hendrik |url=http://www.newyorker.com/online/blogs/comment/2013/06/the-truth-about-pope-francis-and-atheists.html |title=The Truth about Pope Francis and Atheists |publisher=''The New Yorker'' |date= |accessdate=23 June 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt;

In September 2013, Francis wrote a letter to Italian journalist Eugenio Scalfari, saying non-believers would be forgiven by God if they followed their [[conscience]]s. Responding to a list of questions published in his newspaper by Scalfari, who is not a Catholic, Francis wrote: "you ask if the God of Christians forgives those who do not believe and who do not seek faith. Given the premise, and this is fundamental, that the mercy of God is limitless for those who turn to him with a sincere and contrite heart, the issue for the unbeliever lies in obeying his or her conscience."&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web |author=Pope Francis |title=Letter to a non-believer |url=http://webcache.googleusercontent.com/search?q=cache:w2.vatican.va/content/francesco/en/letters/2013/documents/papa-francesco_20130911_eugenio-scalfari.html+%22you+ask+if+the+God+of+Christians+forgives+those+who+do+not+believe+and+who+do+not+seek+faith.+Given+the+premise,+and+this+is+fundamental,+that+the+mercy+of+God+is+limitless+for+those+who+turn+to+him+with+a+sincere+and+contrite+heart,+the+issue++for+the+unbeliever+lies+in+obeying+his+or+her+conscience%22 |publisher=Holy See |date=4 September 2013 |accessdate=4 July 2017}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|author=Pope Francis |url=http://www.repubblica.it/cultura/2013/09/11/news/the_pope_s_letter-66336961/ |title=Pope Francisco writes to La Repubblica: "An open dialogue with non-believers" |newspaper=la Repubblica |date=11 September 2013 |accessdate=4 July 2017}}&lt;/ref&gt;

==International diplomatic role==
[[File:President Barack Obama with Pope Francis at the Vatican, March 27, 2014.jpg|thumb|Pope Francis with [[President of the United States|U.S. President]] [[Barack Obama]], 27 March 2014]]
[[File:Vladimir Putin with Franciscus (2015-06-10) 1.jpg|thumb|Pope Francis shaking hands with Russian [[Foreign Minister]] [[Sergey Lavrov]], behind [[President of Russia|Russian President]] [[Vladimir Putin]], 10 June 2015]]
Pope Francis played a key role in the talks toward restoring [[Cuban Thaw|full diplomatic relations between the U.S. and Cuba]]. The restoration was jointly announced by U.S. President [[Barack Obama]] and Cuban President [[Ral Castro]] on Wednesday, 17 December 2014. The headline in the ''Los Angeles Times'' on 19 December 2014 was "Bridge to Cuba via Vatican," with the further lead "In a rare and crucial role, Pope Francis helped keep U.S. talks with Havana on track and guided final deal."&lt;ref&gt;Paul Richter and Tom Kington, "Bridge to Cuba Via Vatican", ''Los Angeles Times'' 19 December 2014, p. A1.&lt;/ref&gt; The pope, along with the [[Government of Canada]], was a behind the scenes broker of the agreement, taking the role following [[Barack Obama|President Obama's]] request during his visit to the pope in March 2014.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news |first= Barbie Latza |last= Nadeau |url= http://www.thedailybeast.com/articles/2014/12/17/the-pope-s-diplomatic-miracle-ending-the-u-s-cuba-cold-war.html |title= The Pope's Diplomatic Miracle: Ending the U.S.Cuba Cold War |work= The Daily Beast |date= December 17, 2014 |access-date=December 18, 2014}}&lt;/ref&gt; The success of the negotiations was credited to Francis because "as a religious leader with the confidence of both sides, he was able to convince the Obama and Castro administrations that the other side would live up to the deal".&lt;ref&gt;Richter and Kington, ''LA Times'', 17 December 2014, p. A6.&lt;/ref&gt; En route to the United States for a visit in September 2015, the pope stopped in Cuba. "The plan comes amid a breakthrough for which Francis has received much credit."&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|url = http://www.latimes.com/world/mexico-americas/la-fg-pope-cuba-20150422-story.html|title = Pope Francis to stop in Cuba en route to U.S., Vatican announces|last = Wilkinson|first = Tracy|date = 22 April 2015|access-date = 29 July 2015|archive-url = https://web.archive.org/web/20150730034810/http://www.latimes.com/world/mexico-americas/la-fg-pope-cuba-20150422-story.html|archive-date=30 July 2015 |dead-url = no|publication-place = Mexico City, Mexico|newspaper = [[Los Angeles Times]]}}&lt;/ref&gt; The Cuba visit "seals that accomplishment, in which he served as a bridge between two erstwhile enemies".&lt;ref name="Wilkinson, Pope will visit Cuba."&gt;Wilkinson, "Pope will visit Cuba."&lt;/ref&gt; According to one expert on religion in Latin America, Mario Paredes, the pope's visit to Cuba is consistent with his aim to promote an understanding of the role of the Cuban Revolution and that of the Catholic Church. When Francis was archbishop of Buenos Aires he authored a text entitled "Dialogues Between John Paul II and Fidel Castro."&lt;ref name="Wilkinson, Pope will visit Cuba."/&gt; John Paul was the first pope to visit Cuba. In May 2015, the pope met with Cuban leader Ral Castro. After the meeting in [[Vatican City]] on 10 May 2015, Castro said that he is considering returning to the [[Catholic Church]].&lt;ref name="Catholic Cuba"&gt;{{cite news |url= http://edition.cnn.com/2015/05/10/europe/italy-raul-castro-pope-francis-meeting/|title= Raul Castro may join Catholic Church, he says after Pope Francis meeting|author= Eliott C. McLaughlin|date= 14 May 2015|publisher= CNN|accessdate=3 June 2015}}&lt;/ref&gt; He said in a televised news conference, "I read all the speeches of the pope, his commentaries, and if the pope continues this way, I will go back to praying and go back to the [Catholic] church. I am not joking."&lt;ref name=NYT11MAY2015A4&gt;Jim Yardley, "Praising Pope, Cuban President Says He might return to church." ''New York Times'' 11 May 2015, A4&lt;/ref&gt; Castro said that when the pope comes, "I promise to go to all his Masses and with satisfaction".&lt;ref name=NYT11MAY2015A4/&gt;

In December 2014, Pope Francis declined to meet with the [[14th Dalai Lama]], the 1989 [[Nobel Peace Prize]] laureate. According to a ''New York Times'' report, a Vatican spokesman said "Pope Francis obviously holds the Dalai Lama in very high regard, but he will not be meeting any of the Nobel [Peace] laureates."&lt;ref&gt;Alan Cowell, "Pope Declines to Meet with Dalai Lama", ''New York Times'' 13 December 2014, p. A8&lt;/ref&gt; The last meeting between the Dalai Lama and a pope was with [[Benedict XVI]] in 2006.&lt;ref&gt;"Pope Declines to Meet with Dalai Lama", ''New York Times'' 13 December 2014, p. A8.&lt;/ref&gt; In November 2015, Pope Francis met with that year's [[Tunisian National Dialogue Quartet|Nobel Peace Prize laureates from Tunisia]].&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news | accessdate = 7 November 2015 | publisher = Vatican Radio | title= Pope Francis meets with 2015 Nobel Peace Prize winners from Tunisia | url= http://en.radiovaticana.va/news/2015/11/07/pope_francis_meets_with_2015_nobel_peace_prize_winners_/1185125 | date = 7 November 2015}}&lt;/ref&gt;

In May 2014, his visit to the [[state of Israel]], where he delivered 13 speeches, was heavily publicized.&lt;ref&gt;[http://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-27469349 "Pope Francis to tread careful path on Mid-East visit"], David Willey. BBC. 23 May 2014. Retrieved 11 February 2017&lt;/ref&gt; [[Protests Against Pope Francis Visit to Israel 2014|protests against his visit]] resulted in an alleged arson attempt at the [[Dormition Abbey]].&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news | accessdate = 11 December 2016 | title=Holy Land: Vandal tries to set fire to Dormition Abbey | url = http://www.catholicnewsagency.com/news/holy-land-vandal-tries-to-set-fire-to-dormition-abbey/ | publisher = Catholic News Agency }}&lt;/ref&gt; The cave under the [[Church of the Nativity]] caught fire the night after his visit.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news | accessdate = 11 December 2016 | publisher = Novus Ordo Watch | title = Fire breaks out at Nativity Church shortly after Francis visits Bethlehem | date =  2014}}&lt;/ref&gt;

In May 2015, Pope Francis welcomed Palestinian president [[Mahmoud Abbas]] to the Vatican. Several media outlets reported that Francis praised Abbas as "an angel of peace", though his actual words were the following: "The angel of peace destroys the evil spirit of war. I thought about you: may you be an angel of peace."&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news |url=http://www.ncregister.com/blog/edward-pentin/the-pope-mahmoud-abbas-and-the-angel-of-peace |title=The Pope, Mahmoud Abbas, and the 'Angel of Peace' |first=Edward |last=Pentin |date=18 May 2015 |accessdate=18 May 2015}}&lt;/ref&gt; The Vatican signed a treaty recognizing the [[state of Palestine]].&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web |url= http://www.timesofisrael.com/vatican-signs-treaty-recognizing-state-of-palestine/|title= Vatican signs treaty recognizing State of Palestine|date= 26 June 2015|publisher= The Times of Israel|accessdate=2 August 2015}}&lt;/ref&gt; The Vatican issued statements concerning the hope that the peace talks could resume between Israel and Palestine. Abbas's visit was on the occasion of the canonization of two Palestinian nuns.&lt;ref&gt;Elisabetta Povoledo, "At Vatican, Abbas is Praised as 'Angel of Peace'". ''New York Times'' Sunday, 17 May 2015, A11.&lt;/ref&gt;

On 6 June 2015, Pope Francis visited [[Sarajevo]], the capital city of [[Bosnia and Herzegovina]]. He urged peace during his time in the religiously diverse city, known as the "Jerusalem of Europe".&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news | url=http://edition.cnn.com/2015/06/06/europe/bosnia-pope-francis-visit/index.html | title=Pope Francis urges peace on visit to Sarajevo, 'Jerusalem of Europe' | publisher=CNN | date=6 June 2015 | accessdate=6 June 2015 |author1=Robertson, Nic |author2=Smith-Spark, Laura |author3=Karimi, Faith }}&lt;/ref&gt;

On 25 September 2015, Pope Francis addressed the United Nations in New York City.&lt;ref name="Times 2015"&gt;{{cite web | last=Times | first=The New York | title=Pope Francis Addresses the U.N.: Live Updates | website=The New York Times | date=25 September 2015 | url=https://www.nytimes.com/live/pope-visit-2015/ | accessdate=25 September 2015}}&lt;/ref&gt;

On 16 April 2016, he visited, together with the [[Bartholomew I of Constantinople|Ecumenical Patriarch Bartholomew]] and the [[Ieronymos II of Athens|Archbishop Ieronimos II of Athens]], the Mria camp in the [[Greece|Greek]] island of [[Lesbos]], to call the attention of the world to the refugee issue. There the three Christian leaders signed a joint declaration.&lt;ref&gt;[https://www.theguardian.com/world/gallery/2016/apr/16/pope-francis-europe-visits-lesbos-in-pictures Pope Francis visits Lesbos]. The Guardian. Published: 16 April 2016&lt;/ref&gt;

Pope Francis has said he will visit Ireland in 2018, in what will be the first papal tour of the country since John Paul II's historic trip in 1979.&lt;ref&gt;{{Cite news|url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2016/nov/28/pope-francis-to-visit-ireland-in-2018|title=Pope Francis to visit Ireland in 2018|last=correspondent|first=Henry McDonald Ireland|date=28 November 2016|newspaper=The Guardian|language=en-GB|issn=0261-3077|access-date=28 November 2016}}&lt;/ref&gt;

[[File:PresidentTrumpFirstLadyMelaniaTrumpPopeFrancisVaticanOfficialWhiteHousePhoto24May2017.jpg|left|thumb|[[President of the United States|U.S. President]] [[Donald Trump]] and [[First Lady of the United States|First Lady]] [[Melania Trump|Melania]] with Pope Francis, 24 May 2017, [[Vatican City]]]]In January 2017, Pope Francis demanded the resignation of [[Matthew Festing]], the 79th [[List of Princes and Grand Masters of the Sovereign Military Order of Malta|Prince and Grand Master]] of the [[Sovereign Military Order of Malta]]. The Pope's demand came as a response to Festing and Cardinal [[Raymond Leo Burke]]'s firing of [[Boeselager|Baron Albrecht von Boeselager]] from his position in the Order of Malta. The Order is currently under Vatican control until another Prince is appointed.&lt;ref&gt;{{Cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2017/01/28/world/europe/ten-centuries-later-a-pope-and-knights-do-battle.html|title=Ten Centuries Later, a Pope and Knights Do Battle|last=Horowitz|first=Jason|date=28 January 2017|newspaper=The New York Times|issn=0362-4331|access-date=30 January 2017}}&lt;/ref&gt;
On 24 May 2017, Pope Francis met with [[President of the United States|U.S. President]] [[Donald Trump]] in [[Vatican City]] where they discussed the contributions of [[Catholic Church in the United States|Catholics]] to the United States and to the world. Trump and the Pope discussed issues of mutual concern including how religious communities can combat human suffering in crisis regions, such as [[Syria]], [[Libya]], and [[ISIS]]-controlled territory. Trump and Pope Francis also discussed [[terrorism]] and the radicalization of young people. The [[Cardinal Secretary of State|Vatican's secretary of state]], [[Pietro Parolin]], raised the issue of [[climate change]] in the meeting and encouraged Trump to remain in the [[Paris Agreement]].&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news |last= |first= |date=24 May 2017 |title=Trump: Meeting Pope Francis 'the honor of a lifetime' |url=http://www.foxnews.com/politics/2017/05/24/trump-meeting-pope-francis-honor-lifetime.html |work=FOX News |location=New York |access-date=26 May 2017}}&lt;/ref&gt;

==Public image==
{{See also|List of places and things named after Pope Francis}}
{{external media | width = 210px | float = right | headerimage = [[File:Pope Francis (27056871831) (cropped).jpg|210px]] 
 | video1 = [https://www.ted.com/talks/pope_francis_why_the_only_future_worth_building_includes_everyone?language=en#t-62701 Why the only future worth building includes everyone], [[TED (conference)|TED talks]], April 2017, 17:51, in Italian with subtitles in 22 languages | accessdate =27 April 2017 }}

Popular [[mainstream media]] frequently portray Pope Francis either as a [[Progressivism|progressive]] papal reformer or with [[Social liberalism|liberal]], moderate values.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|url=http://www.independent.ie/opinion/does-pope-francis-have-a-cunning-plan-30444898.html|title=Does Pope Francis have a cunning plan?|work=Irish Independent|first=John|last=Waters|date=20 July 2014|accessdate=18 August 2014}}&lt;/ref&gt; The Vatican has claimed that Western news outlets often seek to portray his message with a less-doctrinal tone of papacy, in hopes of extrapolating his words to convey a more merciful and tolerant message.&lt;ref name="Achanging"&gt;{{cite web|first=Mark|last=Binelli |url=https://www.rollingstone.com/culture/news/pope-francis-the-times-they-are-a-changin-20140128 |title=Pope Francis Cover Story: The Times They Are A-Changin' |work=Rolling Stone |date=28 January 2014 |accessdate=24 May 2014}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web |url=http://www.catholicnewsagency.com/news/vatican-spokesman-media-manipulated-popes-comments-on-families/|title=Vatican spokesman: media manipulated Pope's family comments |date=7 January 2014|publisher=Catholic News Agency|accessdate=3 June 2015}}&lt;/ref&gt; In the news media, both faithful and non-believers often refer to a "honeymoon" phase in which the Pope has changed the tone on Catholic doctrines and supposedly initiated [[ecclesiastical]] reform in the Vatican.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web |url=http://www.slate.com/articles/news_and_politics/frame_game/2013/09/pope_francis_interview_forget_homosexuality_and_birth_control_he_s_a_flaming.html |title=Pope Francis Is a Liberal |last=Saletan |first=William |author-link=William Saletan|date=19 September 2013 |website=[[Slate (magazine)|Slate]] |publisher=The Slate Group |accessdate=20 May 2014}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|first=Luke|last=Coppen |url=http://www.spectator.co.uk/features/9112081/the-fantasy-francis/ |title=Sorry  but Pope Francis is no liberal |work=The Spectator |date=11 January 2014 |accessdate=24 May 2014}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|last=O'Loughlin |first=Michael |url=http://www.advocate.com/politics/religion/2014/01/28/catholics-urge-pope-francis-speak-out-lgbt-rights |title=Catholics Urge Pope Francis to Speak Out for LGBT Rights |work=Advocate |date=28 January 2014 |accessdate=24 May 2014}}&lt;/ref&gt; Media systems differ, too, not only in their coverage of Francis's stances but also in how individual events are portrayed. His 2015 trip to Cuba is a prime example. During this trip, American-based AP and British-based Reuters highlighted the religious aspect of the pope's journey while Prensa Latina, the official state media agency, depicted it as a diplomatic visit. American and British media were also more likely during this trip to show Francis interacting with regular Cubans compared to the official Cuban media, which showed Francis interacting with elites most often.&lt;ref&gt;{{Cite journal|last=Thomson|first=T. J.|last2=Perreault|first2=Gregory|last3=Duffy|first3=Margaret|date=17 January 2017|title=Politicians, Photographers, and a Pope|url=https://dx.doi.org/10.1080/1461670X.2016.1268929|journal=Journalism Studies|volume=0|pages=118|doi=10.1080/1461670X.2016.1268929|issn=1461-670X}}&lt;/ref&gt;

In December 2013, both ''[[Time Magazine|Time]]'' and ''[[The Advocate]]'' magazines named the Pontiff as their "Person of the Year" in praise and hopes of reforming the [[Roman Curia]] while hoping to change the Catholic Church's doctrine on various controversial issues. In addition, ''Esquire'' magazine named him as the "Best-dressed man" for 2013 for his simpler vestments often in tune with a modern simplistic design on sartorial fashion.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|url=http://www.smh.com.au/world/pope-francis-named-esquires-best-dressed-man-of-2013--but-why-20140101-hv7ab.html |title=Pope Francis named Esquire's 'Best Dressed Man of 2013'  but why?|first=Michael|last=McGough|date=1 January 2014|work=The Sydney Morning Herald|accessdate=3 June 2015}}&lt;/ref&gt; ''[[Rolling Stone]]'' magazine followed in January 2014 by making the Pontiff their featured front cover.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|url=http://www.dailymail.co.uk/news/article-2530742/A-heavenly-sense-style-Pope-Francis-named-Esquires-Best-Dressed-Man-2013.html |location=London |work=Daily Mail |title=A divine sense of style: Pope Francis is named Esquire's Best Dressed Man of 2013 |first=Sam |last=Webb |date=29 December 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|url=http://poy.time.com/2013/12/11/person-of-the-year-pope-francis-the-peoples-pope |work=Time |title=Person of the Year 2013 |date=11 December 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt; ''[[Fortune (magazine)|Fortune]]'' magazine also ranked Pope Francis as number one in their list of 50 greatest leaders.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news |url=http://money.cnn.com/gallery/leadership/2014/03/20/worlds-best-leaders.fortune/ |publisher=CNN |first=Geoff |last=Colvin |title=Fortune ranks the World's 50 Greatest Leaders |date=20 March 2014 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20140331010527/http://money.cnn.com/gallery/leadership/2014/03/20/worlds-best-leaders.fortune |archivedate=31 March 2014 |df=dmy-all }}&lt;/ref&gt; On 5 November 2014, he was ranked by ''[[Forbes]]'' as the fourth [[Forbes list of The World's Most Powerful People|most powerful person in the world]] and was the only non-political figure in the top ranking.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news |url=https://www.forbes.com/sites/forbespr/2014/11/05/2014-ranking-of-the-worlds-most-powerful-people/|title=2014 Ranking Of The World's Most Powerful People|date=11 May 2014|work=Forbes|accessdate=3 June 2015|first=Corporate|last=Communications}}&lt;/ref&gt; In December 2016, Francis yet made ''Forbes''{{'}}s list of "The World's Most Powerful People", ranking fifth.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|last1=M. Ewalt|first1=David|title=The World's Most Powerful People 2016|url=https://www.forbes.com/sites/davidewalt/2016/12/14/the-worlds-most-powerful-people-2016/#26ec03f2368d|accessdate=3 March 2017|work=[[Forbes]]}}&lt;/ref&gt;

In March 2013, a new song was dedicated to Francis and released in Brazilian Portuguese, European Portuguese, and Italian, titled ''Come Puoi'' ("How You Can").&lt;ref name="nofrills"/&gt; Also in March, Pablo Buera, the mayor of [[La Plata]], Argentina, announced that the city had renamed a section of a street leading up to a local cathedral ''Papa Francisco''.&lt;ref name="street"&gt;Ho, Erica, [http://newsfeed.time.com/2013/03/28/argentinatown-renames-street-after-pope-francis/ "Argentina: Town renames street after Pope Francis"], ''Time'', 28 March 2013, Retrieved 28 March 2013&lt;/ref&gt; There are already efforts to name other streets after him, as well as a school where he studied as a child.&lt;ref name="street"/&gt; A proposal to create a commemorative coin as a tribute to Pope Francis was made in Argentina's lower house on 28 November 2013. On the coins it would read, "Tribute from the Argentine People to Pope Francis." beneath his face.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|url=http://edition.cnn.com/2013/11/27/world/americas/argentina-pope-francis-coin/index.html |title=Argentina weighs putting Pope Francis' face on a coin |publisher=CNN |author=Catherine E. Shoichet|date=28 November 2013|accessdate=27 December 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt; As of May 2013, sales of papal souvenirs, a sign of popularity, were up.&lt;ref name=NYT52513&gt;{{cite news|title=Francis' Humility and Emphasis on the Poor Strike a New Tone at the Vatican|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2013/05/26/world/europe/pope-francis-changes-tone-at-the-vatican.html|accessdate=26 May 2013|work=The New York Times|date=25 May 2013|first=Rachel|last=Donadio|quote=It was so hard to sell anything under Benedict. This pope attracts huge crowds, and they all want to bring back home something with his smiling face on it.}}&lt;/ref&gt;

Pope Francis presided over his first joint public wedding ceremony in a Nuptial Mass for 20 couples from the Archdiocese of Rome on 14 September 2014, just a few weeks before the start of 519 October Extraordinary [[Synod of Bishops (Catholic)|Synod of Bishops]] on the Family.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news | accessdate = 7 November 2015 | publisher = BBC News| date= 14 September 2014 | title= Pope marries 20 cohabiting couples in sign of papacy shift
| url = http://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-29198491}}&lt;/ref&gt;{{efn|[[Pope Emeritus Benedict XVI]] did not do this during his eight-year reign from 20052013; his predecessor, [[Pope John Paul II]], married a group of couples from all over the world in 2000, as part of the Jubilee for Families, and before that in 1994 during the Church's Year of the Family, as well as presiding over a number of private marriages as Pope.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web |last=Glatz |first=Carol |url=http://www.catholicnews.com/services/englishnews/2014/pope-francis-to-preside-over-joint-september-wedding-at-vatican.cfm |title=Pope Francis to preside over joint September wedding at Vatican |date=29 August 2014 |publisher=Catholic News Service |accessdate=23 May 2018}}&lt;/ref&gt;}}

To date, there are two biographical films about Pope Francis: ''[[Call Me Francesco]]'' (Italy, 2015), starring [[Rodrigo de la Serna]], and ''[[Francis: Pray for me]]'' (Argentina, 2015), starring [[Daro Grandinetti]].&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news |url=https://variety.com/2015/film/global/battle-of-the-pope-francis-biopics-begins-with-two-films-shooting-in-buenos-aires-1201403994/|title=Battle of the Pope Francis Biopics Begins With Two Films Shooting In Buenos Aires|first=Nick|last=Vivarelli|date=13 January 2015|work=Variety|accessdate=15 May 2015}}&lt;/ref&gt;

On 19 March 2016, Pope Francis became the first Pope to create an [[Instagram]] account. He broke records after having gained over one million followers in under twelve hours of the account being up.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://money.cnn.com/2016/03/19/technology/instagram-pope-francis-account/|title=Pope Francis gains 1 million Instagram followers in under 12 hours|author=Ahiza Garcia|date=19 March 2016|work=CNNMoney|accessdate=20 May 2016}}&lt;/ref&gt;

On 8 January 2017 at a ceremony commemorating the [[Baptism of Jesus]] at the [[Sistine Chapel]] in which twenty-eight infants were to be baptized, Pope Francis reiterated support for mothers to [[Breastfeeding in public|breastfeed their children in public]], even in sacred places.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=https://www.npr.org/sections/thetwo-way/2017/01/09/508927895/pope-francis-reiterates-support-for-public-breastfeeding|title=Pope Francis Reiterates Support For Public Breastfeeding|author=Rebecca Hersher|date=9 January 2017|work=[[National Public Radio]]|accessdate=9 January 2017}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/news/morning-mix/wp/2017/01/09/go-ahead-and-breastfeed-pope-francis-tells-mothers-in-sistine-chapel/|title=Go Ahead And Breastfeed Pope Francis Tells Mothers In Sistine Chapel|author=Samantha Schmidt|date=9 January 2017|work=[[The Washington Post]]|accessdate=9 January 2017}}&lt;/ref&gt;

In July 2017 Pope Francis reiterated the position of the Church that bread to be used in the [[eucharist]] for the [[transsubstantiation]] into the Body of Christ should not be [[gluten]]free.&lt;ref name="glutenvrij"&gt;[http://en.radiovaticana.va/news/2017/07/08/letter_to_bishops_on_the_bread_and_wine_for_the_eucharist/1323886 Letter to the bishops on the bread and wine for the eucharist], [[Radio Vaticana]], 7 July 2017.&lt;/ref&gt;

== Distinctions ==

===Titles and styles===
{{Infobox Pope styles
| image      = Insigne_Francisci.svg
| dipstyle=[[His Holiness]]
| offstyle=Your Holiness
| relstyle=Holy Father
| deathstyle=}}
The official [[Style (manner of address)|style]] of the Pope in English is ''His Holiness Pope Francis''; in Latin, ''Franciscus, Episcopus Romae''. ''Holy Father'' is another honorific often used for popes.

His full title, rarely used, is:
:''[[His Holiness]] Francis, [[Bishop of Rome]], [[Vicar of Christ|Vicar of Jesus Christ]], Successor of the [[Saint Peter|Prince of the Apostles]], [[Pontifex Maximus|Supreme]] [[Pontiff#Christianity|Pontiff]] of the Universal Church, [[Primate (bishop)|Primate]] of Italy, [[Metropolitan bishop|Archbishop and Metropolitan]] of the [[List of the Roman Catholic dioceses in Italy#Ecclesiastical Province of Rome|Roman]] [[Ecclesiastical province#Catholic Church|Province]], [[List of Sovereigns of the Vatican City State|Sovereign]] of the [[Vatican City]] State, [[Servant of the servants of God]].''

The best-known title, that of "Pope", does not appear in the official list of titles, but is commonly used in the titles of documents, and appears, in abbreviated form, in their signatures as "PP." standing for ''Papa'' (''Pope'').&lt;ref&gt;{{cathEncy|author=Shahan, Thomas Joseph|wstitle=Ecclesiastical Abbreviations|volume=1}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite encyclopedia |year= 2013|title =Pope |encyclopedia=[[Encyclopdia Britannica]] |publisher= Encyclopdia Britannica Online|accessdate=14 April 2013|url=http://www.britannica.com/EBchecked/topic/469994/pope}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://inkunabeln.ub.uni-koeln.de/vdibDevelop/handapparat/nachs_w/cappelli/cappelli.html |first=Adriano|last=Cappelli |title= Lexicon Abbreviaturarum |page=283 |date= |accessdate=18 February 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.ndl.go.jp/incunabula/e/glossary/glo_11.html |title=Contractions and Abbreviations |publisher=Ndl.go.jp |date=4 August 2005 |accessdate=21 November 2011}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://acronyms.thefreedictionary.com/Papa+Pontifex |title=What Does PP Stand For? |publisher=Acronyms.thefreedictionary.com |date= |accessdate=21 November 2011}}&lt;/ref&gt;

It is customary when referring to popes to translate the [[regnal name]] into local languages. Thus he is ''Papa Franciscus'' in Latin (the official language of the Holy See), ''Papa Francesco'' in Italian (the language of the Vatican), ''Papa Francisco'' in his native Spanish, and ''Pope Francis'' in English.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url= http://blogs.canoe.ca/parker/news/a-few-things-you-might-not-know-about-pope-francis/|title= A Few Things You Might Not Know About Pope Francis|first= Alan|last= Parker|date= 15 March 2013|work= |publisher= Toronto Sun|accessdate= 11 April 2014|deadurl= yes|archiveurl= https://archive.is/20140411184409/http://blogs.canoe.ca/parker/news/a-few-things-you-might-not-know-about-pope-francis/|archivedate= 11 April 2014|df= dmy-all}}&lt;/ref&gt;
{{Clear}}&lt;!---putting in break to prevent box breaking into next major section---&gt;

===National orders===
As [[Pope]], representative of the [[Holy See]] and [[head of state]] of [[Vatican City]], Francis is [[Grand Master (order)|Grand Master]] of the following orders:
* {{flag|Holy See}}: [[Supreme Order of Christ]]
* {{flag|Holy See}}: [[Order of the Golden Spur]]
* {{flag|Holy See}}: [[Order of Pius IX]]
* {{flag|Holy See}}: [[Order of St. Gregory the Great]]
* {{flag|Holy See}}: [[Order of St. Sylvester]]

===Foreign orders===
